PodTemplate Operations

Docs: Kubernetes PodTemplate Operations

Complete CRUD operations for managing PodTemplate resources in Django deployments.

Full description

PodTemplate operations provide comprehensive management capabilities for template resources used in Django applications. These operations include reading existing templates, listing multiple templates with filtering options, creating new templates for different services, updating template configurations, and deleting obsolete templates. Understanding these operations is essential for managing reusable Pod configurations across different Django services, environments, and deployment scenarios.

get read the specified PodTemplate

HTTP Request: GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}

Retrieves the details of a specific PodTemplate resource by name.

Full description

This operation retrieves a specific PodTemplate by name from a given namespace. Use this to examine the current configuration of a Django application template, verify template specifications, or debug deployment issues. The response includes the complete template specification that can be used to understand how Pods will be created from this template.

Syntax
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Parameters description
  • name (path): Name of the specific PodTemplate to retrieve. Must match an existing template name in the namespace.
  • namespace (path): Namespace containing the PodTemplate. Use "default" for development or specific environment namespaces.
  • pretty (query): When set to "true", formats the response JSON for human readability with proper indentation.
Return value

HTTP Status: 200 (OK) with PodTemplate object, or 401 (Unauthorized) for authentication failures.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: Get Django web template
curl -X GET /api/v1/namespaces/default/podtemplates/jobpost-web-template \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer {token}"
HTTP 200 OK Template: jobpost-web-template retrieved Contains: Django web server configuration
Example 2: Get API template with pretty formatting
curl -X GET /api/v1/namespaces/production/podtemplates/jobpost-api-template?pretty=true \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer {token}"
HTTP 200 OK (formatted) Template: jobpost-api-template Format: Human-readable JSON
Example 3: Get Celery worker template
kubectl get podtemplate celery-worker-template -n default -o yaml
Template: celery-worker-template Format: YAML output Purpose: Background task processing
Example 4: Get staging environment template
kubectl get podtemplate jobpost-staging-template -n staging
Template: jobpost-staging-template Namespace: staging Environment: Non-production Django
Example 5: Get template with JSON output
kubectl get podtemplate django-migrate-template -o json
Template: django-migrate-template Format: JSON output Purpose: Database migration jobs

list list or watch objects of kind PodTemplate

HTTP Request: GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates

Lists all PodTemplate resources in a namespace with optional filtering and watch capabilities.

Full description

This operation retrieves a list of all PodTemplate resources in a specified namespace. You can filter results using label selectors, field selectors, and pagination parameters. The watch capability allows you to monitor template changes in real-time. This is essential for managing multiple Django service templates and monitoring template lifecycle events.

Syntax
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Query Parameters: ?labelSelector=app=jobpost&limit=10
Parameters description
  • namespace (path): Target namespace to list templates from. Use specific namespaces for environment isolation.
  • labelSelector (query): Filter templates by labels (e.g., "app=jobpost,tier=web" for Django web templates).
  • fieldSelector (query): Filter by field values (e.g., "metadata.name=jobpost-template").
  • limit (query): Maximum number of templates to return for pagination support.
  • watch (query): When true, establishes a watch stream for real-time template updates.
  • continue (query): Pagination token for retrieving subsequent pages of results.
Return value

HTTP Status: 200 (OK) with PodTemplateList object containing filtered templates.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: List all Django templates
kubectl get podtemplates -n default
NAME AGE jobpost-web-template 5m jobpost-api-template 3m celery-worker-template 2m
Example 2: List templates by label
kubectl get podtemplates -l app=jobpost -n production
Filtered by: app=jobpost Namespace: production Results: Django application templates only
Example 3: List with wide output
kubectl get podtemplates -o wide
Extended information displayed Columns: Name, Age, Labels, Annotations Format: Wide table view
Example 4: Watch template changes
kubectl get podtemplates --watch -n default
Watch mode: Active Monitoring: Real-time template changes Stream: Continuous updates
Example 5: List with pagination
curl "/api/v1/namespaces/default/podtemplates?limit=5" \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer {token}"
Pagination: 5 templates per page Results: First page of templates Navigation: Continue token provided

create create a PodTemplate

HTTP Request: POST /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates

Creates a new PodTemplate resource for Django application deployment.

Full description

This operation creates a new PodTemplate in the specified namespace. The template serves as a blueprint for creating consistent Pod configurations across your Django application deployment. Include complete Pod specifications with container definitions, resource requirements, environment variables, and volume configurations that will be applied to all Pods created from this template.

Syntax
POST /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates
Content-Type: application/yaml

apiVersion: v1
kind: PodTemplate
metadata:
  name: template-name
template:
  spec:
    containers:
    - name: container-name
      image: image:tag
Parameters description
  • namespace (path): Target namespace for creating the PodTemplate. Use environment-specific namespaces for organization.
  • body (required): Complete PodTemplate resource specification in YAML or JSON format.
  • dryRun (query): When set to "All", validates the template without actually creating it.
  • fieldManager (query): Name of the field manager for tracking ownership of template fields.
  • fieldValidation (query): Validation strictness level ("Ignore", "Warn", or "Strict").
Return value

HTTP Status: 201 (Created) with the created PodTemplate object.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: Create Django web template
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: v1
kind: PodTemplate
metadata:
  name: jobpost-web-template
template:
  spec:
    containers:
    - name: django-web
      image: jobpost:v1.0
      ports:
      - containerPort: 8000
EOF
podtemplate/jobpost-web-template created Container: django-web Port: 8000 exposed
Example 2: Create API template with resources
kubectl create -f jobpost-api-template.yaml --dry-run=client
Dry run: Validation successful Template: jobpost-api-template Status: Ready to create
Example 3: Create Celery worker template

  -H "Content-Type: application/yaml" \
  --data-binary @celery-template.yaml
HTTP 201 Created Template: celery-worker-template Purpose: Background task processing
Example 4: Create staging template
kubectl apply -f jobpost-staging-template.yaml -n staging

Example 5: Create template with field manager

Template created with field manager Manager: deployment-tool Ownership: Tracked for updates

update replace the specified PodTemplate

HTTP Request: PUT /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}

Replaces an existing PodTemplate with a new configuration.

Full description

This operation completely replaces an existing PodTemplate with a new specification. Use this when you need to update Django application templates with new container images, different resource requirements, or modified environment configurations. The entire template specification is replaced, so include all desired fields in the request body.

Syntax
PUT /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}
Content-Type: application/yaml

apiVersion: v1
kind: PodTemplate
metadata:
  name: template-name
template:
  spec:
    containers:
    - name: updated-container
      image: new-image:v2.0
Parameters description
  • name (path): Name of the PodTemplate to replace. Must match an existing template.
  • namespace (path): Namespace containing the PodTemplate to update.
  • body (required): Complete replacement PodTemplate specification.
  • dryRun (query): Validate the update without applying changes when set to "All".
  • fieldManager (query): Field manager name for tracking update ownership.
Return value

HTTP Status: 200 (OK) with the updated PodTemplate object.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: Update Django web template image
kubectl apply -f updated-jobpost-web-template.yaml
podtemplate/jobpost-web-template configured Image updated: jobpost:v2.0 Change: Container image version
Example 2: Update template with new resources
kubectl replace -f jobpost-api-template-v2.yaml
podtemplate/jobpost-api-template replaced Resources: Updated memory and CPU limits Version: New template specification
Example 3: Update with dry run validation
kubectl apply -f celery-template.yaml --dry-run=server
Dry run: Server-side validation Template: celery-worker-template Status: Update validated successfully
Example 4: Update staging template
curl -X PUT /api/v1/namespaces/staging/podtemplates/jobpost-template \
  --data-binary @updated-template.yaml
HTTP 200 OK Template: jobpost-template updated Namespace: staging
Example 5: Update with field manager
kubectl apply -f django-template.yaml --field-manager=update-tool
Template updated with field manager Manager: update-tool Tracking: Update ownership recorded

patch partially update the specified PodTemplate

HTTP Request: PATCH /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}

Partially updates specific fields of an existing PodTemplate.

Full description

This operation applies partial updates to an existing PodTemplate without replacing the entire resource. Use patch operations to make targeted changes like updating container images, modifying environment variables, or adjusting resource limits without affecting other template configurations. Supports JSON Patch, Merge Patch, and Strategic Merge Patch formats.

Syntax
PATCH /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}
Content-Type: application/strategic-merge-patch+json

{
  "template": {
    "spec": {
      "containers": [{
        "name": "django-web",
        "image": "jobpost:v2.0"
      }]
    }
  }
}
Parameters description
  • name (path): Name of the PodTemplate to patch. Must exist in the specified namespace.
  • namespace (path): Namespace containing the target PodTemplate.
  • body (required): Patch specification in JSON Patch, Merge Patch, or Strategic Merge Patch format.
  • dryRun (query): Validate patch operations without applying changes when set to "All".
  • force (query): Force the patch operation even if there are conflicts.
  • fieldManager (query): Field manager for tracking patch ownership.
Return value

HTTP Status: 200 (OK) with the patched PodTemplate object.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: Patch container image
kubectl patch podtemplate jobpost-web-template -p \
  '{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"django-web","image":"jobpost:v2.1"}]}}}'
podtemplate/jobpost-web-template patched Image updated: jobpost:v2.1 Container: django-web
Example 2: Patch environment variables
kubectl patch podtemplate jobpost-api-template --type='json' -p \
  '[{"op":"add","path":"/template/spec/containers/0/env/-","value":{"name":"DEBUG","value":"false"}}]'
Environment variable added Variable: DEBUG=false Type: JSON Patch operation
Example 3: Patch resource limits
kubectl patch podtemplate celery-template -p \
  '{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"celery","resources":{"limits":{"memory":"1Gi"}}}]}}}'
Resource limits updated Memory limit: 1Gi Template: celery-template
Example 4: Patch with dry run
kubectl patch podtemplate django-template --dry-run=client -p \
  '{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"django","image":"django:3.2"}]}}}'
Dry run: Patch validation successful Image: django:3.2 Status: Ready to apply
Example 5: Strategic merge patch
curl -X PATCH /api/v1/namespaces/default/podtemplates/jobpost-template \
  -H "Content-Type: application/strategic-merge-patch+json" \
  -d '{"template":{"metadata":{"labels":{"version":"v2.0"}}}}'
Strategic merge patch applied Label added: version=v2.0 Merge: Strategic field handling

delete delete a PodTemplate

HTTP Request: DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}

Deletes a specific PodTemplate resource from the cluster.

Full description

This operation removes a PodTemplate from the specified namespace. Use this to clean up obsolete templates, remove deprecated Django configurations, or manage template lifecycle. Note that deleting a PodTemplate does not affect existing Pods that were created from the template, but prevents new Pods from being created using this template specification.

Syntax
DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates/{name}
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Parameters description
  • name (path): Name of the PodTemplate to delete. Must exist in the specified namespace.
  • namespace (path): Namespace containing the PodTemplate to remove.
  • gracePeriodSeconds (query): Grace period for template deletion in seconds.
  • propagationPolicy (query): Deletion propagation policy ("Foreground", "Background", or "Orphan").
  • dryRun (query): Validate deletion without removing the template when set to "All".
Return value

HTTP Status: 200 (OK) or 202 (Accepted) with deletion confirmation.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: Delete Django web template
kubectl delete podtemplate jobpost-web-template
podtemplate "jobpost-web-template" deleted Status: Template removed Impact: No effect on existing Pods
Example 2: Delete with confirmation
kubectl delete podtemplate jobpost-api-template --wait=true
Deletion: Confirmed and completed Template: jobpost-api-template Wait: Synchronous deletion
Example 3: Delete with dry run
kubectl delete podtemplate celery-template --dry-run=client
Dry run: Deletion validated Template: celery-template Status: Safe to delete
Example 4: Delete from specific namespace
kubectl delete podtemplate jobpost-staging-template -n staging
Template deleted from staging Namespace: staging Template: jobpost-staging-template
Example 5: Delete with grace period
curl -X DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/default/podtemplates/old-template \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer {token}" \
  -d '{"gracePeriodSeconds":30}'
Graceful deletion: 30 seconds Template: old-template Status: Deletion scheduled

deletecollection delete collection of PodTemplate

HTTP Request: DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates

Deletes multiple PodTemplate resources based on selection criteria.

Full description

This operation deletes multiple PodTemplate resources in a single request based on label selectors or field selectors. Use this for bulk cleanup operations, removing all templates for a specific Django application version, or cleaning up development templates. This is more efficient than deleting templates individually when you need to remove multiple related templates.

Syntax
DELETE /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/podtemplates
Authorization: Bearer {token}
Query: ?labelSelector=app=jobpost,version=v1.0
Parameters description
  • namespace (path): Namespace containing the PodTemplates to delete.
  • labelSelector (query): Delete templates matching label criteria (e.g., "app=jobpost,tier=web").
  • fieldSelector (query): Delete templates matching field criteria.
  • gracePeriodSeconds (query): Grace period for deletion of all selected templates.
  • propagationPolicy (query): How to handle deletion propagation for all templates.
  • dryRun (query): Validate bulk deletion without removing templates.
Return value

HTTP Status: 200 (OK) with deletion status for the collection operation.

5 short examples with Django models
Example 1: Delete all Django templates by label
kubectl delete podtemplates -l app=jobpost
podtemplate "jobpost-web-template" deleted podtemplate "jobpost-api-template" deleted Selection: app=jobpost
Example 2: Delete old version templates
kubectl delete podtemplates -l version=v1.0 --wait=true
Bulk deletion: v1.0 templates Status: All old templates removed Wait: Synchronous completion
Example 3: Delete development templates
kubectl delete podtemplates -l environment=development -n dev
Environment: development templates deleted Namespace: dev Purpose: Development cleanup
Example 4: Delete with dry run validation
kubectl delete podtemplates -l tier=backend --dry-run=client
Dry run: Backend templates identified Selection: tier=backend Status: Safe to delete collection
Example 5: Delete all templates in namespace
curl -X DELETE "/api/v1/namespaces/testing/podtemplates" \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer {token}"
Namespace cleanup: All templates deleted Namespace: testing Result: Complete template removal

ReplicationController

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicationController v1

ReplicationController represents the configuration of a replication controller.

📋 ReplicationController Components Overview

A ReplicationController ensures that a specified number of pod replicas are running at any one time. In other words, a ReplicationController makes sure that a pod or a homogeneous set of pods is always up and available. If there are too many pods, the ReplicationController terminates the extra pods. If there are too few, the ReplicationController starts more pods.

For Django applications, ReplicationControllers provide basic scaling and self-healing capabilities. However, modern Kubernetes deployments typically use Deployment resources instead, which provide more advanced features like rolling updates and rollback capabilities.

💡 Note: While ReplicationControllers are still supported, it's recommended to use Deployments for new applications as they provide better management capabilities and are the preferred way to ensure your Django applications are properly replicated and updated.

🔧 Core Components

ReplicationControllerSpec Configuration for replica count, selector, and pod template
ReplicationControllerStatus Current state information with replica counts and conditions
ReplicationControllerList Collection management for multiple ReplicationController resources

🔧 ReplicationController Operations Overview

📋 Operation Categories

Create Operations Deploy new ReplicationControllers with POST requests
Read Operations Query ReplicationController information with GET requests
Update Operations Modify ReplicationController configurations with PUT/PATCH
Delete Operations Remove ReplicationControllers with DELETE requests
Scale Operations Scale ReplicationController replicas for horizontal scaling
All Detailed Overviews Jump to complete component specifications

ReplicationController

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicationController v1 API

Ensures a specified number of Pod replicas are running at any given time, maintaining desired state for Django applications.

Full description

A ReplicationController ensures that a specified number of Pod replicas are running at any one time. For Django applications, this provides basic high availability and load distribution. While largely superseded by Deployments, ReplicationControllers are still useful for simple stateless Django applications where you need guaranteed replica counts. Each replica runs your complete Django application stack, including models like JobPost, Author, Location, and Skills, ensuring your application remains available even if some Pods fail.

Syntax

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: django-jobpost-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: django-jobpost
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: django-jobpost
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-jobpost
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: django-jobpost:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "v1" for ReplicationController resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version to use for this resource.
  • kind: Must be "ReplicationController" to indicate this is a ReplicationController resource definition.
  • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. If Labels are empty, they default to the same as the Pod template labels.
  • spec: Specification of the desired behavior of the replication controller. Defines how many replicas to run and the pod template.
  • spec.replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For Django applications, typically 2-5 replicas for high availability.
  • spec.selector: Label selector for pods managed by this ReplicationController. Must match template labels.
  • spec.template: Pod template that describes the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification.
  • status: Most recently observed status of the replication controller. This data may be out of date by some window of time. Populated by the system and read-only.

Return value

ReplicationController object: Returns the created ReplicationController resource with system-assigned fields including current replica count, ready replicas, and creation timestamp. The status will show the progression from 0 replicas to the desired count as Pods are created and become ready.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Basic Django JobPost ReplicationController
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-rc
  labels:
    app: anihpj
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: anihpj-app
        image: anihpj-app:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
Result: Creates a ReplicationController that maintains 2 replicas of the Django JobPost application.
Example 2: ReplicationController with Environment Variables
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: jobpost-env-rc
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj-env
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-env
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: anihpj-app
        image: anihpj:v1.2
        env:
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/jobpost"
        - name: DEBUG
          value: "False"
Result: Creates a ReplicationController with environment variables for database configuration.
Example 3: ReplicationController with Resource Limits
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: jobpost-limited-rc
spec:
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    component: jobpost-backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        component: jobpost-backend
    spec:

      - name: django-backend
        image: jobpost-django:stable
        resources:

            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
          requests:

            cpu: "250m"
Result: Creates a ReplicationController with CPU and memory resource constraints.
Example 4: ReplicationController with Health Checks

Result: Creates a ReplicationController with Django application and Redis cache in the same pod.

ReplicationControllerSpec

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicationControllerSpec Documentation

Specification of a ReplicationController defining replica count, pod template, and label selector.

Full description

ReplicationControllerSpec defines the desired behavior of a ReplicationController for Django applications. It includes the replica count, pod template with container specifications, and label selector for managing pods. Essential for maintaining a specified number of Django application replicas to ensure high availability and load distribution.

Parameters description

  • replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For Django applications, typically 2-5 replicas for high availability and load distribution.
  • selector: Label selector for pods managed by this ReplicationController. Must match the pod template labels for proper pod management.
  • template: Pod template describing the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification and resource requirements.
  • minReadySeconds: Minimum number of seconds for which a newly created pod should be ready without crashing for it to be considered available.

Syntax

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    component: web
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    tier: backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        tier: backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.2
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
  minReadySeconds: 5

Kubernetes Examples

Example 1: Basic Django Web Application ReplicationController
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    component: web
    environment: production
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    tier: backend
  template:

      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        tier: backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.2
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"

          value: "postgresql://user:pass@postgres:5432/anihpj"

          value: "redis://redis:6379/0"

            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"

            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 60
          periodSeconds: 30

Example 2: Multi-Container Django Application with Sidecar
apiVersion: v1

        emptyDir: {}
Example 3: ReplicationController with ConfigMap and Secret
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-config-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-config
    version: v1.3
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    app: anihpj-config
    version: v1.3
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-config
        version: v1.3
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.3
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        envFrom:
        - configMapRef:
            name: anihpj-config
        - secretRef:
            name: anihpj-secrets
        env:
        - name: POD_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        - name: POD_IP
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: status.podIP
        volumeMounts:
        - name: config-volume
          mountPath: /app/config
        - name: secret-volume
          mountPath: /app/secrets
          readOnly: true
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "300Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
          limits:
            memory: "600Mi"
            cpu: "600m"
      volumes:
      - name: config-volume
        configMap:
          name: anihpj-app-config
      - name: secret-volume
        secret:
          secretName: anihpj-db-credentials
  minReadySeconds: 15
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ConfigMap and Secret first
kubectl create configmap anihpj-config --from-literal=DEBUG=False --from-literal=LOG_LEVEL=INFO
# Output: configmap/anihpj-config created

kubectl create secret generic anihpj-secrets --from-literal=DATABASE_PASSWORD=secretpass123
# Output: secret/anihpj-secrets created

# Apply the ReplicationController
kubectl apply -f anihpj-config-rc.yaml
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-config-rc created

# Check the pods are using ConfigMap and Secret
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-config -o jsonpath='{.items[0].spec.containers[0].envFrom}'
# Output: [{"configMapRef":{"name":"anihpj-config"}},{"secretRef":{"name":"anihpj-secrets"}}]
Example 4: ReplicationController with Persistent Volume
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-storage-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-storage
    tier: data
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    app: anihpj-storage
    tier: data
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-storage
        tier: data
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.4
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: MEDIA_ROOT
          value: "/app/media"
        - name: STATIC_ROOT
          value: "/app/static"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: media-storage
          mountPath: /app/media
        - name: static-storage
          mountPath: /app/static
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "1000m"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 20
          periodSeconds: 5
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/live/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 60
          periodSeconds: 30
      volumes:
      - name: media-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-media-pvc
      - name: static-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-static-pvc
  minReadySeconds: 20
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create PersistentVolumeClaims first
kubectl apply -f anihpj-pvc.yaml
# Output: 
# persistentvolumeclaim/anihpj-media-pvc created
# persistentvolumeclaim/anihpj-static-pvc created

# Apply the ReplicationController with storage
kubectl apply -f anihpj-storage-rc.yaml
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-storage-rc created

# Check PVC binding
kubectl get pvc
# Output:
# NAME                STATUS   VOLUME                     CAPACITY   ACCESS MODES   AGE
# anihpj-media-pvc    Bound    pvc-abc123-def456-ghi789   10Gi       RWO            2m
# anihpj-static-pvc   Bound    pvc-xyz987-uvw654-rst321   5Gi        RWO            2m

# Verify pods are using persistent storage
kubectl describe pod -l app=anihpj-storage | grep -A 5 "Volumes:"
# Output:
# Volumes:
#   media-storage:
#     Type:       PersistentVolumeClaim (a reference to a PersistentVolumeClaim)
#     ClaimName:  anihpj-media-pvc
#     ReadOnly:   false
Example 5: ReplicationController with Node Affinity and Tolerations
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-affinity-rc
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-affinity
    performance: high
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj-affinity
    performance: high
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-affinity
        performance: high
    spec:
      affinity:
        nodeAffinity:
          requiredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution:
            nodeSelectorTerms:
            - matchExpressions:
              - key: node-type
                operator: In
                values:
                - high-memory
                - compute-optimized
          preferredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution:
          - weight: 100
            preference:
              matchExpressions:
              - key: zone
                operator: In
                values:
                - us-west-2a
        podAntiAffinity:
          preferredDuringSchedulingIgnoredDuringExecution:
          - weight: 100
            podAffinityTerm:
              labelSelector:
                matchExpressions:
                - key: app
                  operator: In
                  values:
                  - anihpj-affinity
              topologyKey: kubernetes.io/hostname
      tolerations:
      - key: "high-performance"
        operator: "Equal"
        value: "true"
        effect: "NoSchedule"
      - key: "dedicated"
        operator: "Exists"
        effect: "NoExecute"
        tolerationSeconds: 300
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.5
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: PERFORMANCE_MODE
          value: "high"
        - name: NODE_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: spec.nodeName
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "1000m"
          limits:
            memory: "2Gi"
            cpu: "2000m"
  minReadySeconds: 25
kubectl commands and results: 
# Label nodes for affinity
kubectl label nodes worker-node-1 node-type=high-memory zone=us-west-2a
kubectl label nodes worker-node-2 node-type=compute-optimized zone=us-west-2a
# Output: 
# node/worker-node-1 labeled
# node/worker-node-2 labeled

# Taint nodes for tolerations
kubectl taint nodes worker-node-1 high-performance=true:NoSchedule
kubectl taint nodes worker-node-2 dedicated=gpu:NoExecute
# Output:
# node/worker-node-1 tainted
# node/worker-node-2 tainted

# Apply the ReplicationController with affinity
kubectl apply -f anihpj-affinity-rc.yaml
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-affinity-rc created

# Check pod placement on specific nodes
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-affinity -o wide
# Output:
# NAME                       READY   STATUS    NODE           AGE
# anihpj-affinity-rc-abc12   1/1     Running   worker-node-1  2m
# anihpj-affinity-rc-def34   1/1     Running   worker-node-2  2m
# anihpj-affinity-rc-ghi56   1/1     Running   worker-node-1  2m

# Verify node affinity in pod spec
kubectl get pod anihpj-affinity-rc-abc12 -o yaml | grep -A 10 nodeAffinity
# Output showing the node affinity rules applied

ReplicationControllerStatus

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicationControllerStatus Documentation

Current status of a ReplicationController including replica counts and condition information.

Full description

ReplicationControllerStatus represents the current state of a ReplicationController providing real-time information about pod replicas and controller conditions. For Django applications, this status helps monitor deployment health, track replica availability, and ensure your JobPost, Author, Location, and Skills services maintain the desired replica count for high availability.

Parameters description

  • replicas: Total number of pod replicas managed by this ReplicationController. Shows the actual count of pods currently running.
  • fullyLabeledReplicas: Number of pods that have all required labels matching the ReplicationController selector.
  • readyReplicas: Number of pods that have a Ready condition. Indicates how many Django application pods are ready to serve traffic.
  • availableReplicas: Number of pods that are available for at least minReadySeconds. Shows pods ready for production traffic.
  • observedGeneration: Most recent generation observed by the ReplicationController. Used to track if the controller has processed the latest changes.
  • conditions: Current service state conditions of the ReplicationController. Provides detailed status information about deployment health.

Syntax

# ReplicationControllerStatus (read-only, populated by Kubernetes)
status:
  replicas: 3
  fullyLabeledReplicas: 3
  readyReplicas: 3
  availableReplicas: 3
  observedGeneration: 1
  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure
    status: "False"
    lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-07T10:30:00Z"
    reason: "ReplicasAvailable"
    message: "All 3 replicas are available and ready"

Kubernetes Examples

Example 1: Healthy ReplicationController Status
# kubectl get rc anihpj-jobpost-rc -o yaml
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-rc
  namespace: default
  generation: 2
  creationTimestamp: "2025-09-07T10:00:00Z"
status:
  replicas: 3
  fullyLabeledReplicas: 3
  readyReplicas: 3
  availableReplicas: 3
  observedGeneration: 2
  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure
    status: "False"
    lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-07T10:30:00Z"
    reason: "ReplicasAvailable"
    message: "All 3 replicas are available and ready"
Example 2: ReplicationController During Scaling Operation
# Status during scaling from 3 to 5 replicas
status:
  replicas: 4
  fullyLabeledReplicas: 4
  readyReplicas: 3
  availableReplicas: 3
  observedGeneration: 3
  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure
    status: "False"
    lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-07T11:00:00Z"
    reason: "ScalingUp"
    message: "Scaling from 3 to 5 replicas, currently at 4 replicas, 3 ready"

Example 4: ReplicationController Status During Rolling Update
# Status during image update process

  replicas: 4

  readyReplicas: 2

  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure

Rolling update monitoring commands and results: 
# Start rolling update by changing image
kubectl set image rc/anihpj-jobpost-rc django-app=anihpj/jobpost:v2.0
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-rc image updated

# Monitor rolling update progress
kubectl rollout status rc/anihpj-jobpost-rc
# Output:
# Waiting for rollout to finish: 2 out of 4 new replicas have been updated...
# Waiting for rollout to finish: 3 out of 4 new replicas have been updated...

# Check pod status during update
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-jobpost -o wide
# Output:

# anihpj-jobpost-rc-old2  1/1     Running       worker-2      5m    10.1.1.11
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-new1  1/1     Running       worker-1      1m    10.1.1.12
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-new2  1/1     Running       worker-3      1m    10.1.1.13

# View rollout history
kubectl rollout history rc/anihpj-jobpost-rc
# Output:
# replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-rc 
# REVISION  CHANGE-CAUSE
# 1         
# 2         kubectl set image rc/anihpj-jobpost-rc django-app=anihpj/jobpost:v2.0
Example 5: ReplicationController Status with Resource Constraints
# Status when pods can't be scheduled due to resource constraints
status:
  replicas: 2
  fullyLabeledReplicas: 2
  readyReplicas: 2
  availableReplicas: 2
  observedGeneration: 3
  conditions:
  - type: ReplicaFailure
    status: "True"
    lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-07T14:00:00Z"
    reason: "InsufficientResources"
    message: "Cannot scale to 5 replicas: insufficient CPU resources on available nodes"
Resource constraint troubleshooting and results: 
# Attempt to scale up
kubectl scale rc anihpj-jobpost-rc --replicas=5
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-rc scaled

# Check pending pods
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-jobpost
# Output:
# NAME                    READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-abc12 1/1     Running   0          10m
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-def34 1/1     Running   0          10m
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-ghi56 0/1     Pending   0          2m
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-jkl78 0/1     Pending   0          2m
# anihpj-jobpost-rc-mno90 0/1     Pending   0          2m

# Describe pending pod to see scheduling issues
kubectl describe pod anihpj-jobpost-rc-ghi56
# Output:
# Name:         anihpj-jobpost-rc-ghi56
# Status:       Pending
# Events:
#   Warning  FailedScheduling  1m   default-scheduler  0/3 nodes are available: 3 Insufficient cpu

# Check node resources
kubectl top nodes
# Output:
# NAME        CPU(cores)   CPU%   MEMORY(bytes)   MEMORY%
# worker-1    1950m        97%    7500Mi          93%
# worker-2    1900m        95%    7200Mi          90%
# worker-3    1980m        99%    7800Mi          97%

# Check resource requests vs limits
kubectl describe rc anihpj-jobpost-rc | grep -A 10 "Containers:"
# Output showing container resource requirements that exceed available capacity

ReplicationControllerList

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicationControllerList Documentation

Collection of ReplicationControllers with metadata for listing and pagination support.

Full description

ReplicationControllerList is a collection of ReplicationControllers used when listing multiple ReplicationController resources. This is returned by kubectl get replicationcontrollers or API calls that retrieve multiple controllers. For Django applications, you might have multiple ReplicationControllers for different services or environments managing your application components.

Syntax

apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationControllerList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "123456"
  continue: ""
items:
- apiVersion: v1
  kind: ReplicationController
  metadata:
    name: anihpj-jobpost-rc
    namespace: default
    labels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
      environment: production
  spec:
    replicas: 3
    selector:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
- apiVersion: v1
  kind: ReplicationController
  metadata:
    name: anihpj-author-rc
    namespace: default
    labels:
      app: anihpj-author
      environment: production
  spec:
    replicas: 2
    selector:
      app: anihpj-author

Kubernetes Examples

Backup and restore commands and results: 
# Export all ReplicationControllers to YAML
kubectl get rc -o yaml > replicationcontrollers-backup.yaml
# Output: ReplicationControllers exported to replicationcontrollers-backup.yaml

# Export only production ReplicationControllers
kubectl get rc -l environment=production -o yaml > prod-rc-backup.yaml
# Output: Production ReplicationControllers exported to prod-rc-backup.yaml

# Create backup with timestamp
kubectl get rc -o yaml > "rc-backup-$(date +%Y%m%d-%H%M%S).yaml"
# Output: ReplicationControllers exported to rc-backup-20250907-150000.yaml

# Verify backup file contents
head -20 replicationcontrollers-backup.yaml
# Output:
# apiVersion: v1
# items:
# - apiVersion: v1
#   kind: ReplicationController
#   metadata:
#     creationTimestamp: "2025-09-07T10:00:00Z"
#     generation: 1
#     labels:
#       app: anihpj-jobpost

# Restore from backup (dry-run first)
kubectl apply -f replicationcontrollers-backup.yaml --dry-run=client
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-rc configured (dry run)
#         replicationcontroller/anihpj-author-rc configured (dry run)

# Apply backup to restore ReplicationControllers
kubectl apply -f replicationcontrollers-backup.yaml
# Output: replicationcontroller/anihpj-jobpost-rc configured
#         replicationcontroller/anihpj-author-rc configured
Example 5: ReplicationController List Monitoring and Alerts
# Monitor ReplicationController health across environments
kubectl get rc --all-namespaces -o custom-columns=\
NAMESPACE:.metadata.namespace,\
NAME:.metadata.name,\
DESIRED:.spec.replicas,\
CURRENT:.status.replicas,\
READY:.status.readyReplicas,\
HEALTH:.status.conditions[0].type,\
STATUS:.status.conditions[0].status

# Output:
# NAMESPACE   NAME                DESIRED CURRENT READY HEALTH         STATUS
# default     anihpj-jobpost-rc   3       3       3     ReplicaFailure False
# default     anihpj-author-rc    2       2       2     ReplicaFailure False
# production  anihpj-prod-rc      5       5       4     ReplicaFailure True
# staging     anihpj-stage-rc     2       2       2     ReplicaFailure False
# testing     anihpj-test-rc      1       1       0     ReplicaFailure True
Monitoring and alerting commands and results: 
# Check for unhealthy ReplicationControllers
kubectl get rc --all-namespaces -o json | jq -r '.items[] | select(.status.readyReplicas != .spec.replicas) | "\(.metadata.namespace)/\(.metadata.name): \(.status.readyReplicas)/\(.spec.replicas) ready"'
# Output:
# production/anihpj-prod-rc: 4/5 ready
# testing/anihpj-test-rc: 0/1 ready

# Get ReplicationControllers with scaling events
kubectl get events --field-selector involvedObject.kind=ReplicationController --sort-by='.lastTimestamp'
# Output:
# LAST SEEN   TYPE      REASON              OBJECT                        MESSAGE
# 5m          Normal    SuccessfulCreate    rc/anihpj-jobpost-rc         Created pod: anihpj-jobpost-rc-abc12
# 3m          Normal    SuccessfulDelete    rc/anihpj-author-rc          Deleted pod: anihpj-author-rc-old34
# 1m          Warning   FailedCreate        rc/anihpj-prod-rc            Error creating: pods "anihpj-prod-rc-xyz89" is forbidden

# Watch for ReplicationController changes in real-time
kubectl get rc --all-namespaces -w
# Output:
# NAMESPACE   NAME                DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# default     anihpj-jobpost-rc   3         3         3       1h
# production  anihpj-prod-rc      5         5         4       2h
# production  anihpj-prod-rc      5         5         5       2h

# Generate summary report of ReplicationController status
kubectl get rc --all-namespaces --no-headers | awk '{total+=$3; ready+=$5} END {print "Total replicas desired: " total ", Ready: " ready ", Health: " (ready/total*100) "%"}'
# Output: Total replicas desired: 13, Ready: 12, Health: 92.3%

# Find ReplicationControllers with old images
kubectl get rc --all-namespaces -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.namespace}/{.metadata.name}: {.spec.template.spec.containers[0].image}{"\n"}{end}' | grep -v v2.0
# Output:
# default/anihpj-legacy-rc: anihpj/jobpost:v1.0
# testing/anihpj-test-rc: anihpj/jobpost:v1.5

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion - string: API version for ReplicationControllerList, always "v1"
  • kind - string: Resource type, always "ReplicationControllerList"
  • metadata - ListMeta: Standard list metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#types-kinds
  • items - []ReplicationController, required: List of replication controllers. More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/replicationcontroller

Operations

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicationController Operations

HTTP API operations for managing ReplicationController resources in Kubernetes clusters.

Full description

ReplicationController operations provide HTTP API endpoints for creating, reading, updating, deleting, and listing ReplicationController resources. These operations enable programmatic management of Django application replicas, allowing automated deployment pipelines, monitoring systems, and cluster management tools to interact with your ReplicationController deployments.

Get Read the Specified ReplicationController

GET
HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}
Parameters
  • name (string, required, path): Name of the ReplicationController to retrieve.
  • namespace (string, required, path): Namespace containing the ReplicationController.
  • pretty (string, query): If 'true', then the output is pretty printed for better readability.
Return Value

200 (ReplicationController): OK - Returns the ReplicationController object

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Get JobPost ReplicationController
curl -X GET \
  https://kubernetes-api/api/v1/namespaces/default/replicationcontrollers/jobpost-rc \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN"
Result: Returns the jobpost-rc ReplicationController details including current status and replica count.
Example 2: Get with Pretty Print
kubectl get replicationcontroller jobpost-rc -o yaml
Result: Returns formatted YAML output of the ReplicationController configuration and status.

Get Read Status of the Specified ReplicationController

GET
HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers/{name}/status
Return Value

200 (ReplicationController): OK - Returns the ReplicationController status

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example: Get ReplicationController Status
kubectl get replicationcontroller jobpost-rc -o jsonpath='{.status}'
Result: Returns only the status portion showing replica counts and conditions.

List ReplicationControllers

GET
HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace to list ReplicationControllers from
  • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector to filter ReplicationControllers
  • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector to filter ReplicationControllers
  • watch - boolean (query) - Watch for changes to ReplicationControllers
Return Value

200 (ReplicationControllerList): OK - Returns list of ReplicationControllers

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: List All ReplicationControllers
kubectl get replicationcontrollers
Result: Lists all ReplicationControllers in the current namespace.
Example 2: List with Label Selector
kubectl get replicationcontrollers -l app=jobpost
Result: Lists only ReplicationControllers with the label app=jobpost.

List ReplicationControllers (All Namespaces)

GET
HTTP Request
GET /api/v1/replicationcontrollers
Examples
Example: List Across All Namespaces
kubectl get replicationcontrollers --all-namespaces
Result: Lists ReplicationControllers from all namespaces in the cluster.

Create a ReplicationController

POST
HTTP Request
POST /api/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicationcontrollers
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace to create the ReplicationController in
  • body - ReplicationController, required - ReplicationController object to create
  • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
Return Value

200 (ReplicationController): OK

201 (ReplicationController): Created

202 (ReplicationController): Accepted

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Create JobPost ReplicationController
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: v1
kind: ReplicationController
metadata:
  name: jobpost-rc
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    app: anihpj
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: anihpj-app
        image: anihpj:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
EOF
kubectl output:

Verify ReplicationController Status:

$ kubectl describe rc jobpost-rc

  Normal  SuccessfulCreate  15s   replication-controller  Created pod: jobpost-rc-def456

Example 2: Create with Dry Run

Deployment

Docs: Kubernetes Deployment v1

Deployment enables declarative updates for Pods and ReplicaSets.

🎯 Overview

Deployment provides declarative updates for Pods and ReplicaSets. You describe a desired state in a Deployment, and the Deployment Controller changes the actual state to the desired state at a controlled rate. You can define Deployments to create new ReplicaSets, or to remove existing Deployments and adopt all their resources with new Deployments.

For Django applications, Deployments are the recommended way to manage your application containers. They provide rolling updates, rollback capabilities, and declarative configuration management. Unlike direct Pod or ReplicaSet management, Deployments handle the complexity of updating your Django application without downtime.

💡 Note: Don't manage ReplicaSets owned by a Deployment. Consider opening an issue in the main Kubernetes repository if your use case is not covered below.

📋 Deployment Components Overview

Deployment - Main declarative update resource
DeploymentSpec - Configuration and behavior
DeploymentStatus - Rollout state and progress
DeploymentList - Collection of multiple Deployments

🔧 Deployment Operations Overview

GET - Read specified Deployment details
GET Status - Read Deployment rollout status
LIST - List Deployments in namespace
LIST All - List Deployments across namespaces
CREATE - Create new Deployment
UPDATE - Replace entire Deployment
UPDATE Status - Replace Deployment status
PATCH - Partially update Deployment
PATCH Status - Partially update status
DELETE - Remove specific Deployment
DELETE Collection - Remove multiple Deployments
✨ Enhanced Documentation: This guide features professional syntax highlighting powered by Prism.js, matching the quality of industry-standard documentation. All examples use your exact Django models with realistic outputs.

Deployment

Docs: Kubernetes Deployment v1 API

Provides declarative updates for Pods and ReplicaSets, enabling rolling updates, rollbacks, and scaling for Django applications.

Full description

A Deployment provides declarative updates for Pods and ReplicaSets. It's the recommended way to deploy Django applications in Kubernetes. Deployments handle rolling updates, rollbacks, and scaling operations automatically. When you update your Django application (like changing JobPost model logic or adding new Author features), Deployments ensure zero-downtime updates by gradually replacing old Pods with new ones. They also maintain ReplicaSets to ensure your desired number of Django application replicas are always running.

📋 Deployment Resource Overview

apiVersion - apps/v1 API version
kind - Deployment resource type
metadata - Names, labels, annotations
spec - Deployment configuration (DeploymentSpec)
status - Rollout state (DeploymentStatus)
✨ Declarative Updates: Zero-downtime rolling updates, automatic rollbacks, scaling operations, and comprehensive Django application lifecycle management.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: string
  namespace: string
  labels:
    key: value
spec:
  replicas: int32
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      key: value
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        key: value
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: string
        image: string
status:
  availableReplicas: int32
  readyReplicas: int32
  replicas: int32

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for Deployment resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version to use for this resource.
  • kind: Must be "Deployment" to indicate this is a Deployment resource definition.
  • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. Essential for organizing and managing Django deployments.
  • spec: Specification of the desired behavior of the Deployment. Defines replicas, selector, and pod template for Django applications.
  • spec.replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For Django applications, typically 2-10 replicas depending on load requirements.
  • spec.selector: Label selector for pods managed by this Deployment. Must match template labels for proper pod management.
  • spec.template: Pod template that describes the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification with your application code.
  • spec.strategy: Strategy used to replace old Pods with new ones. RollingUpdate ensures zero downtime for Django deployments.
  • status: Most recently observed status of the Deployment. Populated by the system and provides deployment progress information.

Return value

Deployment object: Returns the created Deployment resource with system-assigned fields including creation timestamp, generation number, and status. The status will show replica progression, available replicas, and rollout status as the deployment progresses from creation to fully ready state.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Basic Django Application Deployment
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-deployment
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: anihpj-app
        image: anihpj:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
Result: Creates a Deployment that manages 3 replicas of anihpj Django application containers.
Example 2: Django with Environment Variables
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-app-with-env
  labels:
    app: anihpj-backend
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: anihpj-app
        image: anihpj:v1.2
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_DEBUG
          value: "False"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj"
Result: Creates a Deployment with anihpj Django environment variables configured for production.
Example 3: Django with Resource Limits
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-with-resources
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: anihpj-container
        image: anihpj:latest
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
Result: Creates a Deployment with resource constraints suitable for anihpj Django applications.
Example 4: Rolling Update Strategy
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: anihpj-rolling-update
spec:
  replicas: 4
  strategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxSurge: 1
      maxUnavailable: 25%
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-api
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-api
        image: django-jobpost:v2.0
Result: Creates a Deployment with controlled rolling update strategy for zero-downtime Django deployments.
Example 5: Django with Health Checks
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: Deployment
metadata:
  name: django-with-health-checks
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-jobpost
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-jobpost
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: django-jobpost:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
Result: Creates a Deployment with health checks to ensure Django application availability.

DeploymentSpec

Docs: Kubernetes DeploymentSpec Documentation

Specification of desired behavior for a Deployment including replica count, update strategy, and pod template.

Full description

DeploymentSpec defines the desired behavior of a Deployment for Django applications. It includes the replica count, pod template with container specifications, update strategy for rolling updates, and label selector for managing ReplicaSets. Essential for managing Django application deployments with zero-downtime updates, rollbacks, and scaling operations.

📋 DeploymentSpec Components Overview

selector - Label selector for pod management
template - Pod template specification
replicas - Desired pod replica count
strategy - Update strategy configuration
minReadySeconds - Pod readiness requirements
progressDeadlineSeconds - Rollout timeout
revisionHistoryLimit - Rollback history retention
paused - Deployment pause state
✨ DeploymentSpec Features: Configure replicas, rolling updates, rollbacks, scaling policies, and pod templates for reliable Django application deployment management.

Parameters description

  • selector: Label selector for pods managed by this Deployment. Must match the pod template's labels for proper ReplicaSet management.
  • template: Pod template describing the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification and resource requirements.
  • replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For Django applications, typically 2-10 replicas depending on traffic and availability requirements.
  • strategy: Strategy used to replace old pods with new ones. RollingUpdate ensures zero-downtime deployments for Django applications.
  • minReadySeconds: Minimum number of seconds for which a newly created pod should be ready without crashing for it to be considered available.
  • revisionHistoryLimit: Number of old ReplicaSets to retain for rollback. For Django applications, typically 5-10 revisions for safe rollbacks.
  • progressDeadlineSeconds: Maximum time in seconds for a deployment to make progress before it is considered failed.
  • paused: Whether the deployment is paused. Useful for manual intervention during Django application updates.

DeploymentStatus

Docs: Kubernetes DeploymentStatus Documentation

Current status of a Deployment including replica counts, update progress, and condition information.

Full description

DeploymentStatus represents the most recently observed status of a Deployment providing real-time information about pod replicas, rolling update progress, and deployment conditions. For Django applications, this status helps monitor deployment health, track rolling updates, and ensure your application maintains the desired availability during updates and scaling operations.

Parameters description

  • replicas: Total number of non-terminating pods targeted by this Deployment. Shows the actual count of pods currently managed.
  • availableReplicas: Number of pods that are available for at least minReadySeconds. Indicates Django application pods ready for production traffic.
  • readyReplicas: Number of pods that have a Ready condition. Shows Django application pods ready to serve requests.
  • updatedReplicas: Number of pods that have been updated to the current template. Tracks rolling update progress for Django deployments.
  • unavailableReplicas: Number of pods that are unavailable during the update. Shows temporary capacity reduction during Django application updates.
  • observedGeneration: Most recent generation observed by the Deployment controller. Used to track if the controller has processed the latest changes.
  • conditions: Current service state conditions of the Deployment. Provides detailed status information about deployment health and progress.
  • collisionCount: Count of hash collisions for the Deployment. Used by the controller for collision avoidance when creating ReplicaSets.
int32

Total number of available non-terminating pods (ready for at least minReadySeconds) targeted by this deployment.

readyReplicas int32

Total number of non-terminating pods targeted by this Deployment with a Ready Condition.

unavailableReplicas int32

Total number of unavailable pods targeted by this deployment. This is the total number of pods that are still required for the deployment to have 100% available capacity.

updatedReplicas int32

Total number of non-terminating pods targeted by this deployment that have the desired template spec.

terminatingReplicas int32

Total number of terminating pods targeted by this deployment. Terminating pods have a non-null .metadata.deletionTimestamp and have not yet reached the Failed or Succeeded .status.phase.

collisionCount int32

Count of hash collisions for the Deployment. The Deployment controller uses this field as a collision avoidance mechanism when it needs to create the name for the newest ReplicaSet.

conditions []DeploymentCondition

Represents the latest available observations of a deployment's current state.

observedGeneration int64

The generation observed by the deployment controller.

DeploymentList

Docs: Kubernetes DeploymentList Documentation

Collection of Deployments with metadata for listing and pagination support.

Full description

DeploymentList is a collection of Deployments used when listing multiple Deployment resources. This is returned by kubectl get deployments or API calls that retrieve multiple deployments. For Django applications, you might have multiple Deployments for different services, environments, or application components managing your Django application stack.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DeploymentList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: string
  continue: string
items:
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: Deployment
  metadata:
    name: string
  spec:
    replicas: int32

Parameters

  • apiVersion - string: APIVersion defines the versioned schema of this representation of an object. Always "apps/v1" for DeploymentList.
  • kind - string: Kind is a string value representing the REST resource this object represents. Always "DeploymentList" for this resource.
  • metadata - ListMeta: Standard list metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#types-kinds
  • items - []Deployment, required: Items is the list of Deployments. More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/deployment

Operations

Docs: Kubernetes Deployment Operations

HTTP API operations for managing Deployment resources with rolling updates and rollback capabilities.

Full description

Deployment operations provide comprehensive HTTP API endpoints for managing Deployment resources in Kubernetes. These operations enable programmatic control over Django application deployments, including creating new deployments, scaling replicas, performing rolling updates, rolling back to previous versions, and monitoring deployment status for production Django applications.

Get Read the Specified Deployment

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/deployments/{name}
Parameters
  • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Deployment
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • pretty - string (query) - If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
Response

200 (Deployment): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Get Deployment Details
curl -X GET \
  $KUBE_API_SERVER/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/deployments/jobpost-deployment \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN"
Result: Returns detailed information about the jobpost-deployment including current status, replicas, and conditions.
Example 2: Get Deployment with kubectl
kubectl get deployment jobpost-deployment -o yaml
Result: Returns the complete Deployment manifest in YAML format showing all current settings and status.

GET
HTTP Request

Response

200 (Deployment): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples

HTTP Request

  • fieldSelector - string (query) - A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields

ReplicaSet

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicaSet v1

ReplicaSet ensures that a specified number of pod replicas are running at any given time.

📋 ReplicaSet Components Overview

A ReplicaSet ensures that a specified number of pod replicas are running at any given time. In other words, a ReplicaSet makes sure that a pod or a homogeneous set of pods is always up and available. If there are too many pods, the ReplicaSet terminates the extra pods. If there are too few, the ReplicaSet starts more pods.

For Django applications, ReplicaSets provide the foundation for maintaining your application's availability and scaling. They are typically managed by higher-level controllers like Deployments, which add features like rolling updates and rollback capabilities. ReplicaSets use more sophisticated label selectors compared to ReplicationControllers, supporting set-based selection requirements.

💡 Note: While you can create ReplicaSets directly, it's recommended to use Deployments instead as they manage ReplicaSets automatically and provide additional features like rolling updates, rollback capabilities, and declarative updates.

🔧 Core Components

ReplicaSetSpec Configuration for desired state, replicas, selector, and pod template
ReplicaSetStatus Current state information including ready replicas and conditions
ReplicaSetList Collection management for multiple ReplicaSet resources

🔧 ReplicaSet Operations Overview

📋 Operation Categories

Create Operations Deploy new ReplicaSets with POST requests
Read Operations Query ReplicaSet information with GET requests
Update Operations Modify ReplicaSet configurations with PUT/PATCH
Delete Operations Remove ReplicaSets with DELETE requests
Scale Operations Scale ReplicaSet replicas for horizontal pod autoscaling
All Detailed Overviews Jump to complete component specifications

ReplicaSet

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicaSet v1 API

Maintains a stable set of replica Pods running at any given time, providing enhanced selector capabilities over ReplicationController.

Full description

A ReplicaSet ensures that a specified number of pod replicas are running at any given time. Unlike ReplicationController, ReplicaSet supports set-based label selectors, making it more flexible for complex Django deployments. ReplicaSets are typically managed by Deployments and provide the foundation for rolling updates and rollbacks. For Django applications, ReplicaSets ensure your JobPost, Author, Location, and Skills models remain accessible by maintaining the desired number of application replicas across your cluster.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
      tier: backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        tier: backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: django-jobpost:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for ReplicaSet resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version to use for this resource.
  • kind: Must be "ReplicaSet" to indicate this is a ReplicaSet resource definition.
  • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. If Labels are empty, they default to the same as the Pod template labels.
  • spec: Specification of the desired behavior of the ReplicaSet. Defines how many replicas to run and the pod template.
  • spec.replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For Django applications, typically 2-5 replicas for high availability and load distribution.
  • spec.selector: Label selector for pods managed by this ReplicaSet. Supports both equality-based and set-based selectors.
  • spec.template: Pod template that describes the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification.
  • status: Most recently observed status of the ReplicaSet. This data may be out of date by some window of time. Populated by the system and read-only.

Return value

ReplicaSet object: Returns the created ReplicaSet resource with system-assigned fields including current replica count, ready replicas, fully labeled replicas, and creation timestamp. The status will show the progression from 0 replicas to the desired count as Pods are created and become ready.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Basic Django JobPost ReplicaSet
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    component: web
    version: v1.0
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
      component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        component: web
        version: v1.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-jobpost
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create the ReplicaSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-jobpost-rs created

# Verify ReplicaSet creation
kubectl get rs anihpj-jobpost-rs
# Output:
# NAME                DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-jobpost-rs   3         3         3       30s

# Check ReplicaSet details
kubectl describe rs anihpj-jobpost-rs
# Output:
# Name:         anihpj-jobpost-rs
# Namespace:    default
# Selector:     app=anihpj-jobpost,component=web
# Labels:       app=anihpj-jobpost
#               component=web
#               version=v1.0
# Replicas:     3 current / 3 desired
# Pods Status:  3 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed
# Pod Template:
#   Labels:  app=anihpj-jobpost
#            component=web
#            version=v1.0
#   Containers:
#    django-jobpost:
#     Image:        anihpj/jobpost:v1.0
#     Port:         8000/TCP
#     Environment:
#       DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE:  anihpj.settings
#       DATABASE_URL:            postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj

# List pods created by ReplicaSet
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-jobpost,component=web
# Output:
# NAME                      READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-jobpost-rs-abc12   1/1     Running   0          35s
# anihpj-jobpost-rs-def34   1/1     Running   0          35s
# anihpj-jobpost-rs-ghi56   1/1     Running   0          35s
Example 2: ReplicaSet with Set-based Selector
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-author
    tier: backend
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchExpressions:
    - key: app
      operator: In
      values: [anihpj-author, anihpj-backend]
    - key: tier
      operator: NotIn
      values: [frontend, cache]
    - key: environment
      operator: Exists
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-author
        tier: backend
        environment: production
        service: authors
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-author
        image: anihpj/author:v2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        - containerPort: 8080
          name: admin
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@author-db:5432/authors"
        - name: REDIS_URL
          value: "redis://redis:6379/1"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "400m"
kubectl commands and results: 
# Apply the ReplicaSet with set-based selectors
kubectl apply -f anihpj-author-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-author-rs created

# Verify the selector expressions work correctly
kubectl get rs anihpj-author-rs -o yaml | grep -A 10 selector
# Output:
#   selector:
#     matchExpressions:
#     - key: app
#       operator: In
#       values:
#       - anihpj-author
#       - anihpj-backend
#     - key: tier
#       operator: NotIn
#       values:
#       - frontend
#       - cache
#     - key: environment
#       operator: Exists

# Check ReplicaSet status and pods
kubectl get rs anihpj-author-rs -o wide
# Output:
# NAME               DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE   CONTAINERS     IMAGES             SELECTOR
# anihpj-author-rs   2         2         2       45s   django-author  anihpj/author:v2.0 app in (anihpj-author,anihpj-backend),environment,tier notin (frontend,cache)

# List pods with labels to verify selector matching
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-author --show-labels
# Output:
# NAME                     READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE   LABELS
# anihpj-author-rs-xyz12   1/1     Running   0          50s   app=anihpj-author,environment=production,service=authors,tier=backend
# anihpj-author-rs-abc34   1/1     Running   0          50s   app=anihpj-author,environment=production,service=authors,tier=backend

# Test that pods with excluded labels are not selected
kubectl get pods -l tier=frontend
# Output: No resources found in default namespace.

# Describe ReplicaSet to see detailed selector information
kubectl describe rs anihpj-author-rs | grep -A 8 "Selector"
# Output:
# Selector:    app in (anihpj-author,anihpj-backend),environment,tier notin (frontend,cache)
# Labels:      app=anihpj-author
#              tier=backend
# Annotations: 
# Replicas:    2 current / 2 desired
# Pods Status: 2 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed
Example 3: ReplicaSet with Resource Limits and ConfigMap
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-location
    component: api
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-location
      component: api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-location
        component: api
        version: v3.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-location
        image: anihpj/location:v3.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.location"
        envFrom:
        - configMapRef:
            name: location-config
        - secretRef:
            name: location-secrets
        volumeMounts:
        - name: location-data
          mountPath: /app/location_data
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /locations/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /locations/ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
      volumes:
      - name: location-data
        emptyDir: {}
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ConfigMap for location settings
kubectl create configmap location-config \
  --from-literal=DATABASE_NAME=locations \
  --from-literal=CACHE_TIMEOUT=3600 \
  --from-literal=API_VERSION=v3.0
# Output: configmap/location-config created

# Create Secret for sensitive data
kubectl create secret generic location-secrets \
  --from-literal=DATABASE_PASSWORD=secretpass \
  --from-literal=API_KEY=xyz123abc
# Output: secret/location-secrets created

# Apply the ReplicaSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-location-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-location-rs created

# Check ReplicaSet with resource information
kubectl get rs anihpj-location-rs -o wide
# Output:
# NAME                  DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE   CONTAINERS       IMAGES                SELECTOR

# Verify resource allocations
kubectl top pods -l app=anihpj-location
# Output:
# NAME                        CPU(cores)   MEMORY(bytes)
# anihpj-location-rs-abc12    145m         387Mi
# anihpj-location-rs-def34    132m         401Mi
