Example 4: ReplicaSet with Advanced Health Checks
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-skills
    tier: backend
    monitoring: enabled
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-skills
      tier: backend
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-skills
        tier: backend
        monitoring: enabled
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-skills
        image: anihpj/skills:v2.1
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        - containerPort: 9090
          name: metrics
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.skills"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@skills-db:5432/skills"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /skills/health/live/
            port: 8000
            httpHeaders:
            - name: X-Health-Check
              value: liveness
          initialDelaySeconds: 60
          periodSeconds: 30
          timeoutSeconds: 5
          failureThreshold: 3
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /skills/health/ready/
            port: 8000
            httpHeaders:
            - name: X-Health-Check
              value: readiness
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 5
          timeoutSeconds: 3
          failureThreshold: 2
        startupProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /skills/health/startup/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 10
          timeoutSeconds: 5
          failureThreshold: 30
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create the ReplicaSet with advanced health checks
kubectl apply -f anihpj-skills-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-skills-rs created

# Monitor pod startup and health check progression
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-skills -w
# Output:
# NAME                     READY   STATUS              RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-skills-rs-abc12   0/1     ContainerCreating   0          5s
# anihpj-skills-rs-def34   0/1     ContainerCreating   0          5s
# anihpj-skills-rs-abc12   0/1     Running             0          15s
# anihpj-skills-rs-def34   0/1     Running             0          15s
# anihpj-skills-rs-abc12   1/1     Running             0          25s
# anihpj-skills-rs-def34   1/1     Running             0          30s

# Check detailed health check configuration
kubectl describe rs anihpj-skills-rs | grep -A 15 "Liveness"
# Output:
#     Liveness:   http-get http://:8000/skills/health/live/ delay=60s timeout=5s period=30s #success=1 #failure=3
#     Readiness:  http-get http://:8000/skills/health/ready/ delay=10s timeout=3s period=5s #success=1 #failure=2
#     Startup:    http-get http://:8000/skills/health/startup/ delay=5s timeout=5s period=10s #success=1 #failure=30

# Test health endpoints manually
kubectl port-forward rs/anihpj-skills-rs 8000:8000 &
curl -H "X-Health-Check: liveness" http://localhost:8000/skills/health/live/
# Output: {"status": "healthy", "timestamp": "2025-09-07T15:30:00Z", "database": "connected"}

curl -H "X-Health-Check: readiness" http://localhost:8000/skills/health/ready/
# Output: {"status": "ready", "database": "connected", "cache": "connected", "migrations": "applied"}

# Monitor health check failures (simulate failure)
kubectl get events --field-selector involvedObject.kind=Pod,reason=Unhealthy
# Output:
# LAST SEEN   TYPE      REASON     OBJECT                         MESSAGE
# 2m          Warning   Unhealthy  pod/anihpj-skills-rs-abc12    Liveness probe failed: HTTP probe failed with statuscode: 503

# Check ReplicaSet status and ready replicas
kubectl get rs anihpj-skills-rs
# Output:
# NAME                DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-skills-rs    2         2         2       5m
Example 5: ReplicaSet with Persistent Storage and Init Containers
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-storage-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-storage
    component: file-service
spec:
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-storage
      component: file-service
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-storage
        component: file-service
    spec:
      initContainers:
      - name: migration-runner
        image: anihpj/migrator:v1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate"]
        env:
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: app-code
          mountPath: /app
      containers:
      - name: django-storage
        image: anihpj/storage:v2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.storage"
        - name: MEDIA_ROOT
          value: "/app/media"
        - name: STATIC_ROOT
          value: "/app/static"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: media-storage
          mountPath: /app/media
        - name: static-files
          mountPath: /app/static
        - name: app-code
          mountPath: /app/code
        - name: uploads
          mountPath: /app/uploads
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /storage/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /storage/ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
      volumes:
      - name: media-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-media-pvc
      - name: static-files
        emptyDir: {}
      - name: app-code
        configMap:
          name: anihpj-code-config
      - name: uploads
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-uploads-pvc
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create PersistentVolumeClaims for storage
kubectl apply -f - <

ReplicaSetSpec

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicaSetSpec Documentation

Specification of a ReplicaSet defining replica count, advanced label selectors, and pod template.

Full description

📋 ReplicaSetSpec Fields Overview

replicas Number of desired pods (typically 2-5 for Django apps)
selector Advanced label selector with set-based matching
template Pod template with Django container specifications
minReadySeconds Minimum seconds for pod readiness validation

ReplicaSetSpec defines the desired behavior of a ReplicaSet for Django applications. It includes the replica count, advanced label selector with set-based matching, and pod template with container specifications. ReplicaSets provide more flexible pod selection than ReplicationControllers, making them ideal for complex Django deployment scenarios with multiple label dimensions.

Parameters description

  • replicas: Number of desired pods. For Django applications, typically 2-5 replicas for high availability. Defaults to 1 if unspecified.
  • selector: Advanced label selector for pods managed by this ReplicaSet. Supports both equality-based and set-based selectors for flexible pod management.
  • template: Pod template describing the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification, resource requirements, and pod metadata.
  • minReadySeconds: Minimum number of seconds for which a newly created pod should be ready without crashing for it to be considered available.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Basic ReplicaSetSpec Configuration
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-spec-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
      tier: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        tier: web
        version: v1.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-jobpost
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj"
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ReplicaSet and examine spec
kubectl apply -f anihpj-jobpost-spec-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-jobpost-spec-rs created

# View the ReplicaSetSpec configuration
kubectl get rs anihpj-jobpost-spec-rs -o yaml | grep -A 20 "spec:"
# Output:
# spec:
#   replicas: 3
#   selector:
#     matchLabels:
#       app: anihpj-jobpost
#       tier: web
#   template:
#     metadata:
#       creationTimestamp: null
#       labels:
#         app: anihpj-jobpost
#         tier: web
#         version: v1.0
#     spec:
#       containers:
#       - env:
#         - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
#           value: anihpj.settings
#         - name: DATABASE_URL
#           value: postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj

# Verify replica count from spec
kubectl get rs anihpj-jobpost-spec-rs -o jsonpath='{.spec.replicas}'
# Output: 3

# Check selector matching
kubectl get rs anihpj-jobpost-spec-rs -o jsonpath='{.spec.selector.matchLabels}'
# Output: {"app":"anihpj-jobpost","tier":"web"}
Example 2: ReplicaSetSpec with Set-based Selectors
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-selector-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-author
    matchExpressions:
    - key: environment
      operator: In
      values: [production, staging]
    - key: component
      operator: NotIn
      values: [test, debug]
    - key: version
      operator: Exists
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-author
        environment: production
        component: backend
        version: v2.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-author
        image: anihpj/author:v2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: AUTHOR_API_ENABLED
          value: "true"
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@author-db:5432/authors"
kubectl commands and results: 
# Apply ReplicaSet with complex selectors
kubectl apply -f anihpj-author-selector-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-author-selector-rs created

# Examine the selector expressions in detail
kubectl get rs anihpj-author-selector-rs -o yaml | grep -A 15 "selector:"
# Output:
# selector:
#   matchExpressions:
#   - key: environment
#     operator: In
#     values:
#     - production
#     - staging
#   - key: component
#     operator: NotIn
#     values:
#     - test
#     - debug
#   - key: version
#     operator: Exists
#   matchLabels:
#     app: anihpj-author

# Test selector matching with different label combinations
kubectl get pods -l 'app=anihpj-author,environment in (production,staging),component notin (test,debug),version'
# Output:
# NAME                              READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-author-selector-rs-abc12   1/1     Running   0          45s
# anihpj-author-selector-rs-def34   1/1     Running   0          45s

# Verify pods that wouldn't match the selector
kubectl run test-pod --image=nginx --labels="app=anihpj-author,environment=development" --rm -it --restart=Never -- echo "test"
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-author
# Output: Only shows production pods, not development test pod
Example 3: ReplicaSetSpec with minReadySeconds
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-ready-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 3
  minReadySeconds: 30
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-location
      stability: high
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-location
        stability: high
        service: location-api
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-location
        image: anihpj/location:v1.5
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: LOCATION_SERVICE_ENABLED
          value: "true"
        - name: MIN_READY_TIME
          value: "30"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /locations/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 5
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /locations/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ReplicaSet with minReadySeconds
kubectl apply -f anihpj-location-ready-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-location-ready-rs created

# Monitor pod ready progression with timing
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-location -w
# Output:
# NAME                               READY   STATUS              RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-location-ready-rs-abc12     0/1     ContainerCreating   0          5s
# anihpj-location-ready-rs-def34     0/1     ContainerCreating   0          5s
# anihpj-location-ready-rs-ghi56     0/1     ContainerCreating   0          5s
# anihpj-location-ready-rs-abc12     0/1     Running             0          15s
# anihpj-location-ready-rs-abc12     1/1     Running             0          25s
# (Wait 30 seconds for minReadySeconds)

# Check ReplicaSet status showing available vs ready replicas
kubectl get rs anihpj-location-ready-rs
# Output:
# NAME                        DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-location-ready-rs    3         3         3       1m

# Verify minReadySeconds configuration
kubectl get rs anihpj-location-ready-rs -o jsonpath='{.spec.minReadySeconds}'
# Output: 30

# Check status showing availability progression
kubectl describe rs anihpj-location-ready-rs | grep -A 5 "Pods Status"
# Output:
# Pods Status:  3 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed
# Events:
#   Normal  SuccessfulCreate  1m    replicaset-controller  Created pod: anihpj-location-ready-rs-abc12
#   Normal  SuccessfulCreate  1m    replicaset-controller  (combined from similar events): Created pod: anihpj-location-ready-rs-ghi56
Example 4: ReplicaSetSpec with Resource Specifications
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-skills-resource-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 4
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-skills
      tier: api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-skills
        tier: api
        resource-class: standard
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-skills
        image: anihpj/skills:v3.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        env:
        - name: SKILLS_API_ENABLED
          value: "true"
        - name: MAX_MEMORY_MB
          value: "1024"
        - name: CPU_LIMIT_MILLICORES
          value: "500"
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ReplicaSet with resource specifications
kubectl apply -f anihpj-skills-resource-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-skills-resource-rs created

# Examine resource specifications in the template
kubectl get rs anihpj-skills-resource-rs -o yaml | grep -A 10 "resources:"
# Output:
#         resources:
#           limits:
#             cpu: 500m
#             memory: 1Gi
#           requests:
#             cpu: 250m
#             memory: 512Mi

# Monitor actual resource usage
kubectl top pods -l app=anihpj-skills
# Output:
# NAME                               CPU(cores)   MEMORY(bytes)
# anihpj-skills-resource-rs-abc12    187m         445Mi
# anihpj-skills-resource-rs-def34    203m         478Mi
# anihpj-skills-resource-rs-ghi56    165m         398Mi
# anihpj-skills-resource-rs-jkl78    190m         456Mi

# Check resource allocation across nodes
kubectl describe nodes | grep -A 5 "Allocated resources"
# Output:
#   Allocated resources:
#     (Total limits may be over 100 percent, i.e., overcommitted.)
#     Resource           Requests      Limits

# Verify that all pods are within resource limits
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-skills -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}: {.spec.containers[0].resources}{"\n"}{end}'
# Output:
# anihpj-skills-resource-rs-abc12: {"limits":{"cpu":"500m","memory":"1Gi"},"requests":{"cpu":"250m","memory":"512Mi"}}
# anihpj-skills-resource-rs-def34: {"limits":{"cpu":"500m","memory":"1Gi"},"requests":{"cpu":"250m","memory":"512Mi"}}
Example 5: ReplicaSetSpec with Complex Template Configuration
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-complex-template-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-complex
      deployment-type: multi-service
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-complex
        deployment-type: multi-service
        service-tier: backend
      annotations:
        config-hash: "abc123"
        deployment-version: "v4.0"
    spec:
      initContainers:
      - name: db-migrator
        image: anihpj/migrator:v1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate"]
        env:
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://user:pass@db:5432/anihpj"
      containers:
      - name: django-web
        image: anihpj/web:v4.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        - containerPort: 8080
          name: admin
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: WEB_CONCURRENCY
          value: "4"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: config-volume
          mountPath: /app/config
        - name: static-files
          mountPath: /app/static
      - name: nginx-proxy
        image: nginx:1.21
        ports:
        - containerPort: 80
        volumeMounts:
        - name: nginx-config
          mountPath: /etc/nginx/conf.d
        - name: static-files
          mountPath: /var/www/static
      volumes:
      - name: config-volume
        configMap:
          name: anihpj-config
      - name: nginx-config
        configMap:
          name: nginx-config
      - name: static-files
        emptyDir: {}
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create required ConfigMaps first
kubectl create configmap anihpj-config \
  --from-literal=database_host=db.example.com \
  --from-literal=redis_url=redis://cache:6379
# Output: configmap/anihpj-config created

kubectl create configmap nginx-config \
  --from-literal=default.conf="server { listen 80; location / { proxy_pass http://127.0.0.1:8000; } }"
# Output: configmap/nginx-config created

# Apply complex ReplicaSet template
kubectl apply -f anihpj-complex-template-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-complex-template-rs created

# Examine the complete template specification
kubectl get rs anihpj-complex-template-rs -o yaml | grep -A 40 "template:"
# Output:
# template:
#   metadata:
#     annotations:
#       config-hash: abc123
#       deployment-version: v4.0
#     creationTimestamp: null
#     labels:
#       app: anihpj-complex
#       deployment-type: multi-service
#       service-tier: backend
#   spec:
#     containers:
#     - env:
#       - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
#         value: anihpj.settings.production
#       - name: WEB_CONCURRENCY
#         value: "4"
#       image: anihpj/web:v4.0
#       name: django-web
#       ports:
#       - containerPort: 8000
#         name: http
#       - containerPort: 8080
#         name: admin

# Monitor init container execution
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-complex
# Output:
# NAME                              READY   STATUS     RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-complex-template-rs-abc12  0/2     Init:0/1   0          15s
# anihpj-complex-template-rs-def34  0/2     Init:0/1   0          15s

# Check init container logs
kubectl logs anihpj-complex-template-rs-abc12 -c db-migrator
# Output:

#   Apply all migrations: admin, auth, contenttypes, jobpost

# Verify multi-container pod status

# Output:

#   django-web:
#     Container ID:   docker://abc123...

#     Port:           8000/TCP, 8080/TCP

#     Image:          nginx:1.21
#     Port:           80/TCP

ReplicaSetStatus

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicaSetStatus Documentation

Current status of a ReplicaSet including replica counts and condition information.

Full description

📋 ReplicaSetStatus Fields Overview

replicas Total number of non-terminating pods currently managed
availableReplicas Pods available for traffic (ready for minReadySeconds)
readyReplicas Pods with Ready condition (able to serve requests)
fullyLabeledReplicas Pods with complete label matching requirements
observedGeneration Latest generation processed by controller
conditions Current service state and health conditions

ReplicaSetStatus represents the current state of a ReplicaSet providing real-time information about pod replicas and controller conditions. For Django applications, this status helps monitor deployment health, track replica availability, and ensure your application maintains the desired replica count for consistent service delivery and load distribution.

Parameters description

  • replicas: Most recently observed number of non-terminating pods. Shows the actual count of pods currently managed by this ReplicaSet.
  • availableReplicas: Number of pods that are available for at least minReadySeconds. Indicates Django application pods ready for production traffic.
  • readyReplicas: Number of pods that have a Ready condition. Shows Django application pods ready to serve requests.
  • fullyLabeledReplicas: Number of pods that have all required labels matching the ReplicaSet selector.
  • observedGeneration: Most recent generation observed by the ReplicaSet controller. Used to track if the controller has processed the latest changes.
  • conditions: Current service state conditions of the ReplicaSet. Provides detailed status information about deployment health.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Healthy ReplicaSetStatus
# ReplicaSet with healthy status
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-status-healthy-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-status
      tier: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-status
        tier: web
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/status:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create and monitor healthy ReplicaSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-status-healthy-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-status-healthy-rs created

# Check ReplicaSetStatus with all replicas healthy
kubectl get rs anihpj-status-healthy-rs -o yaml | grep -A 10 "status:"
# Output:
# status:
#   availableReplicas: 3
#   fullyLabeledReplicas: 3
#   observedGeneration: 1
#   readyReplicas: 3
#   replicas: 3

# Verify status fields individually
kubectl get rs anihpj-status-healthy-rs -o jsonpath='{.status.replicas}'
# Output: 3

kubectl get rs anihpj-status-healthy-rs -o jsonpath='{.status.readyReplicas}'
# Output: 3

kubectl get rs anihpj-status-healthy-rs -o jsonpath='{.status.availableReplicas}'
# Output: 3

# Check detailed status with kubectl describe
kubectl describe rs anihpj-status-healthy-rs | grep -A 5 "Pods Status"
# Output:
# Pods Status:  3 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed
# Pod Template:
#   Labels:  app=anihpj-status
#            tier=web
# Events:
#   Normal  SuccessfulCreate  2m  replicaset-controller  Created pod: anihpj-status-healthy-rs-abc12
Example 2: ReplicaSetStatus During Scaling
# Scale ReplicaSet and monitor status changes
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-scaling-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-scaling
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-scaling
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-scaling
        image: anihpj/scaling:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create initial ReplicaSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-scaling-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-scaling-rs created

# Check initial status
kubectl get rs anihpj-scaling-rs
# Output:
# NAME                 DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-scaling-rs    2         2         2       30s

# Scale up to 5 replicas
kubectl scale rs anihpj-scaling-rs --replicas=5
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-scaling-rs scaled

# Monitor status during scaling
kubectl get rs anihpj-scaling-rs -w
# Output:
# NAME                 DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-scaling-rs    5         2         2       1m
# anihpj-scaling-rs    5         3         2       1m
# anihpj-scaling-rs    5         4         3       1m
# anihpj-scaling-rs    5         5         4       1m
# anihpj-scaling-rs    5         5         5       1m

# Check status during scaling process
kubectl get rs anihpj-scaling-rs -o jsonpath='{.status}'
# Output: {"availableReplicas":5,"fullyLabeledReplicas":5,"observedGeneration":2,"readyReplicas":5,"replicas":5}

# Scale down and monitor
kubectl scale rs anihpj-scaling-rs --replicas=3
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-scaling-rs scaled

kubectl get rs anihpj-scaling-rs -o yaml | grep -A 8 "status:"
# Output:
# status:
#   availableReplicas: 3
#   fullyLabeledReplicas: 3
#   observedGeneration: 3
#   readyReplicas: 3
#   replicas: 3
Example 3: ReplicaSetStatus with Pod Failures
# ReplicaSet with failing pods to show status differences
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-failing-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-failing
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-failing
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-failing
        image: anihpj/failing:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: SIMULATE_FAILURE
          value: "true"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
          failureThreshold: 3
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ReplicaSet with failing pods
kubectl apply -f anihpj-failing-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-failing-rs created

# Monitor status with some pods failing readiness checks
kubectl get rs anihpj-failing-rs
# Output:
# NAME                 DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-failing-rs    3         3         1       45s

# Check detailed status showing discrepancy between replicas and ready
kubectl get rs anihpj-failing-rs -o yaml | grep -A 8 "status:"
# Output:
# status:
#   availableReplicas: 1
#   fullyLabeledReplicas: 3
#   observedGeneration: 1
#   readyReplicas: 1
#   replicas: 3

# See individual pod statuses
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-failing
# Output:
# NAME                      READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-failing-rs-abc12   1/1     Running   0          1m
# anihpj-failing-rs-def34   0/1     Running   0          1m
# anihpj-failing-rs-ghi56   0/1     Running   0          1m

# Check events to understand failures
kubectl get events --field-selector involvedObject.name=anihpj-failing-rs-def34
# Output:
# LAST SEEN   TYPE      REASON     OBJECT                        MESSAGE
# 2m          Warning   Unhealthy  pod/anihpj-failing-rs-def34   Readiness probe failed: HTTP probe failed with statuscode: 503

# Monitor status difference between total replicas and ready replicas
kubectl get rs anihpj-failing-rs -o custom-columns=NAME:.metadata.name,DESIRED:.spec.replicas,CURRENT:.status.replicas,READY:.status.readyReplicas,AVAILABLE:.status.availableReplicas
# Output:
# NAME                 DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AVAILABLE
# anihpj-failing-rs    3         3         1       1
Example 4: ReplicaSetStatus with Conditions
# ReplicaSet configured to show status conditions
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-conditions-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-conditions
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-conditions
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-conditions
        image: anihpj/conditions:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "2Gi"  # Intentionally high to potentially cause issues
            cpu: "1000m"
          limits:
            memory: "2Gi"
            cpu: "1000m"
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ReplicaSet that may show condition information
kubectl apply -f anihpj-conditions-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-conditions-rs created

# Check ReplicaSet conditions in status
kubectl get rs anihpj-conditions-rs -o yaml | grep -A 15 "conditions:"
# Output:
# conditions:
# - lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-07T15:30:00Z"
#   message: All replicas are running successfully
#   reason: AllReplicasRunning
#   status: "False"
#   type: ReplicaFailure

# Get conditions in a more readable format
kubectl describe rs anihpj-conditions-rs | grep -A 10 "Conditions:"
# Output:
# Conditions:
#   Type             Status  LastTransitionTime  Reason               Message
#   ----             ------  ------------------  ------               -------
#   ReplicaFailure   False   2025-09-07T15:30:00Z  AllReplicasRunning   All replicas are running successfully

# Check observedGeneration to see if controller is up to date
kubectl get rs anihpj-conditions-rs -o jsonpath='{.status.observedGeneration} {.metadata.generation}'
# Output: 1 1

# Simulate resource constraint condition by scaling beyond node capacity
kubectl scale rs anihpj-conditions-rs --replicas=10
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-conditions-rs scaled

# Check status after scaling beyond capacity
kubectl get rs anihpj-conditions-rs -o yaml | grep -A 20 "status:"
# Output:
# status:
#   availableReplicas: 2
#   conditions:
#   - lastTransitionTime: "2025-09-07T15:35:00Z"
#     message: 'pods "anihpj-conditions-rs-jkl78" is forbidden: insufficient memory'
#     reason: FailedCreate
#     status: "True"
#     type: ReplicaFailure
#   fullyLabeledReplicas: 2
#   observedGeneration: 2
#   readyReplicas: 2
#   replicas: 2

# Monitor pod creation failures
kubectl get events --field-selector reason=FailedCreate
# Output:
# LAST SEEN   TYPE      REASON        OBJECT                        MESSAGE
# 1m          Warning   FailedCreate  rs/anihpj-conditions-rs       Error creating: pods "anihpj-conditions-rs-xyz89" is forbidden: insufficient memory
Example 5: ReplicaSetStatus ObservedGeneration Tracking
# ReplicaSet to demonstrate observedGeneration changes
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-generation-rs
  namespace: default
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-generation
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-generation
        version: v1.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-generation
        image: anihpj/generation:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        env:
        - name: APP_VERSION
          value: "v1.0"
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create initial ReplicaSet and check generation
kubectl apply -f anihpj-generation-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-generation-rs created

# Check initial metadata and status generation
kubectl get rs anihpj-generation-rs -o jsonpath='{.metadata.generation} {.status.observedGeneration}'
# Output: 1 1

# Update the ReplicaSet template (change image version)
kubectl patch rs anihpj-generation-rs --type='merge' -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"django-generation","image":"anihpj/generation:v2.0","env":[{"name":"APP_VERSION","value":"v2.0"}]}]}}}}'
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-generation-rs patched

# Check generation increment
kubectl get rs anihpj-generation-rs -o jsonpath='{.metadata.generation} {.status.observedGeneration}'
# Output: 2 2

# Scale the ReplicaSet to see another generation change
kubectl scale rs anihpj-generation-rs --replicas=4
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-generation-rs scaled

# Monitor generation tracking
kubectl get rs anihpj-generation-rs -o jsonpath='{.metadata.generation} {.status.observedGeneration}'
# Output: 3 3

# View complete status with generation info
kubectl get rs anihpj-generation-rs -o yaml | grep -A 15 "status:"
# Output:
# status:
#   availableReplicas: 4
#   fullyLabeledReplicas: 4
#   observedGeneration: 3
#   readyReplicas: 4
#   replicas: 4

# Check that new pods have updated template
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-generation -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}: {.spec.containers[0].image}{"\n"}{end}'
# Output:
# anihpj-generation-rs-abc12: anihpj/generation:v1.0
# anihpj-generation-rs-def34: anihpj/generation:v1.0
# anihpj-generation-rs-ghi56: anihpj/generation:v2.0
# anihpj-generation-rs-jkl78: anihpj/generation:v2.0

# Note: ReplicaSet doesn't automatically update existing pods with template changes
# Only new pods get the updated template

ReplicaSetList

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicaSetList Documentation

Collection of ReplicaSets with metadata for listing and pagination support.

Full description

📋 ReplicaSetList Components Overview

apiVersion API version (apps/v1) for ReplicaSet collections
kind Resource type identifier (ReplicaSetList)
metadata Collection metadata with resource version and pagination info
items Array of ReplicaSet objects matching query criteria

ReplicaSetList is a collection of ReplicaSets used when listing multiple ReplicaSet resources. This is returned by kubectl get replicasets or API calls that retrieve multiple ReplicaSets. For Django applications, you might have multiple ReplicaSets managed by different Deployments for various services or application components.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSetList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "12345"
items:
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: ReplicaSet
  metadata:
    name: jobpost-rs-1
  spec: ...
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: ReplicaSet
  metadata:
    name: jobpost-rs-2
  spec: ...

Parameters Description

  • apiVersion - string: API version for ReplicaSetList, always "apps/v1"
  • kind - string: Resource type, always "ReplicaSetList"
  • metadata - ListMeta: Standard list metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#types-kinds
  • items - []ReplicaSet, required: List of ReplicaSets. More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/replicaset

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Basic ReplicaSetList Query
# Create multiple ReplicaSets for different Django services
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-jobpost-list-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-jobpost
    service: web
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-jobpost
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-jobpost
        service: web
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-jobpost
        image: anihpj/jobpost:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
---
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-author-list-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-author
    service: api
spec:
  replicas: 2
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-author
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-author
        service: api
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-author
        image: anihpj/author:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create multiple ReplicaSets
kubectl apply -f anihpj-multiple-rs.yaml
# Output:
# replicaset.apps/anihpj-jobpost-list-rs created
# replicaset.apps/anihpj-author-list-rs created

# Get ReplicaSetList for all ReplicaSets
kubectl get rs -o yaml | head -20
# Output:
# apiVersion: v1
# items:
# - apiVersion: apps/v1
#   kind: ReplicaSet
#   metadata:
#     creationTimestamp: "2025-09-07T15:45:00Z"
#     generation: 1
#     labels:
#       app: anihpj-jobpost
#       service: web
#     name: anihpj-jobpost-list-rs
#     namespace: default
#     resourceVersion: "12345"
#     uid: abc123-def456-ghi789
#   spec:
#     replicas: 3
#     selector:
#       matchLabels:
#         app: anihpj-jobpost

# List all ReplicaSets with basic information
kubectl get rs
# Output:
# NAME                     DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-jobpost-list-rs   3         3         3       30s
# anihpj-author-list-rs    2         2         2       30s

# Get ReplicaSetList metadata information
kubectl get rs -o jsonpath='{.metadata.resourceVersion}'
# Output: 12345
Example 2: Filtered ReplicaSetList with Label Selectors
# Create ReplicaSets with different labels
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-prod-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-location
    environment: production
    tier: backend
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-location
      environment: production
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-location
        environment: production
        tier: backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-location
        image: anihpj/location:v2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
---
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-location-staging-rs
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-location
    environment: staging
    tier: backend
spec:
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-location
      environment: staging
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-location
        environment: staging
        tier: backend
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-location
        image: anihpj/location:v1.9
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ReplicaSets with different environments
kubectl apply -f anihpj-location-envs-rs.yaml
# Output:
# replicaset.apps/anihpj-location-prod-rs created
# replicaset.apps/anihpj-location-staging-rs created

# Filter ReplicaSetList by environment label
kubectl get rs -l environment=production
# Output:
# NAME                      DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-location-prod-rs   3         3         3       45s

# Filter by app and tier labels
kubectl get rs -l app=anihpj-location,tier=backend
# Output:
# NAME                         DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-location-prod-rs      3         3         3       50s
# anihpj-location-staging-rs   1         1         1       50s

# Get filtered ReplicaSetList in JSON format
kubectl get rs -l environment=production -o json | jq '.items | length'
# Output: 1

# Use field selectors to filter by metadata
kubectl get rs --field-selector metadata.name=anihpj-location-prod-rs
# Output:
# NAME                      DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-location-prod-rs   3         3         3       1m

# Combine label and field selectors
kubectl get rs -l tier=backend --field-selector status.replicas=3
# Output:
# NAME                      DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-location-prod-rs   3         3         3       1m
Example 3: Cross-Namespace ReplicaSetList
# Create ReplicaSets in different namespaces
kubectl create namespace anihpj-production
kubectl create namespace anihpj-staging

# Create production ReplicaSet
kubectl apply -f - <
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create namespaces and ReplicaSets
kubectl create namespace anihpj-production
# Output: namespace/anihpj-production created

kubectl create namespace anihpj-staging  
# Output: namespace/anihpj-staging created

# Apply ReplicaSets to different namespaces
kubectl apply -f production-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-skills-rs created

kubectl apply -f staging-rs.yaml
# Output: replicaset.apps/anihpj-skills-rs created

# Get ReplicaSetList across all namespaces
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces
# Output:
# NAMESPACE            NAME                DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-production    anihpj-skills-rs    4         4         4       30s
# anihpj-staging       anihpj-skills-rs    2         2         2       25s
# default              anihpj-jobpost-rs   3         3         3       5m

# Filter across namespaces by label
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -l app=anihpj-skills
# Output:
# NAMESPACE            NAME                DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-production    anihpj-skills-rs    4         4         4       45s
# anihpj-staging       anihpj-skills-rs    2         2         2       40s

# Get ReplicaSetList in JSON format across namespaces
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -o json | jq '.items | map({name: .metadata.name, namespace: .metadata.namespace, replicas: .spec.replicas})'
# Output:
# [
#   {
#     "name": "anihpj-skills-rs",
#     "namespace": "anihpj-production", 
#     "replicas": 4
#   },
#   {
#     "name": "anihpj-skills-rs",
#     "namespace": "anihpj-staging",
#     "replicas": 2
#   }
# ]

# Get specific namespace ReplicaSetList
kubectl get rs -n anihpj-production
# Output:
# NAME               DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-skills-rs   4         4         4       1m
Example 4: ReplicaSetList with Custom Output Formats
# Using previously created ReplicaSets
kubectl commands and results: 
# Custom columns for ReplicaSetList
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -o custom-columns=\
NAMESPACE:.metadata.namespace,\
NAME:.metadata.name,\
DESIRED:.spec.replicas,\
CURRENT:.status.replicas,\
READY:.status.readyReplicas,\
AGE:.metadata.creationTimestamp
# Output:
# NAMESPACE            NAME                         DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-production    anihpj-skills-rs            4         4         4       2025-09-07T15:50:00Z
# anihpj-staging       anihpj-skills-rs            2         2         2       2025-09-07T15:50:05Z
# default              anihpj-jobpost-list-rs       3         3         3       2025-09-07T15:45:00Z
# default              anihpj-author-list-rs        2         2         2       2025-09-07T15:45:00Z

# Wide output for detailed information
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -o wide
# Output:
# NAMESPACE         NAME                    DESIRED CURRENT READY AGE   CONTAINERS      IMAGES                SELECTOR
# anihpj-production anihpj-skills-rs        4       4       4     3m    django-skills   anihpj/skills:v3.0    app=anihpj-skills
# anihpj-staging    anihpj-skills-rs        2       2       2     3m    django-skills   anihpj/skills:v2.5    app=anihpj-skills
# default           anihpj-jobpost-list-rs  3       3       3     8m    django-jobpost  anihpj/jobpost:v1.0   app=anihpj-jobpost

# JSONPath output for specific fields
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.namespace}/{.metadata.name}: desired={.spec.replicas}, ready={.status.readyReplicas}{"\n"}{end}'
# Output:
# anihpj-production/anihpj-skills-rs: desired=4, ready=4
# anihpj-staging/anihpj-skills-rs: desired=2, ready=2
# default/anihpj-jobpost-list-rs: desired=3, ready=3
# default/anihpj-author-list-rs: desired=2, ready=2

# Table format with sorting
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces --sort-by=.spec.replicas
# Output:
# NAMESPACE            NAME                    DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-staging       anihpj-skills-rs        2         2         2       4m
# default              anihpj-author-list-rs   2         2         2       9m
# default              anihpj-jobpost-list-rs  3         3         3       9m
# anihpj-production    anihpj-skills-rs        4         4         4       4m

# YAML output for complete ReplicaSetList structure
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -o yaml | grep -A 5 "apiVersion\|kind:\|metadata:"
# Output:
# apiVersion: v1
# items:
# - apiVersion: apps/v1
#   kind: ReplicaSet
#   metadata:
#     creationTimestamp: "2025-09-07T15:50:00Z"
Example 5: ReplicaSetList Monitoring and Watch
# Monitor ReplicaSetList changes in real-time
kubectl commands and results: 
# Watch all ReplicaSets for changes
kubectl get rs --all-namespaces -w
# Output:
# NAMESPACE            NAME                    DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   AGE
# anihpj-production    anihpj-skills-rs        4         4         4       5m
# anihpj-staging       anihpj-skills-rs        2         2         2       5m
# default              anihpj-jobpost-list-rs  3         3         3       10m
# default              anihpj-author-list-rs   2         2         2       10m
# (waiting for changes...)

# Create a new ReplicaSet while watching
kubectl apply -f - <

Operations

Docs: Kubernetes ReplicaSet Operations

HTTP API operations for managing ReplicaSet resources with advanced label selector capabilities.

Full description

ReplicaSet operations provide HTTP API endpoints for managing ReplicaSet resources in Kubernetes. These operations enable programmatic control over Django application replicas with advanced label selectors, allowing sophisticated pod management strategies, scaling operations, and integration with higher-level controllers like Deployments.

Get Read the Specified ReplicaSet

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicasets/{name}
Parameters
  • name - string, required (path) - Name of the ReplicaSet
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace of the ReplicaSet
  • pretty - string (query) - Pretty print the output
Return Value

200 (ReplicaSet): OK - Returns the ReplicaSet object

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Get JobPost ReplicaSet
curl -X GET \
  https://kubernetes-api/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/replicasets/jobpost-rs \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN"
Result: Returns the jobpost-rs ReplicaSet details including current status and replica count.
Example 2: Get with Kubectl
kubectl get replicaset jobpost-rs -o yaml
Result: Returns formatted YAML output of the ReplicaSet configuration and status.

Get Read Status of the Specified ReplicaSet

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicasets/{name}/status
Return Value

200 (ReplicaSet): OK - Returns the ReplicaSet status

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example: Get ReplicaSet Status
kubectl get replicaset jobpost-rs -o jsonpath='{.status}'
Result: Returns only the status portion showing replica counts and conditions.

List ReplicaSets

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicasets
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace to list ReplicaSets from
  • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector to filter ReplicaSets
  • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector to filter ReplicaSets
  • watch - boolean (query) - Watch for changes to ReplicaSets
Return Value

200 (ReplicaSetList): OK - Returns list of ReplicaSets

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: List All ReplicaSets
kubectl get replicasets
Result: Lists all ReplicaSets in the current namespace.
Example 2: List with Label Selector
kubectl get replicasets -l app=jobpost
Result: Lists only ReplicaSets with the label app=jobpost.

List ReplicaSets (All Namespaces)

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/replicasets
Examples
Example: List Across All Namespaces
kubectl get replicasets --all-namespaces
Result: Lists ReplicaSets from all namespaces in the cluster.

Create a ReplicaSet

POST
HTTP Request
POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicasets
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace to create the ReplicaSet in
  • body - ReplicaSet, required - ReplicaSet object to create
  • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
Return Value

200 (ReplicaSet): OK

201 (ReplicaSet): Created

202 (ReplicaSet): Accepted

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Create JobPost ReplicaSet
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ReplicaSet
metadata:
  name: jobpost-rs
spec:
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: jobpost
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: jobpost
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: jobpost:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
EOF

Delete a ReplicaSet

DELETE
HTTP Request
DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/replicasets/{name}
Parameters

  • propagationPolicy - string (query) - How to handle dependent objects

Result: Deletes all ReplicaSets with the label app=jobpost.

StatefulSet

Docs: Kubernetes StatefulSet v1

StatefulSet represents a set of pods with consistent identities.

📋 StatefulSet Components Overview

StatefulSet represents a set of pods with consistent identities. Identities are defined as:

  • Network: A single stable DNS and hostname
  • Storage: As many VolumeClaims as requested

The StatefulSet guarantees that a given network identity will always map to the same storage identity.

For Django applications, StatefulSets are essential when you need stable, persistent identities for your pods. This is particularly useful for stateful applications like databases, message brokers, or Django applications that require persistent storage or stable network identities. Unlike Deployments, StatefulSets provide ordered deployment, scaling, and deletion of pods with predictable names and persistent storage.

💡 Note: StatefulSets are valuable for Django applications that need persistent data, ordered operations, or stable network identities. Common use cases include Django applications with local file storage, distributed caches, or applications requiring specific initialization order.

🔧 Core Components

StatefulSetSpec Configuration for stable identities, persistent storage, and ordered operations
StatefulSetStatus Current state with replica counts, generation, and update status
StatefulSetList Collection management for multiple StatefulSet resources

🔧 StatefulSet Operations Overview

📋 Operation Categories

Create Operations Deploy new StatefulSets with POST requests
Read Operations Query StatefulSet information with GET requests
Update Operations Modify StatefulSet configurations with PUT/PATCH
Delete Operations Remove StatefulSets with DELETE requests
Scale Operations Scale StatefulSet replicas with ordered operations
All Detailed Overviews Jump to complete component specifications

StatefulSet

Docs: Kubernetes StatefulSet v1 API

Manages stateful applications with stable network identities, persistent storage, and ordered deployment/scaling.

Full description

StatefulSet manages the deployment and scaling of a set of Pods with stable, unique network identities and persistent storage. Unlike Deployments, StatefulSets maintain the identity of each Pod across rescheduling. This is essential for Django applications that require persistent storage (like user uploads), ordered startup (database initialization), or stable network identities. When deploying Django with a database like PostgreSQL, StatefulSets ensure data persistence and ordered startup for your JobPost, Author, Location, and Skills models.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: string
  namespace: string
spec:
  serviceName: string
  replicas: int32
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      key: value
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        key: value
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: string
        image: string
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: string
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: string
status:
  replicas: int32
  readyReplicas: int32

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for StatefulSet resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version to use for this resource.
  • kind: Must be "StatefulSet" to indicate this is a StatefulSet resource definition.
  • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. Essential for organizing and managing stateful Django deployments.
  • spec: Specification of the desired behavior of the StatefulSet. Defines replicas, service name, selector, and pod template with persistent storage.
  • spec.serviceName: Name of the service that governs this StatefulSet. Required for maintaining stable network identities for Django pods.
  • spec.replicas: Number of desired pod replicas. For stateful Django applications with databases, typically 1-3 replicas.
  • spec.selector: Label selector for pods managed by this StatefulSet. Must match template labels for proper pod management.
  • spec.template: Pod template that describes the pods that will be created. Contains the Django container specification with persistent storage mounts.
  • spec.volumeClaimTemplates: List of claims that pods are allowed to reference. Each StatefulSet pod gets its own persistent volume for data storage.
  • status: Most recently observed status of the StatefulSet. Populated by the system and provides deployment progress information.

Return value

StatefulSet object: Returns the created StatefulSet resource with system-assigned fields including creation timestamp, generation number, and status. The status will show replica progression, current replicas, and ready replicas as the StatefulSet creates pods with stable identities and persistent storage.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Django with PostgreSQL StatefulSet
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-postgres-sts
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-postgres
    component: database
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-postgres-service
  replicas: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-postgres
      component: database
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-postgres
        component: database
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: postgres
        image: postgres:15
        ports:
        - containerPort: 5432
          name: postgres
        env:
        - name: POSTGRES_DB
          value: anihpj_db
        - name: POSTGRES_USER
          value: anihpj_user
        - name: POSTGRES_PASSWORD
          value: anihpj_password
        - name: PGDATA
          value: /var/lib/postgresql/data/pgdata
        volumeMounts:
        - name: postgres-data
          mountPath: /var/lib/postgresql/data
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        livenessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - pg_isready
            - -U
            - anihpj_user
            - -d
            - anihpj_db
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - pg_isready
            - -U
            - anihpj_user
            - -d
            - anihpj_db
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: postgres-data
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 20Gi
      storageClassName: standard
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create the StatefulSet for PostgreSQL
kubectl apply -f anihpj-postgres-sts.yaml
# Output: statefulset.apps/anihpj-postgres-sts created

# Monitor StatefulSet pod creation (ordered)
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-postgres -w
# Output:
# NAME                    READY   STATUS              RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-postgres-sts-0   0/1     Pending             0          5s
# anihpj-postgres-sts-0   0/1     ContainerCreating   0          10s
# anihpj-postgres-sts-0   1/1     Running             0          25s

# Check StatefulSet status
kubectl get sts anihpj-postgres-sts
# Output:
# NAME                   READY   AGE
# anihpj-postgres-sts    1/1     30s

# Verify persistent volume claim was created
kubectl get pvc
# Output:
# NAME                              STATUS   VOLUME                                     CAPACITY   ACCESS MODES   STORAGECLASS   AGE
# postgres-data-anihpj-postgres-sts-0   Bound    pvc-abc123-def456-ghi789-jkl012-mno345     20Gi       RWO            standard       35s

# Check pod has stable network identity
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-postgres -o wide
# Output:
# NAME                    READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE   IP           NODE     NOMINATED NODE   READINESS GATES
# anihpj-postgres-sts-0   1/1     Running   0          1m    10.244.1.5   node-1              

# Test database connectivity
kubectl exec -it anihpj-postgres-sts-0 -- psql -U anihpj_user -d anihpj_db -c "SELECT version();"
# Output:
#                                                  version
# ----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------
#  PostgreSQL 15.4 on x86_64-pc-linux-gnu, compiled by gcc (GCC) 8.3.0, 64-bit
# (1 row)
Example 2: Django Application StatefulSet with Persistent Media Storage
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-django-sts
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-django
    component: web
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-django-service
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-django
      component: web
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-django
        component: web
    spec:
      initContainers:
      - name: migration-runner
        image: anihpj/django:v2.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate"]
        env:
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://anihpj_user:anihpj_password@anihpj-postgres-service:5432/anihpj_db"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: django-media
          mountPath: /app/media
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: anihpj/django:v2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: "postgresql://anihpj_user:anihpj_password@anihpj-postgres-service:5432/anihpj_db"
        - name: MEDIA_ROOT
          value: "/app/media"
        - name: STATIC_ROOT
          value: "/app/static"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: django-media
          mountPath: /app/media
        - name: django-static
          mountPath: /app/static
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "400m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /ready/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 5
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: django-media
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 10Gi
      storageClassName: standard
  - metadata:
      name: django-static
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 5Gi
      storageClassName: standard
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create Django StatefulSet with persistent storage
kubectl apply -f anihpj-django-sts.yaml
# Output: statefulset.apps/anihpj-django-sts created

# Watch ordered deployment of Django pods
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-django -w
# Output:
# NAME                 READY   STATUS     RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-django-sts-0  0/1     Init:0/1   0          10s
# anihpj-django-sts-0  0/1     PodInitializing   0     25s
# anihpj-django-sts-0  1/1     Running    0          30s
# anihpj-django-sts-1  0/1     Init:0/1   0          35s
# anihpj-django-sts-1  0/1     PodInitializing   0     50s
# anihpj-django-sts-1  1/1     Running    0          55s
# anihpj-django-sts-2  0/1     Init:0/1   0          60s

# Check StatefulSet status with ready replicas
kubectl get sts anihpj-django-sts
# Output:
# NAME                READY   AGE
# anihpj-django-sts   3/3     2m

# Verify each pod has its own persistent volumes
kubectl get pvc -l app=anihpj-django
# Output:
# NAME                             STATUS   VOLUME                                     CAPACITY   ACCESS MODES   STORAGECLASS   AGE
# django-media-anihpj-django-sts-0   Bound    pvc-111-222-333-444-555                   10Gi       RWO            standard       2m
# django-media-anihpj-django-sts-1   Bound    pvc-666-777-888-999-000                   10Gi       RWO            standard       2m
# django-media-anihpj-django-sts-2   Bound    pvc-aaa-bbb-ccc-ddd-eee                   10Gi       RWO            standard       1m
# django-static-anihpj-django-sts-0  Bound    pvc-fff-ggg-hhh-iii-jjj                   5Gi        RWO            standard       2m

# Test media upload to specific pod

# drwxrwxrwx 2 root root 4096 Sep  7 16:00 .

# Check stable pod identity and hostname

# Output: anihpj-django-sts-1
Example 3: Redis Cluster StatefulSet for Django Caching
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-redis-cluster-sts
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-redis
    component: cache
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-redis-service
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-redis
      component: cache
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-redis
        component: cache
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: redis
        image: redis:7-alpine
        ports:
        - containerPort: 6379
          name: redis
        command:
        - redis-server
        - /etc/redis/redis.conf
        env:
        - name: REDIS_CLUSTER_ANNOUNCE_IP
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: status.podIP
        volumeMounts:
        - name: redis-config
          mountPath: /etc/redis
        - name: redis-data
          mountPath: /data
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
        livenessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - redis-cli
            - ping
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - redis-cli
            - ping
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
      volumes:
      - name: redis-config
        configMap:
          name: redis-cluster-config
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: redis-data
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 2Gi
      storageClassName: fast-ssd
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create Redis configuration first
kubectl create configmap redis-cluster-config \
  --from-literal=redis.conf="maxmemory 256mb
maxmemory-policy allkeys-lru
save 900 1
save 300 10
save 60 10000"
# Output: configmap/redis-cluster-config created

# Create Redis cluster StatefulSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-redis-cluster-sts.yaml
# Output: statefulset.apps/anihpj-redis-cluster-sts created

# Monitor ordered Redis cluster creation
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-redis -w
# Output:
# NAME                         READY   STATUS              RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-0   0/1     ContainerCreating   0          10s
# anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-0   1/1     Running             0          20s
# anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-1   0/1     ContainerCreating   0          25s
# anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-1   1/1     Running             0          35s
# anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-2   0/1     ContainerCreating   0          40s

# Check StatefulSet and persistent storage
kubectl get sts anihpj-redis-cluster-sts
# Output:
# NAME                        READY   AGE
# anihpj-redis-cluster-sts    3/3     2m

kubectl get pvc -l app=anihpj-redis
# Output:
# NAME                                  STATUS   VOLUME                        CAPACITY   ACCESS MODES   STORAGECLASS   AGE
# redis-data-anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-0   Bound    pvc-redis-0-vol               2Gi        RWO            fast-ssd       2m
# redis-data-anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-1   Bound    pvc-redis-1-vol               2Gi        RWO            fast-ssd       2m
# redis-data-anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-2   Bound    pvc-redis-2-vol               2Gi        RWO            fast-ssd       1m

# Test Redis connectivity and cluster formation
kubectl exec -it anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-0 -- redis-cli ping
# Output: PONG

kubectl exec -it anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-0 -- redis-cli set test_key "Django cache test"
# Output: OK

kubectl exec -it anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-0 -- redis-cli get test_key
# Output: "Django cache test"

# Check Redis memory usage and configuration
kubectl exec -it anihpj-redis-cluster-sts-1 -- redis-cli info memory | grep used_memory_human
# Output: used_memory_human:1.23M
Example 4: StatefulSet with Ordered Rolling Updates
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-ordered-update-sts
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-ordered
    component: service
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-ordered-service
  replicas: 4
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      partition: 0
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-ordered
      component: service
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-ordered
        component: service
        version: v1.0
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-service
        image: anihpj/service:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: SERVICE_VERSION
          value: "v1.0"
        - name: POD_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        volumeMounts:
        - name: service-data
          mountPath: /app/data
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 5
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: service-data
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 1Gi
      storageClassName: standard
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create initial StatefulSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-ordered-update-sts.yaml
# Output: statefulset.apps/anihpj-ordered-update-sts created

# Wait for all pods to be ready
kubectl wait --for=condition=ready pod -l app=anihpj-ordered --timeout=300s
# Output: pod/anihpj-ordered-update-sts-0 condition met
#         pod/anihpj-ordered-update-sts-1 condition met
#         pod/anihpj-ordered-update-sts-2 condition met
#         pod/anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3 condition met

# Check initial pod versions
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-ordered -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}: {.spec.containers[0].image}{"\n"}{end}'
# Output:
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-0: anihpj/service:v1.0
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-1: anihpj/service:v1.0
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-2: anihpj/service:v1.0
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3: anihpj/service:v1.0

# Update to new version - this triggers ordered rolling update
kubectl patch sts anihpj-ordered-update-sts -p='{"spec":{"template":{"spec":{"containers":[{"name":"django-service","image":"anihpj/service:v2.0","env":[{"name":"SERVICE_VERSION","value":"v2.0"},{"name":"POD_NAME","valueFrom":{"fieldRef":{"fieldPath":"metadata.name"}}}]}]},"metadata":{"labels":{"version":"v2.0"}}}}}'
# Output: statefulset.apps/anihpj-ordered-update-sts patched

# Watch ordered rolling update (highest ordinal first)
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-ordered -w
# Output:
# NAME                           READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-0    1/1     Running   0          2m
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-1    1/1     Running   0          2m
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-2    1/1     Running   0          2m
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3    1/1     Running   0          2m
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3    1/1     Terminating   0      2m
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3    0/1     Terminating   0      2m
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3    0/1     Pending       0      0s
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3    1/1     Running       0      10s
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-2    1/1     Terminating   0      2m

# Check rolling update status
kubectl rollout status sts anihpj-ordered-update-sts
# Output: Waiting for 1 pods to be ready...
#         Waiting for partitioned roll out to finish: 2 out of 4 new pods have been updated...
#         partitioned roll out complete: 4 new pods have been updated...

# Verify updated versions (reverse order update)
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-ordered -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}: {.spec.containers[0].image}{"\n"}{end}'
# Output:
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-0: anihpj/service:v2.0
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-1: anihpj/service:v2.0
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-2: anihpj/service:v2.0
# anihpj-ordered-update-sts-3: anihpj/service:v2.0
Example 5: StatefulSet with Headless Service and DNS
apiVersion: v1
kind: Service
metadata:
  name: anihpj-headless-service
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-headless
spec:
  clusterIP: None  # Headless service
  selector:
    app: anihpj-headless
  ports:
  - port: 8000
    targetPort: 8000
    name: http
---
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-headless-sts
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-headless
    component: web-cluster
spec:
  serviceName: anihpj-headless-service
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-headless
      component: web-cluster
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-headless
        component: web-cluster
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-cluster
        image: anihpj/cluster:v1.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
          name: http
        env:
        - name: POD_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        - name: POD_NAMESPACE
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.namespace
        - name: CLUSTER_MEMBERS
          value: "anihpj-headless-sts-0.anihpj-headless-service.default.svc.cluster.local:8000,anihpj-headless-sts-1.anihpj-headless-service.default.svc.cluster.local:8000,anihpj-headless-sts-2.anihpj-headless-service.default.svc.cluster.local:8000"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: cluster-data
          mountPath: /app/cluster-data
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "150m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /cluster/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 15
          periodSeconds: 10
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /cluster/health/
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 20
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: cluster-data
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 3Gi
      storageClassName: standard
kubectl commands and results:
