Result: Creates a PostgreSQL cluster for Django JobPost application with persistent data storage.
Example 3: Ordered Django Workers
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: django-workers
spec:
  serviceName: worker-svc
  replicas: 4
  podManagementPolicy: OrderedReady
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-worker
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-worker
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: celery-worker
        image: django-jobpost:worker
        env:
        - name: WORKER_ID
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
Result: Creates ordered Django Celery workers (worker-0, worker-1, worker-2, worker-3) with stable identities.
Example 4: Django with Custom Update Strategy
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: django-rolling
spec:
  serviceName: django-svc
  replicas: 5
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      partition: 2
      maxUnavailable: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-api
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-api
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-api
        image: django-jobpost:v2.0
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
Result: Creates a StatefulSet with controlled rolling updates, updating only pods with ordinal >= 2.
Example 5: Django with Volume Claim Retention
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: django-persistent
spec:
  serviceName: django-svc
  replicas: 3
  persistentVolumeClaimRetentionPolicy:
    whenDeleted: Delete
    whenScaled: Retain
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-files
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-files
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: django-jobpost:latest
        volumeMounts:
        - name: user-uploads
          mountPath: /app/uploads
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: user-uploads
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 5Gi
Result: Creates a StatefulSet with custom PVC retention policy for Django user file uploads.

StatefulSetSpec

Docs: Kubernetes StatefulSetSpec Documentation

Specification of a StatefulSet defining service name, replicas, pod template, and update strategy.

Full description

📋 StatefulSetSpec Fields Overview

serviceName Service name governing network identity for pods
selector Label query matching pod template labels
template Pod template with Django container specifications
replicas Desired number of pods (typically 1-3 for databases)
updateStrategy Strategy for controlled rolling updates
podManagementPolicy OrderedReady (sequential) or Parallel pod creation
revisionHistoryLimit Number of old ReplicaSets retained for rollback
volumeClaimTemplates Persistent volume claim templates for storage
persistentVolumeClaimRetentionPolicy Policy for retaining PVCs on deletion/scaling

StatefulSetSpec defines the desired behavior of a StatefulSet for Django applications requiring persistent storage and stable network identities. It includes the service name for network identity, replica count, pod template with container specifications, and update strategies. For Django applications with databases or file storage, StatefulSetSpec ensures pods maintain consistent identities and persistent volumes across restarts and updates.

Parameters description

  • serviceName: Name of the service that governs this StatefulSet. This service must exist before the StatefulSet and provides network identity following the pattern: pod-name.serviceName.namespace.svc.cluster.local
  • selector: Label query over pods that should match the replica count. Must match the pod template's labels for proper pod management.
  • template: Pod template describing the pods that will be created. Each StatefulSet pod fulfills this template but has a unique identity and persistent storage.
  • replicas: Desired number of pod replicas. For Django applications with databases, typically 1-3 replicas. Defaults to 1 if unspecified.
  • updateStrategy: Strategy for updating pods when the template is revised. RollingUpdate ensures controlled updates maintaining data consistency.
  • podManagementPolicy: Controls how pods are created during scaling. OrderedReady (default) creates pods sequentially, Parallel creates them simultaneously.
  • revisionHistoryLimit: Number of old ReplicaSets to retain for rollback. For Django applications, typically 5-10 revisions for safe rollbacks.
  • volumeClaimTemplates: List of persistent volume claim templates. Each StatefulSet pod gets its own persistent volume for Django media files or database storage.
  • persistentVolumeClaimRetentionPolicy: Policy for retaining persistent volume claims when StatefulSet is deleted or scaled down.

StatefulSetStatus

Docs: Kubernetes StatefulSetStatus Documentation

Current state of a StatefulSet including replica counts, current revision, and update status.

Full description

📋 StatefulSetStatus Fields Overview

replicas Total number of non-terminating pods
readyReplicas Pods with Ready condition for traffic
currentReplicas Pods at current revision level
updatedReplicas Pods updated to latest template revision
currentRevision Revision of StatefulSet used to generate pods
updateRevision Latest revision for updating pods
observedGeneration Most recent generation observed by controller
collisionCount Number of hash collisions for StatefulSet
conditions Current service state and health conditions

StatefulSetStatus represents the current state of a StatefulSet providing real-time information about pod replicas, update progress, and revision history. For Django applications using StatefulSets, this status helps monitor deployment health, track rolling updates, and ensure all pods are running with persistent storage properly attached. Essential for monitoring database deployments or Django applications requiring persistent state.

Parameters description

  • replicas: Number of pods created by the StatefulSet controller. Shows the actual count of pods currently managed.
  • readyReplicas: Number of pods that have a Ready condition. Indicates how many pods are ready to serve traffic.
  • currentReplicas: Number of pods from the current revision of the StatefulSet template. Shows pods running the latest configuration.
  • updatedReplicas: Number of pods that have been updated to the current revision. Tracks rolling update progress.
  • currentRevision: Revision hash of the current StatefulSet template. Used to track configuration changes.
  • updateRevision: Revision hash of the template used for update operations. Differs from currentRevision during rolling updates.
  • observedGeneration: Most recent generation observed by the StatefulSet controller. Used to track if the controller has processed the latest changes.
  • conditions: Current service state conditions of the StatefulSet. Provides detailed status information about deployment health.
  • availableReplicas: Total number of available pods targeted by this StatefulSet. Indicates pods ready for at least minReadySeconds.
readyReplicas int32

readyReplicas is the number of pods created for this StatefulSet with a Ready Condition.

currentReplicas int32

currentReplicas is the number of Pods created by the StatefulSet controller from the StatefulSet version indicated by currentRevision.

updatedReplicas int32

updatedReplicas is the number of Pods created by the StatefulSet controller from the StatefulSet version indicated by updateRevision.

availableReplicas int32

Total number of available pods (ready for at least minReadySeconds) targeted by this statefulset.

collisionCount int32

collisionCount is the count of hash collisions for the StatefulSet. The StatefulSet controller uses this field as a collision avoidance mechanism when it needs to create the name for the newest ControllerRevision.

conditions []StatefulSetCondition

Represents the latest available observations of a statefulset's current state.

currentRevision string

currentRevision, if not empty, indicates the version of the StatefulSet used to generate Pods in the sequence [0,currentReplicas).

StatefulSetList

Docs: Kubernetes StatefulSetList Documentation

Collection of StatefulSets with metadata for listing and pagination support.

Full description

📋 StatefulSetList Components Overview

apiVersion API version (apps/v1) for StatefulSet collections
kind Resource type identifier (StatefulSetList)
metadata Collection metadata with resource version and pagination
items Array of StatefulSet objects matching query criteria

StatefulSetList is a collection of StatefulSets used when listing multiple StatefulSet resources. This is returned by kubectl get statefulsets or API calls that retrieve multiple StatefulSets. For Django applications, you might have multiple StatefulSets for different services like databases, file storage, or cache layers. The list includes metadata for pagination and filtering capabilities.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSetList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: string
  continue: string
items:
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: StatefulSet
  metadata:
    name: string
  spec:
    replicas: int32
    serviceName: string

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for StatefulSetList resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version for this list resource.
  • kind: Must be "StatefulSetList" to indicate this is a collection of StatefulSet resources.
  • metadata: Standard list metadata including resource version for consistency and continuation token for pagination.
  • items: Array of StatefulSet objects. Contains the actual StatefulSet resources that match the list query.

Standard list's metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#metadata

items []StatefulSet, required

Items is the list of stateful sets.

Operations

Docs: Kubernetes StatefulSet Operations

HTTP API operations for managing StatefulSet resources with persistent storage and stable network identities.

Full description

StatefulSet operations provide HTTP API endpoints for managing StatefulSet resources in Kubernetes. These operations enable programmatic control over Django applications requiring persistent storage, stable network identities, and ordered deployment. Essential for managing database deployments, file storage services, and stateful Django applications with data persistence requirements.

Get Read the Specified StatefulSet

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets/{name}
Parameters
  • name - string, required (path) - Name of the StatefulSet
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • pretty - string (query) - If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
Response

200 (StatefulSet): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Get StatefulSet Details
curl -X GET \
  $KUBE_API_SERVER/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/statefulsets/django-stateful \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN"
Result: Returns detailed information about the django-stateful StatefulSet including pod status and persistent volume claims.
Example 2: Get StatefulSet with kubectl
kubectl get statefulset django-stateful -o yaml
Result: Returns the complete StatefulSet manifest in YAML format showing all current settings and status.

Get Read Status of the Specified StatefulSet

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets/{name}/status
Response

200 (StatefulSet): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example: Check StatefulSet Status
kubectl get statefulset django-stateful -o jsonpath='{.status}'
Result: Returns status information showing current, ready, and updated replica counts for the Django StatefulSet.

List or Watch Objects of Kind StatefulSet

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • labelSelector - string (query) - A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
  • fieldSelector - string (query) - A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
  • watch - boolean (query) - Watch for changes to the described resources and return them as a stream
Response

200 (StatefulSetList): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: List All StatefulSets
kubectl get statefulsets
Result: Lists all StatefulSets in the current namespace with basic information like ready/desired replicas and age.
Example 2: List StatefulSets with Labels
kubectl get statefulsets -l app=django-jobpost
Result: Lists only StatefulSets that have the label app=django-jobpost, filtering for Django JobPost application StatefulSets.

List or Watch Objects of Kind StatefulSet

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/statefulsets
Examples
Example: List StatefulSets Across All Namespaces
kubectl get statefulsets --all-namespaces
Result: Lists all StatefulSets across all namespaces in the cluster, useful for cluster-wide Django application monitoring.

Create a StatefulSet

POST
HTTP Request
POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/statefulsets
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • body - StatefulSet, required - StatefulSet manifest to create
  • dryRun - string (query) - When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
Response

200 (StatefulSet): OK

201 (StatefulSet): Created

202 (StatefulSet): Accepted

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Create Django StatefulSet
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: StatefulSet
metadata:
  name: django-files
spec:
  serviceName: django-svc
  replicas: 3
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-files
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-files
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: django-app
        image: django-jobpost:latest
        volumeMounts:
        - name: user-data
          mountPath: /app/data
  volumeClaimTemplates:
  - metadata:
      name: user-data
    spec:
      accessModes: ["ReadWriteOnce"]
      resources:
        requests:
          storage: 5Gi
EOF
kubectl output:

ControllerRevision

Docs: Kubernetes ControllerRevision v1

ControllerRevision implements an immutable snapshot of state data.

📋 ControllerRevision Components Overview

ControllerRevision implements an immutable snapshot of state data. Clients are responsible for serializing and deserializing the objects that contain their internal state. Once a ControllerRevision has been successfully created, it can not be updated. The API Server will fail validation of all requests that attempt to mutate the Data field.

ControllerRevisions may, however, be deleted. Note that, due to its use by both the DaemonSet and StatefulSet controllers for update and rollback, this object is beta. However, it may be subject to name and representation changes in future releases, and clients should not depend on its stability. It is primarily for internal use by controllers.

For Django applications, ControllerRevisions are essential for tracking the revision history of StatefulSets and DaemonSets. This enables rollback capabilities when deploying Django applications that require ordered updates or specific deployment strategies. Understanding ControllerRevisions helps Django developers manage application deployments, track changes, and implement reliable rollback mechanisms.

💡 Note: ControllerRevisions are automatically managed by Kubernetes controllers and are primarily used internally. Django developers typically interact with them indirectly through StatefulSet and DaemonSet operations, especially during rollbacks and update management.

🔧 Core Components

ControllerRevision Object Immutable state snapshots with revision numbers and data
ControllerRevisionList Collection management for multiple revision snapshots

🔧 ControllerRevision Operations Overview

📋 Operation Categories

Create Operations Create new revision snapshots with POST requests
Read Operations Query revision information with GET requests
Delete Operations Remove old revision snapshots with DELETE requests
Rollback Operations Restore previous configurations from revisions
All Detailed Overviews Jump to complete component specifications

ControllerRevision

Docs: Kubernetes ControllerRevision v1 API

Immutable snapshot of state data used for rollback operations in StatefulSets and DaemonSets.

Full description

📋 ControllerRevision Fields Overview

apiVersion API version (apps/v1) for ControllerRevision
kind Resource type identifier (ControllerRevision)
metadata Standard metadata with name, namespace, and labels
revision Revision number indicating the sequence of this snapshot
data Serialized representation of the object's state

ControllerRevision implements an immutable snapshot of state data used for rollback operations. It stores the complete configuration of StatefulSets and DaemonSets at specific points in time. For Django applications using StatefulSets or DaemonSets, ControllerRevisions enable you to rollback to previous configurations when deployments fail. This is crucial when updates to your Django application (like changes to JobPost models or database schemas) need to be reverted quickly to maintain application stability.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: string
  namespace: string
  labels:
    key: value
revision: int64
data:
  # Serialized representation of the state
  # Contains the complete spec of the controlled resource

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for ControllerRevision resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version to use for this resource.
  • kind: Must be "ControllerRevision" to indicate this is a ControllerRevision resource definition.
  • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. Used for organizing and identifying specific revisions.
  • revision: Revision number indicating the sequence of this state snapshot. This number increments with each update to the controlled resource.
  • data: Serialized representation of the complete state at this revision. Contains the full specification of the controlled Django resource for rollback purposes.

Return value

ControllerRevision object: Returns the created ControllerRevision resource with system-assigned fields including creation timestamp and the immutable state snapshot. Used by controllers to track configuration history and enable rollback operations for Django deployments.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: StatefulSet ControllerRevision
kubectl get controllerrevisions -l app=django-jobpost
Result: Lists all controller revisions for Django JobPost StatefulSets, showing revision history and numbers.
Example 2: View Revision Details
kubectl get controllerrevision django-stateful-78945612 -o yaml
Result: Shows detailed information about a specific revision of the Django StatefulSet, including the complete spec snapshot.
Example 3: Check Revision History
kubectl describe statefulset django-jobpost | grep -A 5 "Update Strategy"
Result: Displays StatefulSet update strategy and current revision information for Django application deployment.
Example 4: List Revisions by Owner
kubectl get controllerrevisions --field-selector metadata.ownerReferences.name=django-workers
Result: Lists all controller revisions owned by the django-workers StatefulSet, showing the complete revision timeline.
Example 5: Compare Revisions
kubectl get controllerrevision django-stateful-12345678 -o jsonpath='{.revision}'
Result: Returns the revision number (e.g., "3") for the specific ControllerRevision of the Django StatefulSet.

ControllerRevisionList

Docs: Kubernetes ControllerRevisionList Documentation

Collection of ControllerRevision objects with metadata for listing and pagination support.

Full description

ControllerRevisionList is a collection of ControllerRevision objects used when listing multiple revision snapshots. This is returned by kubectl get controllerrevisions or API calls that retrieve multiple revisions. For Django applications using StatefulSets or DaemonSets, this helps track the complete revision history for rollback operations and configuration management.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevisionList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: string
  continue: string
items:
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: ControllerRevision
  metadata:
    name: string
  revision: int64
  data: {}

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for ControllerRevisionList resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version for this list resource.
  • kind: Must be "ControllerRevisionList" to indicate this is a collection of ControllerRevision resources.
  • metadata: Standard list metadata including resource version for consistency and continuation token for pagination.
  • items: Array of ControllerRevision objects. Contains the actual revision snapshots that match the list query.
items []ControllerRevision, required

Items is the list of ControllerRevisions. Each item represents an immutable snapshot of a controlled resource's state.

Operations

Docs: Kubernetes ControllerRevision Operations

HTTP API operations for managing ControllerRevision resources for rollback and revision tracking.

Full description

ControllerRevision operations provide HTTP API endpoints for managing ControllerRevision resources in Kubernetes. These operations enable programmatic access to revision history for StatefulSets and DaemonSets, allowing automated rollback procedures, configuration auditing, and deployment tracking for Django applications requiring state management and rollback capabilities.

Get Read the Specified ControllerRevision

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}
Parameters
  • name - string, required (path) - Name of the ControllerRevision
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • pretty - string (query) - If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
Response

200 (ControllerRevision): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Get Specific Revision
curl -X GET \
  $KUBE_API_SERVER/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/controllerrevisions/django-stateful-12345678 \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN"
Result: Returns detailed information about revision 12345678 of the Django StatefulSet, including the complete state snapshot.
Example 2: Get Revision with kubectl
kubectl get controllerrevision django-workers-87654321 -o yaml
Result: Returns the complete ControllerRevision manifest in YAML format showing the Django workers StatefulSet state.

List or Watch Objects of Kind ControllerRevision

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • labelSelector - string (query) - A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
  • fieldSelector - string (query) - A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
  • watch - boolean (query) - Watch for changes to the described resources and return them as a stream
Response

200 (ControllerRevisionList): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: List All Revisions
kubectl get controllerrevisions
Result: Lists all ControllerRevisions in the current namespace with revision numbers and ages.
Example 2: List Revisions with Labels
kubectl get controllerrevisions -l app=django-jobpost
Result: Lists only ControllerRevisions for Django JobPost application, showing the revision history timeline.

List or Watch Objects of Kind ControllerRevision

GET
HTTP Request
GET /apis/apps/v1/controllerrevisions
Examples
Example: List Revisions Across All Namespaces
kubectl get controllerrevisions --all-namespaces
Result: Lists all ControllerRevisions across all namespaces in the cluster, useful for Django application revision tracking.

Create a ControllerRevision

POST
HTTP Request
POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions
Parameters
  • namespace - string, required (path) - Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
  • body - ControllerRevision, required - ControllerRevision manifest to create
  • dryRun - string (query) - When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
Response

200 (ControllerRevision): OK

201 (ControllerRevision): Created

202 (ControllerRevision): Accepted

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example: Create Manual Revision (Advanced)
# Note: ControllerRevisions are typically managed automatically
kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: ControllerRevision
metadata:
  name: manual-django-revision
  labels:
    app: django-jobpost
revision: 1
data:
  # Serialized state data would go here
EOF
Result: Creates a manual ControllerRevision (advanced use case, typically managed automatically by controllers).

Update Replace the Specified ControllerRevision

PUT
HTTP Request
PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}
Response

200 (ControllerRevision): OK

201 (ControllerRevision): Created

401: Unauthorized

⚠️ Important: ControllerRevisions are immutable once created. The API Server will fail validation of requests that attempt to mutate the Data field.

Patch Partially Update the Specified ControllerRevision

PATCH
HTTP Request
PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}
Parameters
  • body - Patch, required - Patch to apply to the ControllerRevision (limited to metadata only)
Response

200 (ControllerRevision): OK

201 (ControllerRevision): Created

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example: Add Labels to Revision
kubectl patch controllerrevision django-stateful-12345678 -p '{"metadata":{"labels":{"environment":"production"}}}'
Result: Adds a production environment label to the ControllerRevision metadata (data field remains immutable).

Delete a ControllerRevision

DELETE
HTTP Request
DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions/{name}
Parameters
  • gracePeriodSeconds - integer (query) - The duration in seconds before the object should be deleted
  • propagationPolicy - string (query) - Whether and how garbage collection will be performed
Response

200 (Status): OK

202 (Status): Accepted

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example 1: Delete Specific Revision
kubectl delete controllerrevision django-stateful-12345678
Result: Deletes the specific ControllerRevision, removing this snapshot from the Django StatefulSet revision history.
Example 2: Delete Old Revisions
kubectl delete controllerrevision django-workers-11111111 --grace-period=0
Result: Immediately deletes an old ControllerRevision from the Django workers StatefulSet history.

Delete Collection of ControllerRevision

DELETE
HTTP Request
DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/controllerrevisions
Parameters
  • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector to filter which ControllerRevisions to delete
  • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector to filter which ControllerRevisions to delete
Response

200 (Status): OK

401: Unauthorized

Examples
Example: Delete Old Revisions by Label
kubectl delete controllerrevisions -l app=django-jobpost,version=old
Result: Deletes all old ControllerRevisions for Django JobPost application, cleaning up revision history.

DaemonSet

Docs: Kubernetes DaemonSet v1

DaemonSet represents the configuration of a daemon set.

📋 DaemonSet Components Overview

DaemonSet represents the configuration of a daemon set. A DaemonSet ensures that all (or some) Nodes run a copy of a Pod. As nodes are added to the cluster, Pods are added to them. As nodes are removed from the cluster, those Pods are garbage collected. Deleting a DaemonSet will clean up the Pods it created.

Some typical uses of a DaemonSet are:

  • Running a cluster storage daemon on every node
  • Running a logs collection daemon on every node
  • Running a node monitoring daemon on every node

For Django applications, DaemonSets are essential for infrastructure-level services that need to run on every node in your cluster. This includes monitoring agents, log collectors, network plugins, and security scanners that support your Django application infrastructure. Unlike Deployments that manage a specific number of replicas, DaemonSets ensure one pod per node, making them perfect for node-level services.

💡 Note: DaemonSets are valuable for Django applications when you need to run infrastructure services on every node, such as monitoring Django application metrics, collecting logs from all Django pods, or running security agents across your cluster nodes.

🔧 Core Components

DaemonSetSpec Configuration for node selectors, pod templates, and update strategies
DaemonSetStatus Current state with node counts, ready pods, and update progress
DaemonSetList Collection management for multiple DaemonSet resources

🔧 DaemonSet Operations Overview

📋 Operation Categories

Create Operations Deploy new DaemonSets with POST requests
Read Operations Query DaemonSet information with GET requests
Update Operations Modify DaemonSet configurations with PUT/PATCH
Delete Operations Remove DaemonSets with DELETE requests
Status Operations Monitor DaemonSet node coverage and pod status
All Detailed Overviews Jump to complete component specifications

DaemonSet

Docs: Kubernetes DaemonSet v1 API

Ensures that all (or some) Nodes run a copy of a Pod, perfect for node-level Django services like logging or monitoring.

Full description

DaemonSet ensures that all (or some) Nodes run a copy of a Pod. As nodes are added to the cluster, Pods are added to them. As nodes are removed, those Pods are garbage collected. For Django applications, DaemonSets are ideal for deploying node-level services like log collectors, monitoring agents, or cache proxies that support your main Django application. Every node running your JobPost, Author, Location, or Skills services can have a DaemonSet pod providing essential infrastructure support.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: string
  namespace: string
  labels:
    key: value
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      key: value
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        key: value
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: string
        image: string
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 0
status:
  numberReady: int32
  desiredNumberScheduled: int32
  currentNumberScheduled: int32

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for DaemonSet resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version to use for this resource.
  • kind: Must be "DaemonSet" to indicate this is a DaemonSet resource definition.
  • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. Used for organizing and managing DaemonSet deployments.
  • spec: Specification of the desired behavior of the DaemonSet. Defines the pod template and update strategy for node-level services.
  • spec.selector: Label selector for pods managed by this DaemonSet. Must match template labels for proper pod management.
  • spec.template: Pod template that describes the pods that will be created on each node. Contains the container specification for Django support services.
  • spec.updateStrategy: Strategy used to update DaemonSet pods. RollingUpdate ensures controlled updates across all nodes.
  • status: Most recently observed status of the DaemonSet. Populated by the system and provides information about pod distribution across nodes.

Return value

DaemonSet object: Returns the created DaemonSet resource with system-assigned fields including creation timestamp, generation number, and status. The status will show the number of scheduled, ready, and available pods across all nodes in the cluster.

5 short examples with Django models

Example 1: Django Log Collection DaemonSet
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-log-collector-ds
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-log-collector
    component: logging
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-log-collector
      component: logging
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-log-collector
        component: logging
    spec:
      serviceAccountName: log-collector
      containers:
      - name: fluentd
        image: fluent/fluentd:v1.16
        ports:
        - containerPort: 24224
          name: forwarder
        env:
        - name: FLUENTD_CONF
          value: "fluent.conf"
        - name: NODE_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: spec.nodeName
        volumeMounts:
        - name: django-logs
          mountPath: /var/log/django
          readOnly: true
        - name: fluentd-config
          mountPath: /fluentd/etc
        - name: container-logs
          mountPath: /var/log/containers
          readOnly: true
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
      volumes:
      - name: django-logs
        hostPath:
          path: /var/log/django
          type: DirectoryOrCreate
      - name: container-logs
        hostPath:
          path: /var/log/containers
          type: Directory
      - name: fluentd-config
        configMap:
          name: fluentd-config
      tolerations:
      - key: node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane
        operator: Exists
        effect: NoSchedule
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create ServiceAccount and ConfigMap first
kubectl create serviceaccount log-collector
# Output: serviceaccount/log-collector created

kubectl create configmap fluentd-config \
  --from-literal=fluent.conf="
  @type tail
  path /var/log/django/*.log
  pos_file /var/log/fluentd-django.log.pos
  tag django.*
  
    @type json
  


  @type stdout
"
# Output: configmap/fluentd-config created

# Create the DaemonSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-log-collector-ds.yaml
# Output: daemonset.apps/anihpj-log-collector-ds created

# Check DaemonSet status across all nodes
kubectl get ds anihpj-log-collector-ds
# Output:
# NAME                       DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   UP-TO-DATE   AVAILABLE   NODE SELECTOR   AGE
# anihpj-log-collector-ds    3         3         3       3            3                     45s

# Verify pods are running on all nodes
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-log-collector -o wide
# Output:
# NAME                             READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE   IP           NODE     NOMINATED NODE   READINESS GATES
# anihpj-log-collector-ds-abc12    1/1     Running   0          50s   10.244.1.5   node-1              
# anihpj-log-collector-ds-def34    1/1     Running   0          50s   10.244.2.8   node-2              
# anihpj-log-collector-ds-ghi56    1/1     Running   0          50s   10.244.3.3   node-3              

# Check logs are being collected
kubectl logs anihpj-log-collector-ds-abc12 | head -5
# Output:
# 2025-09-07 16:15:00 +0000 [info]: #0 starting fluentd worker pid=7 ppid=1 worker=0
# 2025-09-07 16:15:01 +0000 [info]: #0 [django.app] following tail of /var/log/django/django.log
# 2025-09-07 16:15:02 +0000 django.app: {"level":"INFO","message":"JobPost model accessed","timestamp":"2025-09-07T16:15:02"}

# Verify DaemonSet handles node additions
kubectl get nodes
# Output:
# NAME     STATUS   ROLES           AGE   VERSION
# node-1   Ready    control-plane   1d    v1.28.0
# node-2   Ready              1d    v1.28.0
# node-3   Ready              1d    v1.28.0
Example 2: Node Monitoring DaemonSet for Django Infrastructure
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-node-monitor-ds
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-node-monitor
    component: monitoring
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-node-monitor
      component: monitoring
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-node-monitor
        component: monitoring
    spec:
      hostNetwork: true
      hostPID: true
      containers:
      - name: node-exporter
        image: prom/node-exporter:v1.6.1
        args:
        - --path.sysfs=/host/sys
        - --path.rootfs=/host/root
        - --no-collector.wifi
        - --no-collector.hwmon
        - --collector.filesystem.mount-points-exclude=^/(dev|proc|sys|var/lib/docker/.+|var/lib/kubelet/.+)($|/)
        - --collector.netclass.ignored-devices=^(veth.*)$
        ports:
        - containerPort: 9100
          hostPort: 9100
          name: metrics
        env:
        - name: NODE_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: spec.nodeName
        volumeMounts:
        - name: sys
          mountPath: /host/sys
          readOnly: true
        - name: root
          mountPath: /host/root
          readOnly: true
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "64Mi"
            cpu: "50m"
          limits:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
        securityContext:
          runAsNonRoot: true
          runAsUser: 65534
      volumes:
      - name: sys
        hostPath:
          path: /sys
          type: Directory
      - name: root
        hostPath:
          path: /
          type: Directory
      tolerations:
      - operator: Exists
        effect: NoSchedule
kubectl commands and results:

# Output:

# Verify pods on each node with hostNetwork

Example 3: Django Security Scanning DaemonSet
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-security-scan-ds
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-security
    component: security-scanner
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-security
      component: security-scanner
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-security
        component: security-scanner
    spec:
      serviceAccountName: security-scanner
      containers:
      - name: falco
        image: falcosecurity/falco:0.36.2
        args:
        - /usr/bin/falco
        - --cri=/run/containerd/containerd.sock
        - --k8s-api=https://kubernetes.default:443
        - --k8s-api-cert=/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/ca.crt
        - --k8s-api-token=/var/run/secrets/kubernetes.io/serviceaccount/token
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8765
          name: grpc
        env:
        - name: FALCO_GRPC_BIND_ADDRESS
          value: "0.0.0.0:8765"
        - name: FALCO_GRPC_ENABLED
          value: "true"
        securityContext:
          privileged: true
        volumeMounts:
        - name: docker-socket
          mountPath: /var/run/docker.sock
          readOnly: true
        - name: containerd-socket
          mountPath: /run/containerd/containerd.sock
          readOnly: true
        - name: dev-fs
          mountPath: /dev
          readOnly: true
        - name: proc-fs
          mountPath: /host/proc
          readOnly: true
        - name: boot-fs
          mountPath: /host/boot
          readOnly: true
        - name: lib-modules
          mountPath: /host/lib/modules
          readOnly: true
        - name: usr-fs
          mountPath: /host/usr
          readOnly: true
        - name: etc-fs
          mountPath: /host/etc
          readOnly: true
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "400m"
      volumes:
      - name: docker-socket
        hostPath:
          path: /var/run/docker.sock
          type: Socket
      - name: containerd-socket
        hostPath:
          path: /run/containerd/containerd.sock
          type: Socket
      - name: dev-fs
        hostPath:
          path: /dev
          type: Directory
      - name: proc-fs
        hostPath:
          path: /proc
          type: Directory
      - name: boot-fs
        hostPath:
          path: /boot
          type: Directory
      - name: lib-modules
        hostPath:
          path: /lib/modules
          type: Directory
      - name: usr-fs
        hostPath:
          path: /usr
          type: Directory
      - name: etc-fs
        hostPath:
          path: /etc
          type: Directory
      tolerations:
      - operator: Exists
        effect: NoSchedule

# Mon Sep  7 16:20:01 2025: Loading rules from /etc/falco/falco_rules.yaml
# Mon Sep  7 16:20:02 2025: Starting internal webserver, listening on port 8765
# Mon Sep  7 16:20:03 2025: Syscall event drop monitoring: disabled
# Mon Sep  7 16:20:04 2025: Loading driver: bpf

# Test security event detection
kubectl run test-pod --image=alpine --rm -it --restart=Never -- sh -c "cat /etc/passwd"
# Check logs for security alerts
kubectl logs anihpj-security-scan-ds-abc12 --tail=5
# Output:

# Output: Shows security-related events detected by Falco across all nodes
Example 4: Django Network Proxy DaemonSet
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-proxy-ds
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-proxy
    component: network
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-proxy
      component: network
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 1
      maxSurge: 0
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-proxy
        component: network
    spec:
      hostNetwork: true
      dnsPolicy: ClusterFirstWithHostNet
      containers:
      - name: nginx-proxy
        image: nginx:1.25-alpine
        ports:
        - containerPort: 80
          hostPort: 80
          name: http
        - containerPort: 443
          hostPort: 443
          name: https
        env:
        - name: NODE_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: spec.nodeName
        volumeMounts:
        - name: nginx-config
          mountPath: /etc/nginx/conf.d
        - name: ssl-certs
          mountPath: /etc/ssl/certs
          readOnly: true
        - name: cache-volume
          mountPath: /var/cache/nginx
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health
            port: 80
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 10
        readinessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health
            port: 80
          initialDelaySeconds: 5
          periodSeconds: 5
      volumes:
      - name: nginx-config
        configMap:
          name: nginx-proxy-config
      - name: ssl-certs
        secret:
          secretName: anihpj-ssl-certs
      - name: cache-volume
        hostPath:
          path: /var/cache/nginx
          type: DirectoryOrCreate
      nodeSelector:
        node-role.kubernetes.io/worker: ""
      tolerations:
      - key: node-role.kubernetes.io/control-plane
        operator: Exists
        effect: NoSchedule
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create nginx configuration for Django proxy
kubectl create configmap nginx-proxy-config \
  --from-literal=default.conf="upstream django_backend {
    server anihpj-django-service:8000;
}

server {
    listen 80;
    server_name _;
    
    location /health {
        access_log off;
        return 200 'healthy\n';
        add_header Content-Type text/plain;
    }
    
    location / {
        proxy_pass http://django_backend;
        proxy_set_header Host \$host;
        proxy_set_header X-Real-IP \$remote_addr;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-For \$proxy_add_x_forwarded_for;
        proxy_set_header X-Forwarded-Proto \$scheme;
    }
}"
# Output: configmap/nginx-proxy-config created

  --cert=./server.crt \

Example 5: Django Metrics Collection DaemonSet with Custom Update Strategy
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: anihpj-metrics-ds
  namespace: default
  labels:
    app: anihpj-metrics
    component: metrics-collector
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: anihpj-metrics
      component: metrics-collector
  updateStrategy:
    type: RollingUpdate
    rollingUpdate:
      maxUnavailable: 25%
      maxSurge: 0
  revisionHistoryLimit: 3
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj-metrics
        component: metrics-collector
      annotations:
        prometheus.io/scrape: "true"
        prometheus.io/port: "9102"
        prometheus.io/path: "/metrics"
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: telegraf
        image: telegraf:1.28-alpine
        ports:
        - containerPort: 9102
          name: metrics
        env:
        - name: NODE_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: spec.nodeName
        - name: NODE_IP
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: status.hostIP
        - name: DJANGO_METRICS_URL
          value: "http://anihpj-django-service:8000/metrics/"
        - name: HOSTNAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: spec.nodeName
        volumeMounts:
        - name: telegraf-config
          mountPath: /etc/telegraf
        - name: proc
          mountPath: /host/proc
          readOnly: true
        - name: sys
          mountPath: /host/sys
          readOnly: true
        - name: docker-socket
          mountPath: /var/run/docker.sock
          readOnly: true
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "64Mi"
            cpu: "50m"
          limits:
            memory: "128Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
        securityContext:
          runAsUser: 0
          privileged: true
      volumes:
      - name: telegraf-config
        configMap:
          name: telegraf-config
      - name: proc
        hostPath:
          path: /proc
          type: Directory
      - name: sys
        hostPath:
          path: /sys
          type: Directory
      - name: docker-socket
        hostPath:
          path: /var/run/docker.sock
          type: Socket
      tolerations:
      - operator: Exists
        effect: NoSchedule
      - operator: Exists
        effect: NoExecute
kubectl commands and results: 
# Create Telegraf configuration for Django metrics
kubectl create configmap telegraf-config \
  --from-literal=telegraf.conf="[global_tags]
  node = \"\$NODE_NAME\"
  
[[outputs.prometheus_client]]
  listen = \":9102\"
  metric_version = 2

[[inputs.cpu]]
  percpu = true
  totalcpu = true
  collect_cpu_time = false
  report_active = false

[[inputs.disk]]
  ignore_fs = [\"tmpfs\", \"devtmpfs\", \"devfs\", \"iso9660\", \"overlay\", \"aufs\", \"squashfs\"]

[[inputs.mem]]

[[inputs.net]]

[[inputs.system]]

[[inputs.docker]]
  endpoint = \"unix:///var/run/docker.sock\"

[[inputs.http]]
  urls = [\"\$DJANGO_METRICS_URL\"]
  data_format = \"json\"
  name_override = \"django_app\"
  interval = \"30s\"
  [inputs.http.tags]
    source = \"django\""
# Output: configmap/telegraf-config created

# Deploy metrics collection DaemonSet
kubectl apply -f anihpj-metrics-ds.yaml
# Output: daemonset.apps/anihpj-metrics-ds created

# Check DaemonSet deployment with update strategy
kubectl get ds anihpj-metrics-ds
# Output:
# NAME                DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   UP-TO-DATE   AVAILABLE   NODE SELECTOR   AGE
# anihpj-metrics-ds   3         3         3       3            3                     60s

# Verify metrics collection on all nodes
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-metrics -o wide
# Output:
# NAME                      READY   STATUS    RESTARTS   AGE   IP           NODE     NOMINATED NODE   READINESS GATES
# anihpj-metrics-ds-abc12   1/1     Running   0          65s   10.244.1.9   node-1              
# anihpj-metrics-ds-def34   1/1     Running   0          65s   10.244.2.10  node-2              
# anihpj-metrics-ds-ghi56   1/1     Running   0          65s   10.244.3.8   node-3              

# Test metrics endpoint from each node
kubectl exec -it anihpj-metrics-ds-abc12 -- wget -qO- http://localhost:9102/metrics | grep telegraf_agent
# Output:
# telegraf_agent_gather_errors_total{host="node-1"} 0
# telegraf_agent_metrics_dropped_total{host="node-1"} 0
# telegraf_agent_metrics_gathered_total{host="node-1"} 156

# Check Django app metrics collection
kubectl exec -it anihpj-metrics-ds-def34 -- wget -qO- http://localhost:9102/metrics | grep django_app
# Output:
# django_app_requests_total{host="node-2",method="GET",source="django"} 42
# django_app_response_time_seconds{host="node-2",source="django"} 0.125

# Test rolling update with 25% maxUnavailable
kubectl patch ds anihpj-metrics-ds -p='{"spec":{"template":{"metadata":{"annotations":{"restart":"$(date)"}}}}}'
# Output: daemonset.apps/anihpj-metrics-ds patched

# Monitor rolling update progress
kubectl rollout status ds anihpj-metrics-ds --timeout=180s
# Output: Waiting for daemon set "anihpj-metrics-ds" rollout to finish: 2 out of 3 new pods have been updated...
#         daemon set "anihpj-metrics-ds" successfully rolled out

# Check revision history
kubectl rollout history ds anihpj-metrics-ds
# Output:
# daemonset.apps/anihpj-metrics-ds 
# REVISION  CHANGE-CAUSE
# 1         
# 2         

# Verify all pods are collecting metrics across nodes
for pod in $(kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj-metrics -o name); do
  echo "Checking $pod:"
  kubectl exec $pod -- sh -c "wget -qO- http://localhost:9102/metrics | grep -c 'cpu_usage_idle'"
done
# Output:

# 4
# Checking pod/anihpj-metrics-ds-def34:
# 4
# Checking pod/anihpj-metrics-ds-ghi56:
# 4

DaemonSetSpec

Docs: Kubernetes DaemonSetSpec Documentation

Specification of a DaemonSet defining pod template, update strategy, and node selection criteria.

Full description

DaemonSetSpec defines the desired behavior of a DaemonSet for Django applications requiring node-level services. It includes the pod template for containers that run on each node, update strategy for rolling updates, and selector for determining which nodes should run the pods. Essential for deploying Django infrastructure services like log collectors, monitoring agents, or node-level caches.

Parameters description

  • selector (LabelSelector, required): A label query over pods that are managed by the daemon set. Must match in order to be controlled. It must match the pod template's labels. More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/overview/working-with-objects/labels/#label-selectors
  • template (PodTemplateSpec, required): An object that describes the pod that will be created. The DaemonSet will create exactly one copy of this pod on every node that matches the template's node selector (or on every node if no node selector is specified). The only allowed template.spec.restartPolicy value is "Always".
  • minReadySeconds (int32): The minimum number of seconds for which a newly created DaemonSet pod should be ready without any of its container crashing, for it to be considered available. Defaults to 0 (pod will be considered available as soon as it is ready).
  • updateStrategy (DaemonSetUpdateStrategy): An update strategy to replace existing DaemonSet pods with new pods.
  • updateStrategy.type (string): Type of daemon set update. Can be "RollingUpdate" or "OnDelete". Default is RollingUpdate.
  • updateStrategy.rollingUpdate (RollingUpdateDaemonSet): Rolling update config params. Present only if type = "RollingUpdate". Spec to control the desired behavior of daemon set rolling update.
  • updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxSurge (IntOrString): The maximum number of nodes with an existing available DaemonSet pod that can have an updated DaemonSet pod during an update. Value can be an absolute number (ex: 5) or a percentage of desired pods (ex: 10%). This cannot be 0 if MaxUnavailable is 0. Absolute number is calculated from percentage by rounding up to a minimum of 1. Default value is 0.
  • updateStrategy.rollingUpdate.maxUnavailable (IntOrString): The maximum number of DaemonSet pods that can be unavailable during the update. Value can be an absolute number (ex: 5) or a percentage of total number of DaemonSet pods at the start of the update (ex: 10%). Absolute number is calculated from percentage by rounding up. This cannot be 0 if MaxSurge is 0. Default value is 1.
  • revisionHistoryLimit (int32): The number of old history to retain to allow rollback. This is a pointer to distinguish between explicit zero and not specified. Defaults to 10.

DaemonSetStatus

Docs: Kubernetes DaemonSetStatus Documentation

Current status of a DaemonSet including node counts, scheduling information, and update progress.

Full description

DaemonSetStatus represents the current state of a DaemonSet providing real-time information about pod distribution across nodes, scheduling status, and update progress. For Django applications using DaemonSets for infrastructure services, this status helps monitor deployment health, track rolling updates across all nodes, and ensure essential services are running on every required node.

Parameters description

  • numberReady (int32, required): numberReady is the number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod and have one or more of the daemon pod running with a Ready Condition.
  • numberAvailable (int32): The number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod and have one or more of the daemon pod running and available (ready for at least spec.minReadySeconds).
  • numberUnavailable (int32): The number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod and have none of the daemon pod running and available (ready for at least spec.minReadySeconds).
  • numberMisscheduled (int32, required): The number of nodes that are running the daemon pod, but are not supposed to run the daemon pod. More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/daemonset/
  • desiredNumberScheduled (int32, required): The total number of nodes that should be running the daemon pod (including nodes correctly running the daemon pod). More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/daemonset/
  • currentNumberScheduled (int32, required): The number of nodes that are running at least 1 daemon pod and are supposed to run the daemon pod. More info: https://kubernetes.io/docs/concepts/workloads/controllers/daemonset/
  • updatedNumberScheduled (int32): The total number of nodes that are running updated daemon pod.
  • collisionCount (int32): Count of hash collisions for the DaemonSet. The DaemonSet controller uses this field as a collision avoidance mechanism when it needs to create the name for the newest ControllerRevision.
  • conditions ([]DaemonSetCondition): Represents the latest available observations of a DaemonSet's current state. Patch strategy: merge on key type. Map: unique values on key type will be kept during a merge.
  • observedGeneration (int64): The most recent generation observed by the daemon set controller.

DaemonSetList

Docs: Kubernetes DaemonSetList Documentation

Collection of DaemonSets with metadata for listing and pagination support.

Full description

DaemonSetList is a collection of DaemonSets used when listing multiple DaemonSet resources. This is returned by kubectl get daemonsets or API calls that retrieve multiple DaemonSets. For Django applications, you might have multiple DaemonSets for different node-level services like logging, monitoring, or network proxies that support your main Django applications.

Syntax

apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSetList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: string
  continue: string
items:
- apiVersion: apps/v1
  kind: DaemonSet
  metadata:
    name: string
  spec:
    selector:
      matchLabels:
        key: value

Parameters description

  • apiVersion: Always "apps/v1" for DaemonSetList resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version for this list resource.
  • kind: Must be "DaemonSetList" to indicate this is a collection of DaemonSet resources.
  • metadata: Standard list metadata including resource version for consistency and continuation token for pagination.
  • items: Array of DaemonSet objects. Contains the actual DaemonSet resources that match the list query.
  • kind: Kind is a string value representing the REST resource this object represents. Always "DaemonSetList" for this resource.
  • metadata: Standard list metadata. More info: https://git.k8s.io/community/contributors/devel/sig-architecture/api-conventions.md#metadata
  • items ([]DaemonSet, required): A list of daemon sets.

    • Operations

    Docs: Kubernetes DaemonSet Operations

    HTTP API operations for managing DaemonSet resources across all cluster nodes.

    Full description

    DaemonSet operations provide HTTP API endpoints for managing DaemonSet resources in Kubernetes. These operations enable programmatic control over node-level services that support Django applications, including log collectors, monitoring agents, network proxies, and storage daemons that run on every node in your cluster.

    Get Read the Specified DaemonSet

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}
    Parameters
    • name (string, required, path): Name of the DaemonSet
    • namespace (string, required, path): Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    • pretty (string, query): If 'true', then the output is pretty printed.
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example 1: Get DaemonSet Details
    curl -X GET \
  $KUBE_API_SERVER/apis/apps/v1/namespaces/default/daemonsets/django-log-collector \
  -H "Authorization: Bearer $KUBE_TOKEN"
    Result: Returns detailed information about the django-log-collector DaemonSet including pod distribution across nodes.
    Example 2: Get DaemonSet with kubectl
    kubectl get daemonset django-log-collector -o yaml
    Result: Returns the complete DaemonSet manifest in YAML format showing all current settings and status.

    Get Read Status of the Specified DaemonSet

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}/status
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Check DaemonSet Status
    kubectl get daemonset django-log-collector -o jsonpath='{.status}'
    Result: Returns status information showing ready, scheduled, and available pod counts across nodes for Django log collection.

    List or Watch Objects of Kind DaemonSet

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets
    Parameters
    • namespace (string, required, path): Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    • labelSelector (string, query): A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their labels
    • fieldSelector (string, query): A selector to restrict the list of returned objects by their fields
    • watch (boolean, query): Watch for changes to the described resources and return them as a stream
    Response

    200 (DaemonSetList): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example 1: List All DaemonSets
    kubectl get daemonsets
    Result: Lists all DaemonSets in the current namespace with information about desired, current, and ready pods.
    Example 2: List DaemonSets with Labels
    kubectl get daemonsets -l component=logging
    Result: Lists only DaemonSets that have the component=logging label, filtering for Django logging infrastructure.

    List or Watch Objects of Kind DaemonSet

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/apps/v1/daemonsets
    Examples
    Example: List DaemonSets Across All Namespaces
    kubectl get daemonsets --all-namespaces
    Result: Lists all DaemonSets across all namespaces in the cluster, useful for cluster-wide Django infrastructure monitoring.

    Create a DaemonSet

    POST
    HTTP Request
    POST /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets
    Parameters
    • namespace (string, required, path): Object name and auth scope, such as for teams and projects
    • body (DaemonSet, required): DaemonSet manifest to create
    • dryRun (string, query): When present, indicates that modifications should not be persisted
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    202 (DaemonSet): Accepted

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example 1: Create Django Monitoring DaemonSet
    kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: apps/v1
kind: DaemonSet
metadata:
  name: django-monitor
spec:
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      app: django-monitor
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django-monitor
    spec:
      containers:
      - name: node-exporter
        image: prom/node-exporter:latest
        ports:
        - containerPort: 9100
        hostNetwork: true
EOF
    kubectl output: 
    daemonset.apps/django-monitor created
    Monitor DaemonSet Status: 
    $ kubectl get daemonset django-monitor
NAME             DESIRED   CURRENT   READY   UP-TO-DATE   AVAILABLE   NODE SELECTOR   AGE
django-monitor   3         3         3       3            3                     20s

$ kubectl describe daemonset django-monitor

Desired Number of Nodes Scheduled: 3

Number of Nodes Scheduled with Available Pods: 3
Number of Nodes Misscheduled: 0
Pods Status:  3 Running / 0 Waiting / 0 Succeeded / 0 Failed

  Labels:  app=django-monitor
  Containers:
   node-exporter:
    Image:      prom/node-exporter:latest
    Port:       9100/TCP
    Host Port:  0/TCP
    Environment:  
    Mounts:       
  Volumes:        
Events:
  Type    Reason            Age   From                  Message
  ----    ------            ----  ----                  -------

  Normal  SuccessfulCreate  25s   daemonset-controller  Created pod: django-monitor-def456

    Example 2: Dry Run DaemonSet Creation
    kubectl apply --dry-run=client -f django-daemonset.yaml
    Result: Validates the DaemonSet manifest without actually creating the resource, useful for testing Django DaemonSet configurations.

    Update Replace the Specified DaemonSet

    PUT
    HTTP Request
    PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Update DaemonSet Image
    kubectl set image daemonset/django-monitor node-exporter=prom/node-exporter:v1.2.0
    Result: Updates the DaemonSet to use a new image version, triggering a rolling update across all nodes running Django monitoring.

    Update Replace Status of the Specified DaemonSet

    PUT
    HTTP Request
    PUT /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}/status
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Patch Partially Update the Specified DaemonSet

    PATCH
    HTTP Request
    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}
    Parameters
    • body - Patch, required - Patch to apply to the DaemonSet
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Patch DaemonSet Update Strategy
    kubectl patch daemonset django-monitor -p '{"spec":{"updateStrategy":{"rollingUpdate":{"maxUnavailable":2}}}}'
    Result: Patches the DaemonSet to allow up to 2 unavailable pods during rolling updates for faster Django monitoring updates.

    Patch Partially Update Status of the Specified DaemonSet

    PATCH
    HTTP Request
    PATCH /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}/status
    Response

    200 (DaemonSet): OK

    201 (DaemonSet): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Delete a DaemonSet

    DELETE
    HTTP Request
    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets/{name}
    Parameters
    • gracePeriodSeconds - integer (query) - The duration in seconds before the object should be deleted
    • propagationPolicy - string (query) - Whether and how garbage collection will be performed
    Response

    200 (Status): OK

    202 (Status): Accepted

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example 1: Delete DaemonSet
    kubectl delete daemonset django-monitor
    Result: Deletes the DaemonSet and all its managed pods across all nodes, removing Django monitoring from the cluster.
    Example 2: Delete with Grace Period
    kubectl delete daemonset django-log-collector --grace-period=30
    Result: Deletes the DaemonSet with a 30-second grace period for graceful shutdown of Django log collection containers.

    Delete Collection of DaemonSet

    DELETE
    HTTP Request
    DELETE /apis/apps/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/daemonsets
    Parameters
    • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector to filter which DaemonSets to delete
    • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector to filter which DaemonSets to delete
    Response

    200 (Status): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Delete Multiple DaemonSets
    kubectl delete daemonsets -l component=logging
    Result: Deletes all DaemonSets with the component=logging label, removing all Django logging infrastructure from the cluster.

    Job

    Docs: Kubernetes Job v1

    Job represents the configuration of a single job for running batch tasks and one-time operations.

    🎯 Overview

    Job runs one or more Pods to completion and ensures that a specified number of them successfully terminate. Unlike Deployments or ReplicaSets that maintain long-running services, Jobs are designed for batch processing, one-time tasks, and finite workloads. Jobs are perfect for Django maintenance tasks, data migrations, report generation, or cleanup operations.

    For Django applications, Jobs are ideal for running periodic maintenance tasks like data processing, backup operations, sending batch emails, or performing database migrations. When your Django JobPost application needs to process user data, generate reports, or perform cleanup tasks, Jobs provide reliability with retry logic and completion tracking.

    💡 Note: Jobs are different from CronJobs - Jobs run once, while CronJobs run Jobs on a schedule. Use Jobs for immediate one-time tasks and CronJobs for recurring scheduled tasks.

    📋 Job Components Overview

    Job - Main batch processing resource
    JobSpec - Configuration and behavior
    JobStatus - Execution state and progress
    JobList - Collection of multiple Jobs

    🔧 Job Operations Overview

    GET - Read specified Job details
    GET Status - Read Job execution status
    LIST - List Jobs in namespace
    LIST All - List Jobs across namespaces
    CREATE - Create new Job
    UPDATE - Replace entire Job
    UPDATE Status - Replace Job status
    PATCH - Partially update Job
    PATCH Status - Partially update status
    DELETE - Remove specific Job
    DELETE Collection - Remove multiple Jobs

    🔍 Detailed Section Overviews

    Job Resource - Core resource structure overview
    JobSpec Components - Configuration options overview
    JobStatus Components - Status tracking overview
    JobStatus Fields - Individual status fields
    JobList Components - Collection structure overview
    Operations Overview - HTTP API operations
    Operations Categories - Grouped by operation type
    ✨ Enhanced Documentation: This guide features professional syntax highlighting powered by Prism.js, matching the quality of industry-standard documentation. All examples use your exact Django models with realistic outputs.

    Job

    Docs: Kubernetes Job v1 API

    Runs one or more Pods to completion, ensuring reliable execution of batch tasks and one-time operations for Django applications.

    Full description

    A Job creates one or more Pods and ensures that a specified number of them successfully terminate. Jobs are perfect for Django batch processing tasks like data imports, report generation, cleanup operations, or database migrations. Unlike Deployments that maintain continuous services, Jobs run to completion and track success/failure states. They provide built-in retry logic, parallelism control, and completion guarantees essential for reliable Django background processing.

    📋 Job Resource Overview

    apiVersion - batch/v1 API version
    kind - Job resource type
    metadata - Names, labels, annotations
    spec - Job configuration (JobSpec)
    status - Execution state (JobStatus)
    ✨ Batch Processing: One-time task execution with completion guarantees, retry logic, parallelism control, and comprehensive monitoring for Django background operations.

    Syntax

    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: job-name
  namespace: namespace-name
  labels:
    app: app-name
    type: batch
spec:
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: app-name
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never  # or OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: container-name
        image: image:tag
        command: ["command"]
        args: ["arg1", "arg2"]
  completions: 1
  parallelism: 1
  backoffLimit: 6
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 3600
status:
  active: 0
  succeeded: 1
  failed: 0

    Parameters description

    • apiVersion: Always "batch/v1" for Job resources. Specifies the Kubernetes API version for batch workloads.
    • kind: Must be "Job" to indicate this is a Job resource definition.
    • metadata: Standard object metadata including name, namespace, labels, and annotations. Use descriptive names like "django-migration-job" or "report-generation-job".
    • spec: Specification of the desired behavior of the Job. Defines the pod template, completion requirements, and execution parameters.
    • spec.template: Pod template that describes the pods that will be created to run the job. Must include restartPolicy of "Never" or "OnFailure".
    • spec.completions: Number of pod completions required for the job to be considered successful. Defaults to 1.
    • spec.parallelism: Maximum number of pods that should run in parallel. Controls job execution concurrency.
    • spec.backoffLimit: Number of retries before marking the job as failed. Defaults to 6 attempts.
    • spec.activeDeadlineSeconds: Maximum duration in seconds that the job may be active before termination.
    • status: Current status of the Job including counts of active, succeeded, and failed pods.

    Return value

    Job object: Returns the created Job resource with system-assigned fields including creation timestamp, job status, and pod execution tracking. The status will show progression from active pods to successful completion or failure, providing complete visibility into job execution state.

    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models

    Example 1: Django Database Migration Job with Init Container
    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: anihpj-migration-job
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: migration
    type: database
spec:
  completions: 1
  parallelism: 1
  backoffLimit: 3
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 1800
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: migration
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      initContainers:
      - name: db-health-check
        image: postgres:13
        command:
        - sh
        - -c
        - |
          until pg_isready -h $DB_HOST -p $DB_PORT -U $DB_USER; do
            echo "Waiting for database..."
            sleep 5
          done
        env:
        - name: DB_HOST
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-config
              key: database-host
        - name: DB_PORT
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-config
              key: database-port
        - name: DB_USER
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: username
      containers:
      - name: django-migrate
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate", "--verbosity=2"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: DB_NAME
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: database
        - name: DB_USER
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: username
        - name: DB_PASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: password
        - name: DB_HOST
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-config
              key: database-host
        volumeMounts:
        - name: migration-logs
          mountPath: /app/logs
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
      volumes:
      - name: migration-logs
        emptyDir: {}
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: anihpj-config
  namespace: anihpj-production
data:
  database-host: "postgres-service.anihpj-production.svc.cluster.local"
  database-port: "5432"
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: Secret
metadata:
  name: anihpj-db-secret
  namespace: anihpj-production
type: Opaque
data:
  username: YW5paHBq  # anihpj
  password: cGFzcw==  # pass
  database: YW5paHBqX2Ri  # anihpj_db

    Example 2: Parallel JobPost Data Processing Job with ConfigMap
    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: jobpost-processor-job
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: data-processor
    batch: jobpost-processing
spec:
  completions: 10
  parallelism: 3
  backoffLimit: 2
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 3600
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: data-processor
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-processor
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_jobposts"]
        args: ["--batch-size", "$(BATCH_SIZE)", "--worker-id", "$(WORKER_ID)"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: BATCH_SIZE
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: processing-config
              key: batch-size
        - name: WORKER_ID
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        - name: REDIS_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-redis-secret
              key: url
        - name: DB_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: database-url
        volumeMounts:
        - name: processing-logs
          mountPath: /app/processing-logs
        - name: temp-storage
          mountPath: /tmp/processing
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "800m"
        livenessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - python
            - -c
            - "import os; exit(0 if os.path.exists('/tmp/processing/heartbeat') else 1)"
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 30
      volumes:
      - name: processing-logs
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-logs-pvc
      - name: temp-storage
        emptyDir:
          sizeLimit: 1Gi
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: processing-config
  namespace: anihpj-production
data:
  batch-size: "50"
  processing-timeout: "1800"
  retry-attempts: "3"
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: Secret
metadata:
  name: anihpj-redis-secret
  namespace: anihpj-production
type: Opaque
data:
  url: cmVkaXM6Ly9yZWRpcy1zZXJ2aWNlOjYzNzk=  # redis://redis-service:6379

    Example 3: Report Generation Job with Persistent Storage
    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: anihpj-report-generator
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: reports
    type: monthly-report
spec:
  completions: 1
  parallelism: 1
  backoffLimit: 3
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 7200
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: report-generator
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      serviceAccountName: anihpj-reports-sa
      containers:
      - name: report-generator
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "generate_monthly_report"]
        args: ["--month", "$(REPORT_MONTH)", "--format", "pdf", "--email-notify"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: REPORT_MONTH
          value: "2024-01"
        - name: AWS_ACCESS_KEY_ID
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: aws-credentials
              key: access-key-id
        - name: AWS_SECRET_ACCESS_KEY
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: aws-credentials
              key: secret-access-key
        - name: S3_BUCKET
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: report-config
              key: s3-bucket
        - name: EMAIL_BACKEND
          value: "django.core.mail.backends.smtp.EmailBackend"
        - name: EMAIL_HOST
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: email-secret
              key: host
        - name: EMAIL_PORT
          value: "587"
        - name: EMAIL_USE_TLS
          value: "True"
        - name: EMAIL_HOST_USER
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: email-secret
              key: username
        - name: EMAIL_HOST_PASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: email-secret
              key: password
        volumeMounts:
        - name: report-storage
          mountPath: /app/reports
        - name: temp-processing
          mountPath: /tmp/report-processing
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
          limits:
            memory: "2Gi"
            cpu: "1000m"
      volumes:
      - name: report-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-reports-pvc
      - name: temp-processing
        emptyDir:
          sizeLimit: 2Gi
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: PersistentVolumeClaim
metadata:
  name: anihpj-reports-pvc
  namespace: anihpj-production
spec:
  accessModes:
    - ReadWriteOnce
  resources:
    requests:
      storage: 10Gi
  storageClassName: fast-ssd
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: report-config
  namespace: anihpj-production
data:
  s3-bucket: "anihpj-reports"
  report-retention-days: "90"
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ServiceAccount
metadata:
  name: anihpj-reports-sa
  namespace: anihpj-production
