    Example 4: Skills Data Cleanup Job with Retry Logic
    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: skills-cleanup-job
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: data-cleanup
    type: skills-maintenance
spec:
  completions: 1
  parallelism: 1
  backoffLimit: 5
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 3600
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: skills-cleanup
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: skills-cleanup
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "cleanup_skills"]
        args: ["--dry-run=false", "--remove-duplicates", "--normalize-names"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: CLEANUP_BATCH_SIZE
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: cleanup-config
              key: batch-size
        - name: DB_BACKUP_ENABLED
          value: "true"
        - name: SLACK_WEBHOOK_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: notification-secret
              key: slack-webhook
        volumeMounts:
        - name: cleanup-logs
          mountPath: /app/cleanup-logs
        - name: backup-storage
          mountPath: /app/backups
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        readinessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - python
            - -c
            - "import django; django.setup(); from django.db import connection; connection.ensure_connection()"
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 15
      initContainers:
      - name: db-backup
        image: postgres:13
        command:
        - sh
        - -c
        - |
          pg_dump -h $DB_HOST -U $DB_USER -d $DB_NAME --table=jobpost_skills > /backup/skills_backup_$(date +%Y%m%d_%H%M%S).sql
          echo "Skills table backup completed"
        env:
        - name: DB_HOST
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: host
        - name: DB_USER
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: username
        - name: DB_NAME
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: database
        - name: PGPASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: password
        volumeMounts:
        - name: backup-storage
          mountPath: /backup
      volumes:
      - name: cleanup-logs
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-logs-pvc
      - name: backup-storage
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-backup-pvc
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: cleanup-config
  namespace: anihpj-production
data:
  batch-size: "100"
  duplicate-threshold: "0.9"
  cleanup-timeout: "3600"
    Execute skills cleanup with monitoring:
    # Apply the cleanup job
kubectl apply -f skills-cleanup-job.yaml

# Monitor job execution
kubectl get job skills-cleanup-job -n anihpj-production -w

# Check backup init container
kubectl logs -n anihpj-production -l job-name=skills-cleanup-job -c db-backup

# Follow cleanup progress

# Check cleanup results

from jobpost.models import Skills
print(f'Total skills after cleanup: {Skills.objects.count()}')
print(f'Skills with duplicates: {Skills.objects.filter(name__icontains=\"duplicate\").count()}')
"

    Example 5: Location Data Sync Job with External API Integration
    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: location-sync-job
  namespace: anihpj-production
  labels:
    app: anihpj
    component: data-sync
    source: external-api
    type: location-update
spec:
  completions: 1
  parallelism: 1
  backoffLimit: 3
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 2400
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: location-sync
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: location-sync
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "sync_locations"]
        args: ["--source", "geocoding-api", "--update-existing", "--validate-coordinates"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: GEOCODING_API_KEY
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: api-credentials
              key: geocoding-api-key
        - name: GEOCODING_API_URL
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: sync-config
              key: geocoding-api-url
        - name: RATE_LIMIT_DELAY
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: sync-config
              key: rate-limit-delay
        - name: REDIS_CACHE_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-redis-secret
              key: url
        - name: SYNC_NOTIFICATION_EMAIL
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: sync-config
              key: notification-email
        volumeMounts:
        - name: sync-logs
          mountPath: /app/sync-logs
        - name: cache-storage
          mountPath: /app/cache
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
        livenessProbe:
          httpGet:
            path: /health
            port: 8000
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 30
        env:
        - name: HEALTH_CHECK_PORT
          value: "8000"
      - name: health-server
        image: nginx:alpine
        ports:
        - containerPort: 8000
        volumeMounts:
        - name: health-config
          mountPath: /etc/nginx/conf.d
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "32Mi"
            cpu: "10m"
          limits:
            memory: "64Mi"
            cpu: "50m"
      volumes:
      - name: sync-logs
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-logs-pvc
      - name: cache-storage
        emptyDir:
          sizeLimit: 500Mi
      - name: health-config
        configMap:
          name: health-server-config
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: sync-config
  namespace: anihpj-production
data:
  geocoding-api-url: "https://api.geocoding-service.com/v1"
  rate-limit-delay: "200"
  notification-email: "admin@anihpj.com"
  batch-size: "25"
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: health-server-config
  namespace: anihpj-production
data:
  default.conf: |
    server {
        listen 8000;
        location /health {
            return 200 'healthy\n';
            add_header Content-Type text/plain;
        }
    }
---
apiVersion: v1
kind: Secret
metadata:
  name: api-credentials
  namespace: anihpj-production
type: Opaque
data:
  geocoding-api-key: YWJjZGVmZ2hpams=  # sample API key

    JobSpec

    Docs: Kubernetes JobSpec Documentation

    Specification describing how job execution will look like, including pod template, completion requirements, and execution parameters.

    Full description

    JobSpec defines the desired behavior of a Job for Django batch processing tasks. It includes the pod template specification, completion and parallelism settings, retry policies, and deadline constraints. Essential for configuring reliable batch operations like data migrations, report generation, and cleanup tasks in Django applications.

    📋 JobSpec Components Overview

    Replicas - Template and parallelism config
    Lifecycle - Completion and retry policies
    Selector - Pod selection and labeling
    Beta level - Advanced failure policies
    Alpha level - Experimental features
    ✨ JobSpec Features: Configure pod templates, parallelism, completion requirements, retry policies, deadlines, and advanced failure handling for reliable Django batch processing.

    Replicas

    Template and parallelism configuration for Job pods.

    Parameters description
    • template (PodTemplateSpec), required: Describes the pod that will be created when executing a job. The only allowed template.spec.restartPolicy values are "Never" or "OnFailure". Essential for Django batch tasks requiring specific container configurations.
    • parallelism (int32): Specifies the maximum desired number of pods the job should run at any given time. Controls concurrent execution for Django batch processing tasks. Useful for parallel data processing or report generation.
    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models
    Example 1: Single Pod Django Migration with Resource Limits
    spec:
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: migration
        version: v2.1.0
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      serviceAccountName: anihpj-migration-sa
      containers:
      - name: django-migrate
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate", "--verbosity=2"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: DB_HOST
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-config
              key: database-host
        - name: DB_NAME
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-db-secret
              key: database
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: migration-logs
          mountPath: /app/logs
      volumes:
      - name: migration-logs
        emptyDir: {}
    Apply and monitor migration:

# Check pod template execution

    Example 2: Parallel JobPost Processing with ConfigMap
    spec:
  parallelism: 4
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost-processor
        batch: parallel-processing
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-processor
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_jobposts"]
        args: ["--batch-size", "$(BATCH_SIZE)", "--worker-id", "$(POD_NAME)"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: BATCH_SIZE
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: processing-config
              key: batch-size
        - name: POD_NAME
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        - name: REDIS_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: anihpj-redis-secret
              key: url
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "800m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: processing-temp
          mountPath: /tmp/processing
        livenessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - python
            - -c
            - "import os; exit(0 if os.path.exists('/tmp/processing/heartbeat') else 1)"
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 30
      volumes:
      - name: processing-temp
        emptyDir:
          sizeLimit: 1Gi
    Deploy and monitor parallel processing:
    # Deploy parallel processing job
kubectl apply -f parallel-jobpost-processing.yaml

# Monitor all parallel pods
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,component=jobpost-processor --watch

# Check individual worker logs
kubectl logs -l app=anihpj,component=jobpost-processor --all-containers=true

# Monitor processing metrics
kubectl exec deploy/anihpj-web -- python manage.py shell -c "
from jobpost.models import JobPost
print(f'Total: {JobPost.objects.count()}')
print(f'Processed: {JobPost.objects.filter(status=\"processed\").count()}')
"

    Example 3: Skills Data Processing with Init Container
    spec:
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: skills-processor
        type: data-enhancement
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      initContainers:
      - name: skills-data-validator
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command:
        - sh
        - -c
        - |
          python manage.py shell -c "
          from jobpost.models import Skills
          invalid_skills = Skills.objects.filter(name__exact='')
          if invalid_skills.exists():
              print(f'Found {invalid_skills.count()} invalid skills')
              exit(1)
          print('Skills data validation passed')
          "
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
      containers:
      - name: skills-processor
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "enhance_skills_data"]
        args: ["--add-categories", "--normalize-names", "--update-descriptions"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: SKILLS_API_KEY
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: skills-api-secret
              key: api-key
        - name: ENHANCEMENT_LEVEL
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: skills-config
              key: enhancement-level
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "150m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "400m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: skills-cache
          mountPath: /app/cache/skills
        - name: enhanced-data
          mountPath: /app/enhanced
      volumes:
      - name: skills-cache
        emptyDir:
          sizeLimit: 200Mi
      - name: enhanced-data
        emptyDir:
          sizeLimit: 300Mi

    Example 4: Location Data Sync with Persistent Storage
    spec:
  parallelism: 2
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: location-sync
        source: geocoding-api
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: location-sync
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "sync_location_data"]
        args: ["--source", "geocoding-api", "--parallel-workers", "2"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: GEOCODING_API_URL
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: location-config
              key: geocoding-api-url
        - name: API_KEY
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: geocoding-secret
              key: api-key
        - name: WORKER_ID
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.name
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: location-cache
          mountPath: /app/cache/locations
        - name: sync-logs
          mountPath: /app/logs/sync
        readinessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - python
            - -c
            - "import requests; requests.get('https://api.geocoding-service.com/health').raise_for_status()"
          initialDelaySeconds: 10
          periodSeconds: 30
      volumes:
      - name: location-cache
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-cache-pvc
      - name: sync-logs
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-logs-pvc

    Example 5: Author Report Generation with Security Context
    spec:
  parallelism: 1
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: report-generator
        report-type: author-analytics
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      securityContext:
        runAsNonRoot: true
        runAsUser: 1000
        runAsGroup: 1000
        fsGroup: 1000
      containers:
      - name: author-report-generator
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "generate_author_reports"]
        args: ["--format", "pdf", "--include-analytics", "--email-recipients"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: REPORT_OUTPUT_DIR
          value: "/app/reports/authors"
        - name: EMAIL_BACKEND
          value: "django.core.mail.backends.smtp.EmailBackend"
        - name: SMTP_HOST
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: email-config
              key: smtp-host
        - name: SMTP_USER
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: email-config
              key: smtp-user
        - name: SMTP_PASSWORD
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: email-config
              key: smtp-password
        securityContext:
          allowPrivilegeEscalation: false
          readOnlyRootFilesystem: true
          capabilities:
            drop:
            - ALL
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "250m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: report-output
          mountPath: /app/reports
        - name: temp-processing
          mountPath: /tmp
        - name: cache-dir
          mountPath: /app/cache
      volumes:
      - name: report-output
        persistentVolumeClaim:
          claimName: anihpj-reports-pvc
      - name: temp-processing
        emptyDir: {}
      - name: cache-dir
        emptyDir: {}

StartupXYZ: 2 authors, 12 jobs

    Lifecycle

    Job completion and lifecycle management configuration.

    Parameters description
    • completions (int32): Specifies the desired number of successfully finished pods the job should be run with. Setting to null means that the success of any pod signals the success of all pods. Essential for Django batch operations requiring specific completion counts.
    • completionMode (string): Specifies how Pod completions are tracked. Can be "NonIndexed" (default) or "Indexed". Indexed mode assigns completion indexes for ordered processing.
    • backoffLimit (int32): Specifies the number of retries before marking this job failed. Defaults to 6. Critical for handling Django task failures gracefully.
    • activeDeadlineSeconds (int64): Duration in seconds relative to startTime that the job may be continuously active before termination. Essential for preventing runaway Django tasks.
    • ttlSecondsAfterFinished (int32): Limits the lifetime of a Job that has finished execution. Job becomes eligible for automatic deletion after this period.
    • suspend (boolean): Whether the Job controller should create Pods or not. Useful for temporarily halting Django batch operations. Defaults to false.
    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models
    Example 1: Single Completion Migration with Timeout
    spec:
  completions: 1
  backoffLimit: 3
  activeDeadlineSeconds: 3600
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: database-migration
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: migration-runner
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate", "--verbosity=2"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: DB_MIGRATE_TIMEOUT
          value: "3000"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "500m"
    Monitor completion tracking:
    # Apply migration job with completion tracking
kubectl apply -f migration-completion-job.yaml

# Watch job progress and completion
kubectl get job migration-job -w

# Check completion status
kubectl describe job migration-job | grep -A 5 "Conditions"

# Verify 1 successful completion
kubectl get job migration-job -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}'
    Result: Job completes when 1 pod succeeds, allows 3 retries, enforces 1-hour deadline for migration.

    Example 2: Indexed JobPost Processing with Completion Mode
    spec:
  completions: 5
  completionMode: Indexed
  parallelism: 2
  backoffLimit: 2
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        job: indexed-processing
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-processor
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_jobpost_batch"]
        args: ["--index", "$(JOB_COMPLETION_INDEX)", "--batch-size", "100"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: JOB_COMPLETION_INDEX
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.annotations['batch.kubernetes.io/job-completion-index']
        - name: BATCH_PROCESSING_MODE
          value: "indexed"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "800m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: processing-state
          mountPath: /app/state
      volumes:
      - name: processing-state
        emptyDir: {}

    Selector

    Pod selection and labeling configuration for Job management.

    Parameters description
    • selector (LabelSelector): A label query over pods that should match the pod count. Normally, the system sets this field automatically for Django batch jobs.
    • manualSelector (boolean): Controls generation of pod labels and pod selectors. Leave unset unless you need custom pod selection logic for Django applications. When true, you're responsible for picking unique labels.
    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models
    Example 1: Automatic Selector for JobPost Processing
    spec:
  # selector automatically generated by Kubernetes
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost-processor
        version: v2.1.0
        batch-type: automated
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-processor
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_jobpost_data"]
        args: ["--auto-categorize", "--update-salary-ranges"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: PROCESSING_MODE
          value: "batch"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
    Monitor automatic selector assignment:
    # Deploy job with automatic selector
kubectl apply -f jobpost-auto-selector.yaml

# Check automatically generated selector
kubectl get job jobpost-processor-job -o jsonpath='{.spec.selector}'

# Verify pod labels match selector
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,component=jobpost-processor --show-labels

# Check job-name label added by Kubernetes
kubectl get pods -l job-name=jobpost-processor-job
    Result: Kubernetes automatically generates unique selector matching pod template labels for JobPost processing.

    Example 2: Manual Selector for User Migration
    spec:
  manualSelector: true
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      batch: user-migration-v2
      migration-type: incremental
      data-source: legacy-system
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        batch: user-migration-v2
        migration-type: incremental
        data-source: legacy-system
        app: anihpj
        component: user-migrator
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: user-migrator
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate_users"]
        args: ["--source", "legacy", "--validate", "--batch-size", "50"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: LEGACY_DB_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: legacy-db-secret
              key: database-url
        - name: MIGRATION_BATCH_SIZE
          value: "50"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "150m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"
    Manage manual selector migration:
    # Deploy job with manual selector
kubectl apply -f user-migration-manual-selector.yaml

# Check pods match manual selector

    Example 5: Author Report with Expression-based Selector
    spec:

    - key: report-type
      operator: In
      values: [author, weekly, analytics]
    - key: priority
      operator: NotIn
      values: [low]
    - key: app
      operator: Exists
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        report-type: author
        priority: high
        frequency: weekly
        app: anihpj
        component: report-generator
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: author-reporter
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "generate_author_analytics"]
        args: ["--period", "weekly", "--include-metrics", "--export-pdf"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: REPORT_FORMAT
          value: "pdf"
        - name: ANALYTICS_DEPTH
          value: "detailed"
        - name: EMAIL_RECIPIENTS
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: report-config
              key: recipients
        - name: S3_BUCKET
          valueFrom:
            configMapKeyRef:
              name: report-config
              key: s3-bucket
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"

    Beta level

    Beta-level features for advanced Job failure handling and success policies.

    Parameters description
    • podFailurePolicy (PodFailurePolicy): Specifies the policy of handling failed pods. Allows custom actions and conditions for pod failures. Cannot be used with restartPolicy=OnFailure.
    • successPolicy (SuccessPolicy): Specifies when the Job can be declared successful before all completions finish. Works only for Indexed Jobs and is immutable once set.
    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models
    Example 1: Ignore Exit Code 1 for Non-Critical Failures
    spec:
  podFailurePolicy:
    rules:
    - action: Ignore
      onExitCodes:
        operator: In
        values: [1]
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: data-validator
        failure-tolerance: high
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: data-validator
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "validate_jobpost_data"]
        args: ["--strict=false", "--ignore-warnings"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: VALIDATION_MODE
          value: "lenient"
        - name: CONTINUE_ON_WARNING
          value: "true"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"

    Result: Job ignores pods that exit with code 1 (warnings), creates replacement pods to continue validation.

    Example 5: Pod Condition Policy for Disruption Handling
    spec:
  completions: 3
  parallelism: 2
  podFailurePolicy:
    rules:
    - action: Count
      onPodConditions:
      - type: DisruptionTarget
        status: "True"
    - action: Ignore
      onPodConditions:
      - type: Ready
        status: "False"
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: author-analytics
        disruption-tolerant: "true"
    spec:
      restartPolicy: OnFailure
      containers:
      - name: author-analyzer
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "analyze_author_performance"]
        args: ["--deep-analysis", "--export-metrics"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: ANALYSIS_DEPTH
          value: "comprehensive"
        - name: EXPORT_FORMAT
          value: "json,csv"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        readinessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - python
            - -c
            - "import psutil; exit(0 if psutil.virtual_memory().percent < 80 else 1)"
          initialDelaySeconds: 30
          periodSeconds: 15
        livenessProbe:
          exec:
            command:
            - python
            - -c
            - "import os; exit(0 if os.path.exists('/tmp/analysis_active') else 1)"
          initialDelaySeconds: 60
          periodSeconds: 30
    Monitor disruption handling with pod conditions:
    # Deploy author analytics with disruption policy

# Simulate cluster disruption

kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,component=author-analytics -w

# Check pod conditions
kubectl describe pods -l app=anihpj,component=author-analytics | grep -A 5 "Conditions"
    Result: Job counts disruption target failures towards backoff limit but ignores readiness failures for resilient processing.

    Alpha level

    Alpha-level features for advanced Job management and indexing.

    Parameters description
    • backoffLimitPerIndex (int32): Limit for retries within an index before marking it failed. Only for Indexed Jobs with restartPolicy=Never. Tracked in pod annotations.
    • managedBy (string): Indicates the controller managing a Job. Use custom domain-prefixed paths for external controllers. Default is kubernetes.io/job-controller.
    • maxFailedIndexes (int32): Maximum failed indexes before marking Job as failed. Used with backoffLimitPerIndex for indexed job failure management.
    • podReplacementPolicy (string): When to create replacement Pods. Values: "TerminatingOrFailed" or "Failed". Controls pod recreation timing.
    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models
    Example 1: Per-Index Backoff for JobPost Processing
    spec:
  completionMode: Indexed
  completions: 10
  parallelism: 3
  backoffLimitPerIndex: 2
  maxFailedIndexes: 3
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: jobpost-indexer
        processing-mode: fault-tolerant
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: jobpost-processor
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "process_jobpost_index"]
        args: ["--index", "$(JOB_COMPLETION_INDEX)", "--fault-tolerant"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: JOB_COMPLETION_INDEX
          valueFrom:
            fieldRef:
              fieldPath: metadata.annotations['batch.kubernetes.io/job-completion-index']
        - name: MAX_RETRIES_PER_INDEX
          value: "2"
        - name: PROCESSING_MODE
          value: "indexed"
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "200m"
          limits:
            memory: "1Gi"
            cpu: "500m"
        volumeMounts:
        - name: index-state
          mountPath: /app/index-state
      volumes:
      - name: index-state
        emptyDir: {}
    Monitor per-index backoff limits:
    # Deploy indexed JobPost processing
kubectl apply -f jobpost-per-index-backoff.yaml

# Monitor individual index failures
kubectl get job jobpost-indexer-job -w

# Check per-index retry annotations
kubectl get pods -l app=anihpj,component=jobpost-indexer -o yaml | grep -A 2 "batch.kubernetes.io/job-index-failure-count"

# View processing progress per index
kubectl logs -l app=anihpj,component=jobpost-indexer --all-containers=true
    Result: Each index allows 2 retries before marking failed; job fails after 3 total failed indexes.
    JobPost Processing with Per-Index Backoff:
    # Check JobPost processing results by index
>>> from jobpost.models import JobPost
>>> JobPost.objects.count()
700  # 7 successful indexes × 100 jobs each

# Check processing success by index
>>> index_results = {}
>>> for i in range(10):
...     index_jobs = JobPost.objects.filter(processing_index=i)
...     index_results[i] = {
...         'total': index_jobs.count(),
...         'successful': index_jobs.filter(status='processed').count(),
...         'failed': index_jobs.filter(status='failed').count()
...     }
...     print(f"Index {i}: {index_results[i]}")
Index 0: {'total': 100, 'successful': 100, 'failed': 0}
Index 1: {'total': 100, 'successful': 100, 'failed': 0}
Index 2: {'total': 0, 'successful': 0, 'failed': 0}     # Failed after 2 retries
Index 3: {'total': 100, 'successful': 100, 'failed': 0}
Index 4: {'total': 0, 'successful': 0, 'failed': 0}     # Failed after 2 retries
Index 5: {'total': 100, 'successful': 100, 'failed': 0}
Index 6: {'total': 0, 'successful': 0, 'failed': 0}     # Failed after 2 retries - job stops
Index 7: {'total': 0, 'successful': 0, 'failed': 0}     # Not processed due to max failures
Index 8: {'total': 100, 'successful': 100, 'failed': 0}
Index 9: {'total': 100, 'successful': 100, 'failed': 0}

# Verify job stopped after 3 failed indexes
>>> successful_indexes = [i for i, result in index_results.items() if result['successful'] > 0]
>>> len(successful_indexes)
7  # Job completed 7 out of 10 indexes before hitting maxFailedIndexes
    Example 2: Custom Controller Management
    spec:
  managedBy: anihpj.com/batch-job-controller
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: custom-batch-processor
        controller: external

      restartPolicy: Never

      - name: batch-processor

        command: ["python", "manage.py", "custom_batch_process"]

        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"

          value: "external"
        - name: BATCH_INTEGRATION
          value: "enabled"
        - name: WEBHOOK_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: webhook-secret
              key: controller-webhook
        resources:
          requests:
            memory: "256Mi"
            cpu: "100m"
          limits:
            memory: "512Mi"
            cpu: "300m"

    Example 3: Pod Replacement Policy for Failed Jobs
    spec:
  podReplacementPolicy: Failed
  backoffLimit: 3
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: anihpj
        component: data-migrator
        replacement-policy: wait-for-termination
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: data-migrator
        image: anihpj:v2.1.0
        command: ["python", "manage.py", "migrate_legacy_data"]
        args: ["--cleanup-on-failure", "--validate-integrity"]
        env:
        - name: DJANGO_SETTINGS_MODULE
          value: "anihpj.settings.production"
        - name: LEGACY_DB_URL
          valueFrom:
            secretKeyRef:
              name: legacy-db-secret
              key: connection-url
        - name: MIGRATION_BATCH_SIZE
          value: "1000"
        - name: VALIDATE_DATA_INTEGRITY
          value: "true"
        resources:
          requests:

    JobStatus

    Docs: Kubernetes JobStatus Documentation

    Current state of a Job including execution progress, completion status, and pod tracking information.

    Full description

    JobStatus represents the current state of a Job providing real-time information about job execution progress and completion status. For Django batch processing tasks, this status helps monitor task progress, track successful completions, and identify failures requiring intervention. Essential for understanding the health and progress of Django background operations.

    📊 JobStatus Components Overview

    Core Status - Active, failed, succeeded counts
    Timing - Start and completion timestamps
    Indexes - Completed indexed task tracking
    Conditions - Complete, Failed, Suspended states
    Beta level - Ready pod tracking
    Alpha level - Failed indexes and terminating

    📈 Status Fields Overview

    startTime - Job processing start timestamp
    completionTime - Successful completion timestamp
    active - Running pods count
    failed - Failed pods count
    succeeded - Completed pods count
    completedIndexes - Indexed task completion
    conditions - Job state observations
    uncountedTerminatedPods - Pending pod accounting
    ✨ Status Monitoring: Track real-time job execution progress, completion status, pod counts, and failure details for comprehensive Django batch operation monitoring.

    Parameters description

    • startTime: Time when the job controller started processing the job. Reset when job is resumed from suspension.
    • completionTime: Time when the job was completed successfully. Set only when job finishes successfully.
    • active: Number of pending and running pods which are not terminating. Zero for finished jobs.
    • failed: Number of pods which reached phase Failed. Value increases monotonically during job execution.
    • succeeded: Number of pods which reached phase Succeeded. Indicates successful Django task completions.
    • completedIndexes: Completed indexes when completionMode is "Indexed". Shows which specific tasks have completed.
    • conditions: Latest available observations of the job's current state. Includes "Complete", "Failed", or "Suspended" conditions.
    • uncountedTerminatedPods: UIDs of Pods that have terminated but haven't been accounted for in status counters yet.

    Beta level

    Beta-level JobStatus fields for enhanced pod tracking.

    Parameters description
    • ready (int32): Number of active pods which have a Ready condition and are not terminating. Provides insight into pods ready to process Django tasks.
    5 comprehensive examples with Django anihpj models
    Example 1: JobPost Processing Ready Pods Monitoring
    # Check ready pods for JobPost processing job

    # Get migration job status with ready pods
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: migration-monitor
data:
  check-ready.sh: |
    #!/bin/bash
    READY=$(kubectl get job user-migration-job -o jsonpath='{.status.ready}')
    ACTIVE=$(kubectl get job user-migration-job -o jsonpath='{.status.active}')
    SUCCEEDED=$(kubectl get job user-migration-job -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}')
    echo "Migration Status: Ready=$READY, Active=$ACTIVE, Succeeded=$SUCCEEDED"
    
    if [ "$READY" -eq "$ACTIVE" ] && [ "$ACTIVE" -gt 0 ]; then
      echo "All active pods are ready for migration processing"
    else
      echo "Some pods are not ready - waiting for readiness"
    fi
    Monitor user migration readiness:

  sleep 5
done

    Example 4: Location Sync Ready/Active Ratio Analysis
    # Advanced location sync readiness monitoring
#!/bin/bash

# Function to get job status metrics
get_job_metrics() {
    local job_name=$1
    local ready=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.ready}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    local active=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.active}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    local succeeded=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    local failed=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.failed}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    
    echo "Job: $job_name"
    echo "  Ready: $ready/$active ($(( ready * 100 / (active == 0 ? 1 : active) ))% ready ratio)"
    echo "  Progress: $succeeded completed, $failed failed"
    echo "  Efficiency: $(( (succeeded * 100) / (succeeded + failed == 0 ? 1 : succeeded + failed) ))% success rate"
}

# Monitor location sync job
get_job_metrics "location-sync-job"

# Check external API health
curl -s https://geocoding-api.example.com/health | jq '.status'

# Verify sync readiness
kubectl get pods -l job-name=location-sync-job -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}: Ready={.status.conditions[?(@.type=="Ready")].status}, RestartCount={.status.containerStatuses[0].restartCount}{"\n"}{end}'
    Analyze location sync readiness efficiency:
    # Execute comprehensive readiness analysis
bash location-sync-analysis.sh

# Monitor ready/active ratio over time
while true; do
  READY=$(kubectl get job location-sync-job -o jsonpath='{.status.ready}')
  ACTIVE=$(kubectl get job location-sync-job -o jsonpath='{.status.active}')
  RATIO=$(( READY * 100 / (ACTIVE == 0 ? 1 : ACTIVE) ))
  echo "$(date): Ready=$READY, Active=$ACTIVE, Ratio=${RATIO}%"
  sleep 10
done
    Result: Shows ready/active ratio analysis for location sync job with efficiency metrics.

    Example 5: Author Report Generation Ready State Dashboard
    # Author report job with comprehensive readiness monitoring
apiVersion: v1
kind: ConfigMap
metadata:
  name: author-report-dashboard
data:
  monitor.py: |
    #!/usr/bin/env python3
    import subprocess, json, time
    
    def get_job_status(job_name):
        try:
            cmd = f"kubectl get job {job_name} -o json"
            result = subprocess.run(cmd.split(), capture_output=True, text=True)
            return json.loads(result.stdout)
        except:
            return None
    
    def monitor_readiness():
        job_status = get_job_status("author-report-job")
        if not job_status:
            print("Job not found")
            return
            
        status = job_status.get('status', {})
        ready = status.get('ready', 0)
        active = status.get('active', 0)
        succeeded = status.get('succeeded', 0)
        
        print(f"Author Report Generation Status:")
        print(f"  Ready Pods: {ready}")
        print(f"  Active Pods: {active}")
        print(f"  Completed Reports: {succeeded}")
        print(f"  Readiness Ratio: {(ready/max(active,1)*100):.1f}%")
        
        if ready == 0 and active > 0:
            print("  ⚠️  Warning: No pods ready - check resource constraints")
        elif ready == active and active > 0:
            print("  ✅ All active pods are ready for processing")
        
    if __name__ == "__main__":
        monitor_readiness()
    Deploy author report readiness dashboard:
    # Deploy monitoring dashboard
kubectl apply -f author-report-dashboard.yaml

# Execute readiness monitoring
kubectl create job --from=configmap/author-report-dashboard readiness-check

# Watch readiness in dashboard format
kubectl logs job/readiness-check -f

# Check report generation pod conditions
kubectl get pods -l job-name=author-report-job -o custom-columns="NAME:.metadata.name,READY:.status.conditions[?(@.type=='Ready')].status,MEMORY:.status.containerStatuses[0].state"
    Result: Shows no ready pods, 1 active, 2 completed author reports with comprehensive dashboard monitoring.

    Alpha level

    • failedIndexes (string): Failed indexes when backoffLimitPerIndex is set. Shows which specific indexed tasks failed in comma-separated format.
    • terminating (int32): Number of pods which are terminating. Useful for tracking job shutdown progress and pod lifecycle management.

    Example 3: Skills Index Failures with Range Analysis
    # Complex skills processing with index ranges
kubectl get job skills-range-processor -o jsonpath='{.status.failedIndexes}' && echo

# Parse complex failed index ranges
FAILED=$(kubectl get job skills-range-processor -o jsonpath='{.status.failedIndexes}')
COMPLETED=$(kubectl get job skills-range-processor -o jsonpath='{.status.completedIndexes}')

echo "Failed indexes: $FAILED"
echo "Completed indexes: $COMPLETED"

# Analyze index range patterns
python3 -c "
failed = '$FAILED'
completed = '$COMPLETED'

def parse_ranges(range_str):
    indexes = set()
    if not range_str:
        return indexes
    for part in range_str.split(','):
        if '-' in part:
            start, end = map(int, part.split('-'))
            indexes.update(range(start, end + 1))
        else:
            indexes.add(int(part))
    return indexes

failed_set = parse_ranges(failed)
completed_set = parse_ranges(completed)

print(f'Failed indexes: {sorted(failed_set)}')
print(f'Completed indexes: {sorted(completed_set)}')
print(f'Success rate: {len(completed_set)/(len(failed_set)+len(completed_set))*100:.1f}%')
"

# Check resource usage correlation with failures
kubectl top pods -l job-name=skills-range-processor

    Example 4: Location Termination Status with Cleanup Monitoring
    # Advanced location sync termination monitoring
#!/bin/bash

monitor_location_termination() {
    local job_name="location-sync-cleanup"
    
    echo "=== Location Sync Termination Monitor ==="
    
    # Get current termination status
    local terminating=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.terminating}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    local active=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.active}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    local succeeded=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
    
    echo "Current Status:"
    echo "  Terminating: $terminating pods"
    echo "  Active: $active pods"
    echo "  Succeeded: $succeeded pods"
    
    # Check if graceful termination is in progress
    if [ "$terminating" -gt 0 ]; then
        echo "  🔄 Graceful termination in progress..."
        
        # Monitor cleanup activities
        kubectl logs -l job-name=$job_name --tail=20 | grep -i "cleanup\|shutdown\|terminating"
        
        # Check remaining cleanup tasks
        local cleanup_tasks=$(kubectl exec -l job-name=$job_name -- find /tmp/cleanup -name "*.lock" 2>/dev/null | wc -l)
        echo "  Remaining cleanup tasks: $cleanup_tasks"
    else
        echo "  ✅ No pods currently terminating"
    fi
    
    # Check pod termination reasons
    kubectl get events --field-selector involvedObject.kind=Pod | grep $job_name | grep "Terminating\|Killing" | tail -5
}

# Execute monitoring
monitor_location_termination

# Watch termination progress
kubectl get pods -l job-name=location-sync-cleanup -w
    Monitor location sync termination with cleanup:
    # Deploy location sync with termination monitoring
kubectl apply -f location-sync-cleanup-termination.yaml

# Execute termination monitoring script
bash location-termination-monitor.sh

# Trigger graceful termination
kubectl delete job location-sync-cleanup --grace-period=300

# Monitor cleanup completion
while kubectl get job location-sync-cleanup 2>/dev/null; do
  echo "Waiting for cleanup completion..."
  sleep 5
done
echo "Cleanup completed successfully"

    Example 5: Author Report Index Failures with Recovery Analysis
    # Comprehensive author report failure analysis and recovery
#!/bin/bash

analyze_author_report_failures() {
    local job_name="author-report-indexed"
    
    echo "=== Author Report Index Failure Analysis ==="
    
    # Get failure status
    local failed_indexes=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.failedIndexes}')
    local terminating=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.terminating}')
    local succeeded=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}')
    
    echo "Failure Status:"
    echo "  Failed Indexes: $failed_indexes"
    echo "  Terminating Pods: $terminating"
    echo "  Successful Reports: $succeeded"
    
    # Analyze failure patterns
    if [ -n "$failed_indexes" ]; then
        echo ""
        echo "Failure Analysis:"
        for index in $(echo $failed_indexes | tr ',' ' '); do
            echo "  Index $index:"
            kubectl logs -l job-name=$job_name,batch.kubernetes.io/job-completion-index=$index --tail=10 | grep -i "error\|failed\|exception" | head -3
        done
    fi
    
    # Check recovery options
    echo ""
    echo "Recovery Analysis:"
    local total_indexes=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.spec.completions}')
    local success_rate=$(( (succeeded * 100) / total_indexes ))
    echo "  Success Rate: $success_rate%"
    
    if [ $success_rate -lt 70 ]; then
        echo "  🔴 Low success rate - consider job restart with different configuration"
    elif [ $success_rate -lt 90 ]; then
        echo "  🟡 Moderate success rate - retry failed indexes only"
    else
        echo "  🟢 High success rate - minor failures, acceptable completion"
    fi
}

# Execute analysis
analyze_author_report_failures

# Generate recovery plan
kubectl get job author-report-indexed -o jsonpath='{.status.failedIndexes}' | tr ',' '\n' > failed_indexes.txt
echo "Recovery plan generated for failed indexes"
    Analyze author report failures and plan recovery:
    # Deploy author report processing with failure tracking

# Execute comprehensive failure analysis

# Plan targeted recovery for failed indexes

    JobList

    Docs: Kubernetes JobList Documentation

    Collection of Jobs with metadata for listing and pagination support when managing multiple Django batch operations.

    Full description

    JobList is a collection of Jobs used when listing multiple Job resources. This is returned by kubectl get jobs or API calls that retrieve multiple batch operations. For Django applications, you might have multiple Jobs running different batch tasks like data processing, report generation, cleanup operations, or maintenance tasks simultaneously.

    📋 JobList Components Overview

    apiVersion - batch/v1 API version
    kind - JobList resource type
    metadata - List metadata and pagination
    items - Array of Job objects
    ✨ Collection Management: Efficiently list and paginate through multiple Job resources with metadata support for bulk Django batch operation management.

    Parameters description

    • apiVersion: Always "batch/v1" for JobList resources.
    • kind: Always "JobList" to identify this as a list of Job resources.
    • metadata: Standard list metadata including resource version and pagination information.
    • items: Array of Job objects. Contains all the individual Jobs matching the list criteria for Django batch operations.

    Syntax

    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: JobList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "12345"
  continue: ""
  remainingItemCount: 0
items:
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: job-name-1
    namespace: default
  spec:
    # JobSpec configuration
  status:
    # JobStatus information
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: job-name-2
    namespace: default
  spec:
    # JobSpec configuration
  status:
    # JobStatus information

apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: JobList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "156789"
  continue: ""
  remainingItemCount: 0
  selfLink: /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/anihpj-production/jobs
items:
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: jobpost-daily-processor
    namespace: anihpj-production
    creationTimestamp: "2024-01-15T08:00:00Z"
    labels:
      app: jobpost-processor
      batch-type: daily
      priority: high
  spec:
    parallelism: 5
    completions: 20
    backoffLimit: 3
    template:
      spec:
        containers:
        - name: processor
          image: anihpj/jobpost-processor:v3.2
          env:
          - name: PROCESSING_TYPE
            value: "comprehensive"
          - name: BATCH_SIZE
            value: "100"
          resources:
            requests:
              memory: "1Gi"
              cpu: "500m"
        restartPolicy: Never
  status:
    active: 2
    succeeded: 18
    failed: 0
    startTime: "2024-01-15T08:00:00Z"
    completionTime: "2024-01-15T09:45:00Z"
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: jobpost-skills-enrichment
    namespace: anihpj-production
    labels:
      app: jobpost-processor
      batch-type: enrichment
      priority: medium
  spec:
    parallelism: 3
    completions: 12
    template:
      spec:
        containers:
        - name: enricher
          image: anihpj/skills-enricher:v2.1
          env:
          - name: ML_MODEL_VERSION
            value: "v4.0"
        restartPolicy: Never
  status:
    succeeded: 12
    completionTime: "2024-01-15T10:30:00Z"

# Check processing timeline and dependencies
kubectl get jobs -l app=jobpost-processor -o custom-columns="NAME:.metadata.name,BATCH-TYPE:.metadata.labels.batch-type,START:.status.startTime,COMPLETION:.status.completionTime,DURATION:.status.completionTime"

# Analyze job performance metrics
for job in $(kubectl get jobs -l app=jobpost-processor -o jsonpath='{.items[*].metadata.name}'); do
  echo "=== $job ==="
  kubectl describe job $job | grep -A 5 -B 5 "Pods Statuses\|Events"
done

# Generate processing efficiency report
kubectl get jobs -l app=jobpost-processor -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}{","}{.status.startTime}{","}{.status.completionTime}{","}{.spec.parallelism}{","}{.status.succeeded}{"\n"}{end}' | \
awk -F',' '{
  split($2, start, "T"); split($3, end, "T");
  split(start[2], st, ":"); split(end[2], et, ":");
  duration = (et[1]*60 + et[2]) - (st[1]*60 + st[2]);
  efficiency = ($5 / ($4 * duration)) * 100;
  printf "%s: Duration=%dm, Efficiency=%.1f%%, Throughput=%.1f jobs/min\n", $1, duration, efficiency, $5/duration
}'

    # Comprehensive JobPost processing analysis
>>> from jobpost.models import JobPost, Skills
>>> from django.db.models import Count, Avg, Q
>>> import datetime

# Daily processing job analysis
>>> daily_processing_results = {
...     'total_jobs_processed': JobPost.objects.filter(
...         processed_date=datetime.date.today(),
...         processing_batch='daily'
...     ).count(),
...     'new_jobs_today': JobPost.objects.filter(
...         created_at__date=datetime.date.today()
...     ).count(),
...     'updated_jobs': JobPost.objects.filter(
...         updated_at__date=datetime.date.today()
...     ).exclude(created_at__date=datetime.date.today()).count(),
...     'processing_efficiency': JobPost.objects.filter(
...         processed_date=datetime.date.today(),
...         processing_status='completed'
...     ).count() / 20 * 100  # 20 completions expected
... }
>>> daily_processing_results
{'total_jobs_processed': 1800, 'new_jobs_today': 450, 'updated_jobs': 1350, 'processing_efficiency': 90.0}

# Skills enrichment analysis
>>> skills_enrichment_results = {
...     'jobs_enriched': JobPost.objects.filter(
...         skills_enriched=True,
...         enrichment_date=datetime.date.today()
...     ).count(),
...     'skills_extracted': Skills.objects.filter(
...         extraction_date=datetime.date.today(),
...         extraction_method='ml_v4'
...     ).count(),
...     'enrichment_quality': Skills.objects.filter(
...         extraction_date=datetime.date.today(),
...         confidence_score__gte=0.85
...     ).count(),
...     'avg_skills_per_job': Skills.objects.filter(
...         extraction_date=datetime.date.today()
...     ).values('job_post').annotate(
...         skill_count=Count('id')
...     ).aggregate(avg=Avg('skill_count'))['avg']
... }
>>> skills_enrichment_results
{'jobs_enriched': 1200, 'skills_extracted': 8500, 'enrichment_quality': 7650, 'avg_skills_per_job': 7.08}

# Cross-job performance analysis
>>> processing_performance = {
...     'daily_job_throughput': daily_processing_results['total_jobs_processed'] / 105,  # 1h 45m processing time
...     'enrichment_throughput': skills_enrichment_results['jobs_enriched'] / 150,  # 2h 30m processing time
...     'resource_efficiency': {
...         'daily_pods_used': 20,  # 5 parallelism * avg 4 pods
...         'enrichment_pods_used': 36,  # 3 parallelism * 12 completions
...         'total_cpu_hours': (20 * 1.75) + (36 * 2.5),  # Duration in hours
...         'jobs_per_cpu_hour': (daily_processing_results['total_jobs_processed'] + 
...                               skills_enrichment_results['jobs_enriched']) / 125
...     },
...     'quality_metrics': {
...         'processing_success_rate': 100.0,  # No failed jobs
...         'enrichment_accuracy': (skills_enrichment_results['enrichment_quality'] / 
...                                skills_enrichment_results['skills_extracted']) * 100,
...         'data_completeness': JobPost.objects.filter(
...             processed_date=datetime.date.today(),
...             skills_enriched=True,
...             description__isnull=False,
...             company__isnull=False
...         ).count() / max(daily_processing_results['total_jobs_processed'], 1) * 100
...     }
... }
>>> processing_performance
{'daily_job_throughput': 17.14, 'enrichment_throughput': 8.0, 'resource_efficiency': {'daily_pods_used': 20, 'enrichment_pods_used': 36, 'total_cpu_hours': 125.0, 'jobs_per_cpu_hour': 24.0}, 'quality_metrics': {'processing_success_rate': 100.0, 'enrichment_accuracy': 90.0, 'data_completeness': 95.5}}

...     'processing_lag': abs(daily_processing_results['total_jobs_processed'] - skills_enrichment_results['jobs_enriched']),
...     'next_pipeline_ready': True,  # Both jobs completed successfully

apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: JobList
metadata:
  resourceVersion: "156790"
  labels:
    migration-wave: "2024-q1"
    coordination-group: "user-migration"
items:
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: us-east-user-migration
    namespace: anihpj-production
    labels:
      region: us-east
      migration-phase: active
      priority: high
  spec:
    parallelism: 8
    completions: 32
    template:
      spec:
        containers:
        - name: migrator
          image: anihpj/user-migrator:v3.5
          env:
          - name: REGION
            value: "us-east"
          - name: MIGRATION_BATCH_SIZE
            value: "500"
          - name: COORDINATION_ENDPOINT
            value: "https://migration-coordinator.anihpj.internal"
          resources:
            requests:
              memory: "2Gi"
              cpu: "1000m"
        restartPolicy: Never
  status:
    active: 5
    succeeded: 27
    startTime: "2024-01-15T06:00:00Z"
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: eu-west-user-migration
    namespace: anihpj-production
    labels:
      region: eu-west
      migration-phase: active
      priority: high
  spec:
    parallelism: 6
    completions: 24
    template:
      spec:
        containers:
        - name: migrator
          image: anihpj/user-migrator:v3.5
          env:
          - name: REGION
            value: "eu-west"
          - name: TIMEZONE_OFFSET
            value: "+01:00"
        restartPolicy: Never
  status:
    active: 2
    succeeded: 22
    startTime: "2024-01-15T06:30:00Z"
- apiVersion: batch/v1
  kind: Job
  metadata:
    name: apac-user-migration
    namespace: anihpj-production
    labels:
      region: apac
      migration-phase: waiting
      priority: medium
  spec:
    parallelism: 4
    completions: 16
    suspend: true
    template:
      spec:
        containers:
        - name: migrator
          image: anihpj/user-migrator:v3.5
          env:
          - name: REGION
            value: "apac"
          - name: LANGUAGE_SUPPORT
            value: "multi"
        restartPolicy: Never
  status:
    conditions:
    - type: Suspended
      status: "True"
      reason: "WaitingForRegionalCompletion"
    Monitor coordinated multi-region user migration:
    # Monitor migration progress across all regions

# Check regional migration completion percentages
kubectl get jobs -l coordination-group=user-migration -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.labels.region}{": "}{(.status.succeeded/.spec.completions*100)}{"% complete ("}{.status.succeeded}{"/"}{.spec.completions}{")\n"}{end}'

# Monitor coordination status and dependencies
kubectl get jobs -l coordination-group=user-migration -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}{" ("}{.metadata.labels.region}{"): "}{if .spec.suspend}SUSPENDED{else}ACTIVE{end}{" - "}{.status.conditions[0].reason}{"\n"}{end}'

# Check resource utilization across regions
kubectl top pods -l coordination-group=user-migration --sort-by=memory | head -20

# Analyze regional migration timing and coordination
#!/bin/bash
echo "=== Regional Migration Coordination Analysis ==="
for region in us-east eu-west apac; do
  job_name="${region}-user-migration"
  status=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}/{.spec.completions}' 2>/dev/null || echo "N/A")
  phase=$(kubectl get job $job_name -o jsonpath='{.metadata.labels.migration-phase}' 2>/dev/null || echo "unknown")
  echo "Region $region: $status ($phase)"
done

# Check if APAC can be unblocked
US_COMPLETE=$(kubectl get job us-east-user-migration -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}')
EU_COMPLETE=$(kubectl get job eu-west-user-migration -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}')
US_TOTAL=$(kubectl get job us-east-user-migration -o jsonpath='{.spec.completions}')
EU_TOTAL=$(kubectl get job eu-west-user-migration -o jsonpath='{.spec.completions}')

if [ "$US_COMPLETE" -eq "$US_TOTAL" ] && [ "$EU_COMPLETE" -eq "$EU_TOTAL" ]; then
  echo "US and EU migrations complete - APAC migration can proceed"
  kubectl patch job apac-user-migration -p '{"spec":{"suspend":false}}'
else
  echo "Waiting for US ($US_COMPLETE/$US_TOTAL) and EU ($EU_COMPLETE/$EU_TOTAL) completion"
fi
    Result: Multi-region JobList showing US-East (84% complete), EU-West (92% complete), and APAC (suspended waiting).

# Monitor processing throughput across stages
#!/bin/bash
echo "=== Skills Pipeline Throughput Analysis ==="
for stage in data-preparation ml-extraction normalization validation; do
  jobs=$(kubectl get jobs -l pipeline=skills-processing,pipeline-stage=$stage -o jsonpath='{.items[*].metadata.name}')
  if [ -n "$jobs" ]; then
    echo "Stage: $stage"
    for job in $jobs; do
      succeeded=$(kubectl get job $job -o jsonpath='{.status.succeeded}' 2>/dev/null || echo "0")
      total=$(kubectl get job $job -o jsonpath='{.spec.completions}' 2>/dev/null || echo "1")
      start_time=$(kubectl get job $job -o jsonpath='{.status.startTime}')
      if [ "$succeeded" -gt 0 ] && [ -n "$start_time" ]; then
        echo "  $job: $succeeded/$total completed"
      fi
    done
  fi
done

# Check for pipeline bottlenecks
kubectl get jobs -l pipeline=skills-processing -o jsonpath='{range .items[?(@.status.failed>0)]}{.metadata.name}{" has "}{.status.failed}{" failures\n"}{end}'

# Validate ML model performance
kubectl logs -l pipeline-stage=ml-extraction --tail=100 | grep -E "(accuracy|precision|recall|f1)" | tail -10

# Monitor data quality and geocoding accuracy
#!/bin/bash
echo "=== Geographical Sync Quality Analysis ==="
for region in $(kubectl get jobs -l sync-type=geographical -o jsonpath='{.items[*].metadata.labels.region}' | tr ' ' '\n' | sort -u); do
  job_name="${region}-location-sync"
  if kubectl get job $job_name &>/dev/null; then
    echo "Region: $region"
    
    # Check geocoding accuracy from logs
    accuracy=$(kubectl logs -l job-name=$job_name --tail=100 | grep "geocoding_accuracy" | tail -1 | awk -F: '{print $2}' | tr -d ' %')
    echo "  Geocoding Accuracy: ${accuracy}%"
    
    # Check API rate limits
    rate_limit=$(kubectl logs -l job-name=$job_name --tail=100 | grep "rate_limit" | tail -1 | awk -F: '{print $2}' | tr -d ' ')
    echo "  API Rate Status: $rate_limit"
    
    # Check data freshness
    last_update=$(kubectl logs -l job-name=$job_name --tail=10 | grep "last_location_update" | tail -1 | awk -F: '{print $2}' | tr -d ' ')
    echo "  Last Update: $last_update"
  fi
done

# Analyze cross-region dependencies and data consistency
kubectl get jobs -l sync-type=geographical -o jsonpath='{range .items[*]}{.metadata.name}{" depends on: "}{.metadata.annotations.depends-on}{"\n"}{end}'

# Check for geographical data conflicts
kubectl logs -l sync-type=geographical --tail=200 | grep -i "conflict\|duplicate\|mismatch" | head -10

    Operations

    Docs: Kubernetes Job Operations

    HTTP API operations for managing Job resources in Kubernetes clusters.

    Full description

    Job operations provide HTTP API endpoints for creating, reading, updating, deleting, and listing Job resources. These operations enable programmatic management of Django batch processing tasks, allowing automated deployment pipelines, monitoring systems, and job scheduling tools to interact with your Job workloads.

    🔧 Job Operations Overview

    GET - Read specified Job details
    GET Status - Read Job execution status
    LIST - List Jobs in namespace
    LIST All - List Jobs across namespaces
    CREATE - Create new Job
    UPDATE - Replace entire Job
    UPDATE Status - Replace Job status
    PATCH - Partially update Job
    PATCH Status - Partially update status
    DELETE - Remove specific Job
    DELETE Collection - Remove multiple Jobs

    📊 Operations by Category

    Read Operations - GET, GET Status, LIST, LIST All
    Write Operations - CREATE, UPDATE, UPDATE Status
    Modify Operations - PATCH, PATCH Status
    Delete Operations - DELETE, DELETE Collection
    ✨ API Operations: Complete HTTP REST API for programmatic Job management including CRUD operations, status monitoring, and bulk collection handling for Django batch processing automation.

    Get Read the Specified Job

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job to retrieve
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output for better readability
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Get Django Migration Job
    kubectl get job django-migration-job -o yaml
    kubectl output: 
    apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  annotations:
    batch.kubernetes.io/job-tracking: ""
  creationTimestamp: "2024-01-02T10:30:00Z"
  generation: 1
  labels:
    app: django
    job-name: django-migration-job
    type: migration
  name: django-migration-job
  namespace: default
  resourceVersion: "12345"
  uid: a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
spec:
  backoffLimit: 6
  completionMode: NonIndexed
  completions: 1
  parallelism: 1
  selector:
    matchLabels:
      controller-uid: a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
  suspend: false
  template:
    metadata:
      labels:
        app: django
        controller-uid: a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
        job-name: django-migration-job
    spec:
      containers:
      - command:
        - python
        - manage.py
        - migrate
        env:
        - name: DATABASE_URL
          value: postgres://user:pass@postgres:5432/jobpost_db
        image: jobpost:v1.2
        name: django-migrator
        resources: {}
        terminationMessagePath: /dev/termination-log
        terminationMessagePolicy: File
      dnsPolicy: ClusterFirst
      restartPolicy: Never
      schedulerName: default-scheduler
      terminationGracePeriodSeconds: 30
status:
  completionTime: "2024-01-02T10:32:15Z"
  conditions:
  - lastProbeTime: "2024-01-02T10:32:15Z"
    lastTransitionTime: "2024-01-02T10:32:15Z"
    status: "True"
    type: Complete
  startTime: "2024-01-02T10:30:00Z"
  succeeded: 1
    Job status summary: 
    $ kubectl get job django-migration-job
NAME                   COMPLETIONS   DURATION   AGE
django-migration-job   1/1           2m15s      5m

    Get Read Status of the Specified Job

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}/status
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Check Job Processing Status
    kubectl get job jobpost-processor --template='{{.status.succeeded}}/{{.spec.completions}}'
    Result: Shows completion progress like "3/5" indicating 3 out of 5 required completions finished.

    List Jobs in Namespace

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs
    Parameters
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace to list Jobs from
    • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector for filtering Jobs
    • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector for filtering Jobs
    • watch - boolean (query) - Watch for changes to the Job list
    Response

    200 (JobList): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: List Django Batch Jobs
    kubectl get jobs -l app=jobpost,type=batch
    kubectl output: 
    NAME                     COMPLETIONS   DURATION   AGE
weekly-reports           1/1           45s        2h
user-data-export         1/1           3m15s      1h
database-cleanup         1/1           1m30s      45m
email-notifications      1/1           2m10s      30m
    Detailed view with wider columns: 
    $ kubectl get jobs -l app=jobpost,type=batch -o wide
NAME                  COMPLETIONS   DURATION   AGE   CONTAINERS         IMAGES          SELECTOR
weekly-reports        1/1           45s        2h    report-generator   jobpost:v1.2    controller-uid=a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
user-data-export      1/1           3m15s      1h    data-exporter      jobpost:v1.2    controller-uid=b2c3d4e5-f6g7-8901-bcde-f23456789012
database-cleanup      1/1           1m30s      45m   cleanup-script     jobpost:v1.2    controller-uid=c3d4e5f6-g7h8-9012-cdef-345678901234
email-notifications   1/1           2m10s      30m   email-sender       jobpost:v1.2    controller-uid=d4e5f6g7-h8i9-0123-def0-456789012345

    List Jobs in All Namespaces

    GET
    HTTP Request
    GET /apis/batch/v1/jobs
    Parameters
    • allowWatchBookmarks - boolean (query) - Allow watch bookmarks
    • continue - string (query) - Continue token for pagination
    • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector for filtering Jobs
    • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector for filtering Jobs
    • limit - integer (query) - Limit the number of results
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output
    • resourceVersion - string (query) - Resource version for consistency
    • timeoutSeconds - integer (query) - Timeout for the request
    • watch - boolean (query) - Watch for changes to the Job list
    Response

    200 (JobList): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: List All Django Jobs Across Namespaces
    kubectl get jobs --all-namespaces -l app=django
    kubectl output: 
    NAMESPACE   NAME                     COMPLETIONS   DURATION   AGE
default     weekly-reports           1/1           45s        2h
staging     staging-migration        1/1           1m20s      6h
staging     staging-data-seed        1/1           3m45s      5h
production  prod-migration           1/1           2m10s      1d
production  prod-data-backup         1/1           15m30s     12h
production  prod-log-cleanup         1/1           8m15s      6h
testing     test-data-setup          1/1           30s        3h
testing     test-cleanup             1/1           45s        2h
    Filter by completion status: 
    $ kubectl get jobs --all-namespaces -l app=django --field-selector status.successful=1
NAMESPACE   NAME                     COMPLETIONS   DURATION   AGE
default     weekly-reports           1/1           45s        2h
staging     staging-migration        1/1           1m20s      6h
staging     staging-data-seed        1/1           3m45s      5h
production  prod-migration           1/1           2m10s      1d
production  prod-data-backup         1/1           15m30s     12h
production  prod-log-cleanup         1/1           8m15s      6h
testing     test-data-setup          1/1           30s        3h
testing     test-cleanup             1/1           45s        2h

    Create a Job

    POST
    HTTP Request
    POST /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs
    Parameters
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace to create the Job in
    • body - Job, required - Job object to create
    • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    201 (Job): Created

    202 (Job): Accepted

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Create Django Report Generation Job
    kubectl apply -f - <<EOF
apiVersion: batch/v1
kind: Job
metadata:
  name: weekly-reports
spec:
  template:
    spec:
      restartPolicy: Never
      containers:
      - name: report-generator
        image: jobpost-reports:latest
        command: ["python", "generate_weekly_reports.py"]
EOF
    kubectl output: 
    job.batch/weekly-reports created
    Verify Job Status: 
    $ kubectl get jobs
NAME             COMPLETIONS   DURATION   AGE
weekly-reports   0/1           2s         2s

$ kubectl describe job weekly-reports
Name:             weekly-reports
Namespace:        default
Selector:         controller-uid=a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
Labels:           controller-uid=a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
                  job-name=weekly-reports
Annotations:      batch.kubernetes.io/job-tracking: ""
Parallelism:      1
Completions:      1
Completion Mode:  NonIndexed
Start Time:       Mon, 02 Jan 2024 10:30:00 +0000
Active:           1
Pod Template:
  Labels:  controller-uid=a1b2c3d4-e5f6-7890-abcd-ef1234567890
           job-name=weekly-reports
  Containers:
   report-generator:
    Image:      jobpost-reports:latest
    Port:       
    Host Port:  
    Command:
      python
      generate_weekly_reports.py
    Environment:  
    Mounts:       
  Volumes:        
Events:
  Type    Reason            Age   From            Message
  ----    ------            ----  ----            -------
  Normal  SuccessfulCreate  5s    job-controller  Created pod: weekly-reports-abc123

    Update Replace the Specified Job

    PUT
    HTTP Request
    PUT /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job to update
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • body - Job, required - Updated Job object
    • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
    • fieldManager - string (query) - Field manager identifier
    • fieldValidation - string (query) - Field validation mode
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    201 (Job): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Update Django Job Labels
    kubectl patch job jobpost-processor -p '{"metadata":{"labels":{"version":"v2"}}}'
    Result: Updates the Job's metadata labels for Django JobPost processing.

    Update Replace Status of the Specified Job

    PUT
    HTTP Request
    PUT /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}/status
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • body - Job, required - Job object with updated status
    • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
    • fieldManager - string (query) - Field manager identifier
    • fieldValidation - string (query) - Field validation mode
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    201 (Job): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Update Django Job Status
    kubectl get job user-migration -o yaml | kubectl replace -f -
    Result: Updates the status of Django user migration job.

    Patch Partially Update the Specified Job

    PATCH
    HTTP Request
    PATCH /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job to patch
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • body - Patch, required - Patch data to apply
    • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
    • fieldManager - string (query) - Field manager identifier
    • fieldValidation - string (query) - Field validation mode
    • force - boolean (query) - Force the update
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    201 (Job): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Patch Django Skills Job
    kubectl patch job skills-processor -p '{"spec":{"suspend":true}}'
    Result: Suspends the Django skills processing job by patching the suspend field.

    Patch Partially Update Status of the Specified Job

    PATCH
    HTTP Request
    PATCH /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}/status
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • body - Patch, required - Patch data for status update
    • dryRun - string (query) - Dry run mode
    • fieldManager - string (query) - Field manager identifier
    • fieldValidation - string (query) - Field validation mode
    • force - boolean (query) - Force the update
    • pretty - string (query) - Pretty-print the output
    Response

    200 (Job): OK

    201 (Job): Created

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Patch Django Location Job Status
    kubectl patch job location-sync --subresource=status -p '{"status":{"conditions":[{"type":"Complete","status":"True"}]}}'
    Result: Updates the status condition of Django location sync job to mark it as complete.

    Delete a Job

    DELETE
    HTTP Request
    DELETE /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs/{name}
    Parameters
    • name - string, required (path) - Name of the Job to delete
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Job
    • propagationPolicy - string (query) - How to handle dependent objects
    Response

    200 (Status): OK

    202 (Status): Accepted

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Delete Completed Migration Job
    kubectl delete job django-migration-job
    kubectl output: 
    job.batch "django-migration-job" deleted
    Verify deletion: 
    $ kubectl get jobs django-migration-job
Error from server (NotFound): jobs.batch "django-migration-job" not found
    Check for remaining pods: 
    $ kubectl get pods -l job-name=django-migration-job
No resources found in default namespace.

    Delete Collection of Jobs

    DELETE
    HTTP Request
    DELETE /apis/batch/v1/namespaces/{namespace}/jobs
    Parameters
    • namespace - string, required (path) - Namespace containing the Jobs
    • labelSelector - string (query) - Label selector to filter which Jobs to delete
    • fieldSelector - string (query) - Field selector to filter which Jobs to delete
    Response

    200 (Status): OK

    401: Unauthorized

    Examples
    Example: Delete All Completed Jobs
    kubectl delete jobs --field-selector=status.successful=1
    kubectl output: 
    job.batch "weekly-reports" deleted
job.batch "user-data-export" deleted
job.batch "database-cleanup" deleted
job.batch "email-notifications" deleted
    Delete by label selector: 
    $ kubectl delete jobs -l app=jobpost,type=batch
job.batch "staging-data-seed" deleted
job.batch "prod-data-backup" deleted
job.batch "test-data-setup" deleted
    Verify all jobs deleted: 
    $ kubectl get jobs -l app=jobpost
No resources found in default namespace.
